> - **Network ACL** = subnet level, **stateless** (must allow return traffic explicitly), supports **allow and deny** rules.
> "Block a specific IP address at the subnet level" -> **NACL** (because security groups can't explicitly deny).

*Practice:*
1. A company wants a logically isolated private network within AWS to launch its resources. Which service? **-> Amazon VPC.**
2. Which firewall is stateful and operates at the instance level? **-> Security group.**

### Amazon Route 53

- **What it is:** A scalable **DNS (Domain Name System)** web service. Also does **domain registration** and **health checks/routing policies**.
- **Analogy:** The internet's phone book — translates names (example.com) into addresses (IPs), and can route users to the best/healthiest location.
- **When to use:** Manage DNS, register domains, route users (e.g., latency-based, geolocation, failover routing).
- **When NOT to use:** Caching/serving content (that's CloudFront).
- **Exam keywords:** "DNS," "domain registration," "route traffic by latency/geolocation/failover," "health checks."
- **Similar services:** CloudFront (CDN, different job).

> **Common Trap: Route 53 vs. CloudFront.** Route 53 = **DNS / routing by name**. CloudFront = **CDN / caching content at edge locations**. "Translate domain names" -> Route 53. "Cache and deliver content fast to global users" -> CloudFront.

*Practice:*
1. A company needs to register a domain and manage DNS records with latency-based routing. Which service? **-> Amazon Route 53.**
2. Route 53 can route users to a backup site if the primary fails. What is this called? **-> Failover (DNS) routing with health checks.**

### Amazon CloudFront

- **What it is:** A **Content Delivery Network (CDN)** that caches content at **edge locations** worldwide to deliver it with low latency.
- **Analogy:** Local warehouses near customers so deliveries (web content) arrive fast instead of shipping from one far-away store.
- **When to use:** Speed up delivery of websites, images, videos, APIs to a global audience; reduce latency; offload origin servers. Integrates with **Shield** and **WAF** for protection.
- **When NOT to use:** As DNS (Route 53) or primary storage (S3).
- **Exam keywords:** "CDN," "content delivery network," "edge locations," "cache content close to users," "low latency global delivery."

*Practice:*
1. A media company wants to stream videos to a global audience with minimal latency by caching at edge locations. Which service? **-> Amazon CloudFront.**
2. CloudFront delivers content from which infrastructure component? **-> Edge locations.**

### AWS Direct Connect

- **What it is:** A **dedicated, private physical network connection** from your data center to AWS (bypasses the public internet).
- **Analogy:** A private express lane straight to AWS instead of public highways.
- **When to use:** Consistent, low-latency, high-bandwidth, private connectivity for hybrid setups; large/steady data transfer; compliance needs.
- **When NOT to use:** Quick, cheap, encrypted connection where a VPN over the internet is enough.
- **Exam keywords:** "dedicated private connection," "bypass the internet," "consistent low latency," "hybrid."

*Practice:*
1. A bank wants a private, dedicated, consistent connection between its data center and AWS, not over the public internet. Which service? **-> AWS Direct Connect.**
2. Direct Connect vs. VPN: which avoids the public internet entirely? **-> Direct Connect.**

### AWS VPN (Virtual Private Network)

- **What it is:** A **secure, encrypted connection over the internet** between your network and AWS (Site-to-Site VPN) or for users (Client VPN).
- **Analogy:** A secure tunnel through the public internet.
- **When to use:** Quick, encrypted hybrid connectivity without the cost/lead time of Direct Connect.
- **Exam keywords:** "encrypted tunnel," "secure connection over the internet," "Site-to-Site VPN."

> **Common Trap: Direct Connect vs. VPN.** Direct Connect = **private, dedicated, not over the internet** (consistent performance, costs more, takes time to set up). VPN = **encrypted over the public internet** (fast to set up, cheaper, performance varies with the internet).

*Practice:*
1. A company needs a quick, encrypted connection from its office to AWS over the internet. Which service? **-> AWS Site-to-Site VPN.**
2. Which option provides a dedicated private line and which uses the public internet? **-> Direct Connect = private line; VPN = public internet (encrypted).**

## 3.7 Application integration

### Amazon SQS (Simple Queue Service)

- **What it is:** A fully managed **message queue** that lets application components communicate **asynchronously** by storing messages until they're processed. **Decouples** components.
- **Analogy:** A to-do inbox: senders drop tasks in; workers pick them up when ready. If a worker is busy, the task waits safely in the queue.
- **When to use:** Decouple and buffer between components; handle spikes; ensure no message is lost if a consumer is down.
- **Exam keywords:** "message queue," "decouple," "asynchronous," "buffer requests," "pull-based."
- **Similar services:** SNS (pub/sub notifications).

*Practice:*
1. A company wants to decouple its order-processing components so a slow worker doesn't lose orders during traffic spikes. Which service? **-> Amazon SQS.**
2. SQS messages are retrieved how? **-> Consumers poll/pull messages from the queue.**

### Amazon SNS (Simple Notification Service)

- **What it is:** A managed **pub/sub messaging and notification** service — publish a message once and **push** it to many subscribers (email, SMS, Lambda, SQS, HTTP).
- **Analogy:** A broadcast announcement: one message, many listeners get it instantly.
- **When to use:** Fan-out notifications, alerts, sending messages to multiple endpoints at once.
- **Exam keywords:** "pub/sub," "publish/subscribe," "push notifications," "fan-out," "send to many subscribers."

> **Common Trap: SQS vs. SNS.** SQS = **queue, pull-based, one consumer group processes each message** (decoupling/buffering). SNS = **pub/sub, push-based, many subscribers get the same message** (notifications/fan-out).

*Practice:*
1. A system must instantly notify email, SMS, and several services whenever an event occurs. Which service? **-> Amazon SNS.**
2. Is SNS push-based or pull-based? **-> Push-based (publish/subscribe).**

### Amazon EventBridge

- **What it is:** A **serverless event bus** that connects applications using **events** (from AWS services, your apps, or SaaS partners) and routes them to targets based on rules.
- **Analogy:** A smart switchboard that routes events to the right handlers automatically.
- **When to use:** Build event-driven architectures; react to AWS service events; schedule tasks; integrate SaaS events.
- **Exam keywords:** "event bus," "event-driven," "route events," "react to changes," "schedule."

*Practice:*
1. A team wants to route events from many AWS and SaaS sources to different targets based on rules. Which service? **-> Amazon EventBridge.**
2. EventBridge is most associated with which architectural style? **-> Event-driven architecture.**

### AWS Step Functions

- **What it is:** A **serverless workflow orchestration** service that coordinates multiple AWS services into **visual workflows** (state machines) with steps, branches, and retries.
- **Analogy:** A flowchart that runs itself, calling each service in order and handling errors.
- **When to use:** Coordinate multi-step processes (e.g., order -> payment -> ship), manage retries and sequencing across Lambda and other services.
- **Exam keywords:** "orchestrate workflows," "coordinate multiple steps/services," "state machine," "visual workflow."

*Practice:*
1. A company needs to coordinate a multi-step order-fulfillment workflow across several Lambda functions with retries and branching. Which service? **-> AWS Step Functions.**
2. Step Functions models a workflow as what? **-> A state machine (visual workflow).**

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## 3.8 Analytics and AI/ML services

CLF-C02 added AI/ML. You only need to know **what each service does**, not how to build models.

### Amazon Athena

- **What it is:** **Serverless** service to run **SQL queries directly on data in Amazon S3** — no servers, no loading into a database.
- **Analogy:** Asking questions of your files in S3 in plain SQL, paying only per query.
- **When to use:** Ad-hoc analysis of S3 data (logs, exports) without setting up a database/warehouse.
- **Exam keywords:** "query data in S3 using SQL," "serverless analytics," "pay per query."

*Practice:*
1. An analyst wants to run SQL queries on log files stored in S3 without provisioning any infrastructure. Which service? **-> Amazon Athena.**
2. Athena queries data located where? **-> In Amazon S3.**

### AWS Glue

- **What it is:** A **serverless ETL** (Extract, Transform, Load) service to prepare and combine data for analytics; includes a data catalog.
- **Analogy:** A prep kitchen that cleans and combines raw ingredients (data) before cooking (analysis).
- **When to use:** Cleaning, transforming, and cataloging data for analytics pipelines.
- **Exam keywords:** "ETL," "extract transform load," "data preparation," "data catalog," "serverless."

*Practice:*
1. A company needs to extract, transform, and load data from many sources to prepare it for analytics, without managing servers. Which service? **-> AWS Glue.**
2. "ETL" maps to which AWS service? **-> AWS Glue.**

### Amazon QuickSight

- **What it is:** A **business intelligence (BI) / dashboard and visualization** service.
- **Analogy:** A tool that turns spreadsheets and databases into charts and dashboards.
- **When to use:** Create interactive dashboards and visual reports for business users.
- **Exam keywords:** "BI," "dashboards," "data visualization," "reports/charts."

*Practice:*
1. A manager wants interactive dashboards and visualizations from the company's data. Which service? **-> Amazon QuickSight.**
2. QuickSight is which category of service? **-> Business intelligence / visualization.**

### Amazon Kinesis (good to know)

- **What it is:** Services for **real-time streaming data** (ingesting and processing data as it arrives, like clickstreams, logs, IoT).
- **Exam keywords:** "real-time," "streaming data," "ingest data continuously."

### AI/ML services

| Service | What it does | Exam keyword |
|---------|-------------|--------------|
| **Amazon SageMaker** | Fully managed platform to **build, train, and deploy machine learning models**. | "build/train/deploy ML models" |
| **Amazon Rekognition** | **Image and video analysis** (detect objects, faces, text). | "analyze images/video" |
| **Amazon Comprehend** | **Natural language processing** — find insights/sentiment in text. | "NLP / sentiment / text analysis" |
| **Amazon Transcribe** | **Speech to text**. | "audio to text / transcription" |
| **Amazon Polly** | **Text to speech**. | "text to lifelike speech" |
| **Amazon Translate** | **Language translation**. | "translate languages" |
| **Amazon Lex** | Build **chatbots / conversational interfaces** (the tech behind Alexa). | "chatbot / voice assistant" |
| **Amazon Kendra** | **Intelligent enterprise search**. | "smart search across documents" |

> **Note on Amazon Bedrock:** Bedrock is AWS's service for building **generative AI** apps using foundation models. The **official CLF-C02 exam guide examples** for AI/ML specifically name **SageMaker, Lex, and Kendra**, so prioritize those. Bedrock is increasingly relevant general knowledge (generative AI / foundation models), but it is **not** listed in the official task-statement examples — know it at a high level only ("managed access to foundation models for generative AI").

> **Exam Tip:** Match the AI service to the data type: **images** -> Rekognition; **text sentiment** -> Comprehend; **speech-to-text** -> Transcribe; **text-to-speech** -> Polly; **translation** -> Translate; **chatbot** -> Lex; **build custom ML** -> SageMaker.

*Practice:*
1. A team wants a fully managed platform to build, train, and deploy custom machine learning models. Which service? **-> Amazon SageMaker.**
2. Which service converts spoken audio into text? **-> Amazon Transcribe.**

## 3.9 Management and governance

### AWS CloudFormation

- **What it is:** **Infrastructure as Code (IaC)** — define your AWS resources in a template file and deploy them automatically and repeatably.
- **Analogy:** A blueprint that builds your entire environment identically every time.
- **When to use:** Repeatable, automated, version-controlled provisioning of infrastructure.
- **Exam keywords:** "infrastructure as code," "template," "repeatable provisioning," "automate resource creation."

*Practice:*
1. A company wants to define and deploy its AWS infrastructure from a repeatable template. Which service? **-> AWS CloudFormation.**
2. CloudFormation enables which practice? **-> Infrastructure as Code (IaC).**

### AWS Systems Manager

- **What it is:** A suite to **manage and operate** your resources at scale — run commands, patch fleets, store parameters, view operational data.
- **Analogy:** A mission-control panel for operating your servers and resources.
- **When to use:** Operational tasks like patching many EC2 instances, running commands fleet-wide, storing config (Parameter Store).
- **Exam keywords:** "operate/manage resources at scale," "patch fleet," "run commands," "Parameter Store."

*Practice:*
1. An ops team wants to patch and run commands across hundreds of EC2 instances centrally. Which service? **-> AWS Systems Manager.**
2. Where can Systems Manager store configuration values and secrets? **-> Parameter Store.**

### AWS Trusted Advisor

- **What it is:** An **automated best-practice checker** that inspects your account and gives recommendations across **cost optimization, performance, security, fault tolerance, and service limits**.
- **Analogy:** A consultant that scans your account and suggests improvements.
- **When to use:** Identify savings, security gaps (e.g., open ports, MFA on root), and reliability issues.
- **Exam keywords:** "recommendations," "best practices," "cost/security/performance/fault tolerance/service quotas checks."

> **Common Trap:** The **full set** of Trusted Advisor checks requires **Business or Enterprise** support plans. Basic/Developer plans get a limited subset.

*Practice:*
1. A company wants automated recommendations to reduce cost and improve security and reliability. Which service? **-> AWS Trusted Advisor.**
2. Full Trusted Advisor checks require which support plans? **-> Business or Enterprise.**

### AWS Health Dashboard

- **What it is:** Shows the **health/status of AWS services** and **personalized alerts** about events that affect *your* resources.
- **Exam keywords:** "service health," "is AWS having an outage," "events affecting my account."

*Practice:*
1. Where do you check whether an AWS service issue is affecting your specific resources? **-> AWS Health Dashboard.**
2. Is the Health Dashboard about your bill or AWS service status? **-> AWS service status/health.**

### AWS Service Catalog

- **What it is:** Lets organizations create and manage **approved catalogs** of IT products for users to deploy in a controlled, compliant way.
- **Exam keywords:** "approved products," "self-service catalog," "governance/standardization."

*Practice:*
1. An enterprise wants employees to deploy only pre-approved, standardized resources. Which service? **-> AWS Service Catalog.**
2. Service Catalog mainly supports which goal? **-> Governance/standardization of approved products.**

### AWS Control Tower

- **What it is:** **Sets up and governs a secure, multi-account AWS environment** (a "landing zone") using best practices automatically.
- **Exam keywords:** "set up and govern multi-account environment," "landing zone," "guardrails."

*Practice:*
1. A company wants to quickly set up a well-architected, governed multi-account environment with guardrails. Which service? **-> AWS Control Tower.**
2. Control Tower builds what kind of environment? **-> A secure, governed multi-account "landing zone."**

## 3.10 Migration and data transfer

### AWS Migration Hub

- **What it is:** A single place to **track migration progress** across tools and AWS services.
- **Exam keywords:** "track migrations," "central view of migration progress."

### AWS Database Migration Service (DMS)

- **What it is:** Migrate databases to AWS with **minimal downtime**; can also convert between database engines (with Schema Conversion Tool).
- **Exam keywords:** "migrate databases," "minimal downtime," "homogeneous/heterogeneous migration."

*Practice:*
1. A company wants to migrate an on-premises database to AWS with minimal downtime. Which service? **-> AWS DMS.**

### AWS Snow Family (Snowcone, Snowball, Snowmobile)

- **What it is:** **Physical devices** to transfer **large amounts of data** into/out of AWS when network transfer would be too slow or expensive. AWS ships you a rugged device; you load data and ship it back.
- **Analogy:** Mailing a hard drive (a very big, secure one) because uploading petabytes over the internet would take forever.
- **When to use:** Massive datasets, poor/limited bandwidth, edge locations.
- **Exam keywords:** "transfer large data physically," "limited bandwidth," "petabytes," "ship a device."

> **Common Trap:** If a question stresses **huge data + slow/limited internet + a deadline**, the answer is usually **Snowball/Snow Family**, not uploading over the network.

*Practice:*
1. A company must move 80 TB to AWS but has very limited internet bandwidth. Which option is best? **-> AWS Snowball (Snow Family).**
2. Snow Family transfers data using what? **-> Physical, shippable devices.**

### AWS Storage Gateway

- **What it is:** Connects **on-premises** environments to AWS storage; provides **hybrid** cloud storage (caches frequently used data locally while storing in AWS).
- **Exam keywords:** "hybrid storage," "on-premises access to cloud storage," "cached file system."

*Practice:*
1. A company wants on-premises applications to use AWS storage seamlessly with local caching. Which service? **-> AWS Storage Gateway.**
2. Storage Gateway supports which deployment model? **-> Hybrid.**

## 3.11 Domain 3 — Real exam traps

> **Common Trap 1:** **S3 (object) vs. EBS (block, one instance) vs. EFS (shared file, many instances).**

> **Common Trap 2:** **EC2 (you manage servers) vs. Lambda (serverless) vs. Elastic Beanstalk (PaaS) vs. Fargate (serverless containers).**

> **Common Trap 3:** **RDS/Aurora (relational/SQL) vs. DynamoDB (NoSQL) vs. Redshift (data warehouse/analytics).**

> **Common Trap 4:** **Security group (instance, stateful, allow-only) vs. NACL (subnet, stateless, allow+deny).**

> **Common Trap 5:** **Route 53 (DNS) vs. CloudFront (CDN).**

> **Common Trap 6:** **Direct Connect (private dedicated line) vs. VPN (encrypted over internet).**

> **Common Trap 7:** **SQS (queue, pull, decouple) vs. SNS (pub/sub, push, fan-out).**

> **Common Trap 8:** **Snowball (physical bulk transfer) vs. uploading over the network.** Big data + low bandwidth = Snow Family.

> **Common Trap 9:** Multi-AZ = **high availability**; multiple **Regions** = global reach/DR; **edge locations** = low-latency content delivery.

## 3.12 Domain 3 — Mini Quiz

**Q1.** A company needs virtually unlimited **object storage** for images and backups. Which service?
- A. Amazon EBS
- B. Amazon S3
- C. Amazon EFS
- D. Amazon FSx

**Q2.** Which service runs code **without provisioning or managing servers**, charging only for execution time?
- A. Amazon EC2
- B. AWS Lambda
- C. Amazon ECS on EC2
- D. AWS Elastic Beanstalk

**Q3.** A workload needs a **NoSQL key-value** database with millisecond latency at any scale. Which service?
- A. Amazon RDS
- B. Amazon Redshift
- C. Amazon DynamoDB
- D. Amazon Aurora

**Q4.** To make a web application **highly available**, an architect should deploy instances across:
- A. Multiple edge locations
- B. Multiple Availability Zones
- C. A single large instance
- D. Multiple VPCs in one subnet

**Q5.** Which service is a **CDN** that caches content at edge locations to reduce latency?
- A. Amazon Route 53
- B. Amazon CloudFront
- C. AWS Direct Connect
- D. Amazon VPC

**Q6.** (Choose TWO) Which statements about **security groups** are correct?
- A. They operate at the subnet level
- B. They are stateful
- C. They support both allow and deny rules
- D. They operate at the instance level
- E. They are stateless

**Q7.** A company must transfer **100 TB** to AWS but has **very limited bandwidth** and a tight deadline. Best option?
- A. Upload over the internet to S3
- B. AWS Snowball
- C. AWS Direct Connect provisioned next year
- D. Email the files

**Q8.** Which service distributes incoming application traffic across multiple EC2 instances?
- A. EC2 Auto Scaling
- B. Elastic Load Balancing
- C. Amazon Route 53 only
- D. AWS Lambda

**Q9.** A team wants to run **SQL queries directly on data stored in S3** without managing infrastructure. Which service?
- A. Amazon Redshift
- B. Amazon Athena
- C. AWS Glue
- D. Amazon QuickSight

**Q10.** Which service provides a **managed relational database** with automated patching and backups?
- A. Amazon DynamoDB
- B. Amazon RDS
- C. Amazon S3
- D. Amazon ElastiCache

**Q11.** Which service lets you define infrastructure as code from a reusable template?
- A. AWS CloudFormation
- B. AWS Trusted Advisor
- C. Amazon CloudWatch
- D. AWS Config

**Q12.** A messaging pattern requires **one message to be pushed to many subscribers** at once. Which service?
- A. Amazon SQS
- B. Amazon SNS
- C. AWS Step Functions
- D. Amazon MQ

### Domain 3 — Answers & Explanations

**Q1 -> B. Amazon S3** is object storage. EBS is single-instance block; EFS/FSx are file systems.

**Q2 -> B. AWS Lambda** is serverless and bills per execution. EC2 and ECS-on-EC2 require server management; Beanstalk provisions servers under the hood.

**Q3 -> C. Amazon DynamoDB** is the NoSQL key-value option. RDS/Aurora are relational; Redshift is analytics.

**Q4 -> B. Multiple Availability Zones** gives high availability. Edge locations are for content delivery; one big instance and one subnet are single points of failure.

**Q5 -> B. Amazon CloudFront.** Route 53 is DNS; Direct Connect is private connectivity; VPC is networking.

**Q6 -> B and D.** Security groups are **stateful** and operate at the **instance level**. Subnet-level, stateless, and allow+deny describe **NACLs**.

**Q7 -> B. AWS Snowball.** Physical transfer beats slow uploads for large data with limited bandwidth. Direct Connect next year misses the deadline; email is absurd.

**Q8 -> B. Elastic Load Balancing.** Auto Scaling changes the *number* of instances; ELB *distributes traffic* across them. Route 53 does DNS-level routing, not instance load balancing in this sense.

**Q9 -> B. Amazon Athena** queries S3 data with SQL, serverless. Redshift is a warehouse (load data first); Glue is ETL; QuickSight is BI dashboards.

**Q10 -> B. Amazon RDS.** Managed relational DB. DynamoDB is NoSQL; S3 is object storage; ElastiCache is a cache.

**Q11 -> A. AWS CloudFormation** is Infrastructure as Code. Trusted Advisor recommends; CloudWatch monitors; Config tracks configuration.

**Q12 -> B. Amazon SNS** (pub/sub, push to many subscribers). SQS is a pull-based queue; Step Functions orchestrates workflows; Amazon MQ is a managed message broker (not the foundational answer here).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Domain 4: Billing, Pricing, and Support (12%)

Only 12% of the exam, but these are **predictable, easy points**. Master the pricing models, the billing/cost tools, and the support plans, and you'll likely get most of this domain right.

## 4.1 Core pricing principles

AWS pricing rests on a few ideas:

- **Pay-as-you-go:** Pay only for what you use, no large upfront commitments required.
- **Pay less when you reserve:** Commit to usage (Reserved Instances / Savings Plans) for big discounts.
- **Pay less per unit by using more:** Volume-based discounts (e.g., S3 tiers).
- **Pay less as AWS grows:** Prices drop over time due to economies of scale.

**Three things you're generally charged for:** **compute** (e.g., EC2 hours), **storage** (e.g., GB stored), and **data transfer OUT** of AWS. Note: **inbound data transfer is usually free**, and data transfer **between services in the same Region** is often free or cheap; **outbound to the internet** typically costs money.

> **Exam Tip:** "Which incurs cost?" Data **transfer out** to the internet usually does; data **in** is usually free.

## 4.2 AWS Free Tier

The **AWS Free Tier** lets you try services for free within limits. It has three types:

| Free Tier type | Meaning | Example |
|----------------|---------|---------|
| **Always Free** | Free up to a limit, forever | 1 million Lambda requests/month; 25 GB DynamoDB |
| **12 months free** | Free for 12 months after signup | 750 hours/month of a t2.micro/t3.micro EC2 instance; 5 GB S3 Standard |
| **Free trials** | Short-term free trial of a service | Some services offer a limited trial period |

*Practice:* "New customers can run a small EC2 instance free for 12 months" -> **12-months-free** part of the Free Tier.

## 4.3 EC2 pricing models (purchasing options)

This is one of the most tested topics in Domain 4. Learn each option and when to use it.

| Option | What it is | Best for |
|--------|-----------|----------|
| **On-Demand** | Pay by the hour/second, no commitment. Highest per-unit price, most flexible. | Short-term, unpredictable, spiky, or test workloads; new apps. |
| **Reserved Instances (RIs)** | Commit to 1 or 3 years for a big discount (up to ~72%). | Steady, predictable, always-on workloads. |
| **Savings Plans** | Commit to a consistent **amount of usage ($/hour)** for 1 or 3 years; flexible across instance families/services (incl. Lambda/Fargate). | Steady usage where you want more flexibility than RIs. |
| **Spot Instances** | Use spare AWS capacity at up to ~90% off, but AWS can **reclaim** them with little notice. | Fault-tolerant, flexible, interruptible workloads (batch jobs, big data, CI). |
| **Dedicated Hosts** | A physical server dedicated to you. | Licensing/compliance that requires dedicated hardware. |

> **Common Trap: Reserved Instances vs. Savings Plans vs. Spot.**
> - **Steady, predictable, want lowest cost with commitment** -> **Reserved Instances** or **Savings Plans** (Savings Plans are more flexible).
> - **Interruptible / fault-tolerant / can be stopped anytime** -> **Spot Instances** (cheapest, but can be reclaimed).
> - **Short-term, unpredictable, no commitment** -> **On-Demand**.
> - **Critical workload that must NOT be interrupted** -> NOT Spot. Use On-Demand or Reserved.

> **Exam Tip:** Spot's giveaway is "**fault-tolerant**," "**flexible start/end times**," "**can tolerate interruption**," "**batch processing**." If the workload **can't** be interrupted, Spot is wrong.

*Practice:*
1. A batch-processing job can be interrupted and restarted, and the company wants the lowest cost. Which EC2 option? **-> Spot Instances.**
2. A production database server runs 24/7 for 3 years. Which option saves the most? **-> Reserved Instances (or a Savings Plan).**

## 4.4 Billing and cost-management tools

These tools confuse people. Learn the **one-line difference** for each.

| Tool | One-line job | When to pick it |
|------|--------------|-----------------|
| **AWS Pricing Calculator** | **Estimate costs BEFORE you build.** | "Estimate the monthly cost of a planned architecture." |
| **AWS Cost Explorer** | **Visualize, analyze, and forecast PAST/CURRENT spend.** | "See where money went and forecast future spend." |
| **AWS Budgets** | **Set custom budgets and get ALERTS** when you exceed (or are forecast to exceed) thresholds. | "Alert me when spend crosses $500." |
| **AWS Billing Dashboard** | Overview of your current bill and charges. | "View this month's charges." |
| **AWS Cost and Usage Report (CUR)** | The most detailed line-item billing data. | "Get the most granular billing data for analysis." |
| **Cost Allocation Tags** | **Tag resources** to categorize and track costs by project/team/environment. | "Break down cost by department." |

> **Common Trap (very frequent): Pricing Calculator vs. Cost Explorer vs. Budgets.**
> - **BEFORE deployment, estimate cost** -> **Pricing Calculator**.
> - **After/while running, analyze and forecast actual spend** -> **Cost Explorer**.
> - **Get alerted when spending crosses a limit** -> **Budgets**.

*Practice:*
1. A team wants an email alert when monthly spend is forecast to exceed $1,000. Which tool? **-> AWS Budgets.**
2. Before launching, a company wants to estimate the monthly cost of an EC2 + RDS + S3 design. Which tool? **-> AWS Pricing Calculator.**

## 4.5 Consolidated billing and AWS Organizations

**Consolidated billing** (via **AWS Organizations**) combines multiple accounts into **one bill**. Benefits:

- **One payment** for all accounts.
- **Combined usage** can reach **volume discount tiers** faster (and share Reserved Instance/Savings Plan benefits across accounts).
- Easier tracking of each account's costs.

*Practice:* "A company with 20 AWS accounts wants a single bill and to share volume discounts" -> **Consolidated billing via AWS Organizations.**

## 4.6 AWS Marketplace

**AWS Marketplace** is a **digital catalog** to find, buy, and deploy **third-party software** that runs on AWS, with billing through your AWS account.

*Practice:* "Buy and deploy third-party software with charges on your AWS bill" -> **AWS Marketplace.**

## 4.7 AWS Support plans

Know the **four** plans and what each adds. (Basic is free; the others are paid and stack features.)

| Plan | Cost | Key features |
|------|------|--------------|
| **Basic** | Free (all accounts) | Documentation, whitepapers, forums, limited Trusted Advisor checks, AWS Health Dashboard. **No technical support cases.** |
| **Developer** | Paid | Business-hours **email** access to support (Cloud Support Associates); general guidance. |
| **Business** | Paid | **24/7** phone, email, chat; **full Trusted Advisor**; production system support; faster response times. |
| **Enterprise On-Ramp** | Paid | Everything in Business + a **pool of Technical Account Managers (TAMs)**; faster critical response; some concierge. |
| **Enterprise** | Paid (highest) | Everything + a **designated Technical Account Manager (TAM)**, **concierge support**, fastest response (~15 min for business-critical), well-architected reviews. |

> **Common Trap: who gets a TAM?** A **designated TAM** comes with **Enterprise** (and a *pool* of TAMs with **Enterprise On-Ramp**). Basic, Developer, and Business do **not** get a designated TAM.

> **Common Trap: full Trusted Advisor checks** require **Business or Enterprise** (and Enterprise On-Ramp). Basic and Developer get only a **limited** set.

> **Exam Tip:** Match the need to the plan:
> - "Free, just docs and forums" -> **Basic**.
> - "Cheap email support during business hours for a non-production app" -> **Developer**.
> - "24/7 support and full Trusted Advisor for production" -> **Business**.
> - "Need a designated Technical Account Manager and fastest response" -> **Enterprise**.

*Practice:*
1. A company running a critical production workload needs 24/7 phone support and full Trusted Advisor, but doesn't need a dedicated TAM. Which plan? **-> Business.**
2. Which plan provides a **designated** Technical Account Manager? **-> Enterprise.**

## 4.8 Other technical resources and people

- **AWS Knowledge Center / re:Post / Documentation:** self-service help (free).
- **AWS Professional Services & AWS Partner Network (APN):** consultants/partners to help you build and migrate.
- **AWS Solutions Architects:** help design well-architected solutions (relevant with higher support tiers).
- **Technical Account Manager (TAM):** a proactive advisor included with Enterprise (and pooled with Enterprise On-Ramp).

## 4.9 Domain 4 — Real exam traps

> **Trap 1:** **Pricing Calculator (estimate before) vs. Cost Explorer (analyze after) vs. Budgets (alert on threshold).**

> **Trap 2:** **Spot** is only for **interruptible** workloads. Never the answer for "must not be interrupted."

> **Trap 3:** **Reserved Instances vs. Savings Plans** — both for steady usage; Savings Plans are more **flexible** across families/services.

> **Trap 4:** **Designated TAM = Enterprise** only. Full **Trusted Advisor = Business/Enterprise**.

> **Trap 5:** **Data transfer IN is usually free; OUT to the internet usually costs.**

> **Trap 6:** **Consolidated billing** is a feature of **AWS Organizations** (one bill + volume discounts).

## 4.10 Domain 4 — Mini Quiz

**Q1.** Which tool **estimates costs before** you deploy a planned architecture?
- A. AWS Cost Explorer
- B. AWS Budgets
- C. AWS Pricing Calculator
- D. AWS Cost and Usage Report

**Q2.** A workload runs nightly, can be safely interrupted, and the company wants the **lowest possible cost**. Which EC2 pricing option?
- A. On-Demand
- B. Reserved Instances
- C. Spot Instances
- D. Dedicated Hosts

**Q3.** Which support plan includes a **designated Technical Account Manager**?
- A. Developer
- B. Business
- C. Enterprise On-Ramp
- D. Enterprise

**Q4.** A finance team wants to be **alerted by email** when monthly spend exceeds a set amount. Which tool?
- A. AWS Pricing Calculator
- B. AWS Budgets
- C. AWS Trusted Advisor
- D. AWS Organizations

**Q5.** (Choose TWO) Which are benefits of **consolidated billing** in AWS Organizations?
- A. A single bill across all member accounts
- B. Free Enterprise support for all accounts
- C. Volume pricing discounts from combined usage
- D. Automatic encryption of all data
- E. Elimination of the root user

**Q6.** A production system needs **24/7 support and full Trusted Advisor checks**, but a dedicated TAM is not required. Which plan is most cost-effective?
- A. Basic
- B. Developer
- C. Business
- D. Enterprise

**Q7.** Which EC2 option is best for a **steady, predictable, 3-year** production workload to minimize cost?
- A. On-Demand
- B. Spot Instances
- C. Reserved Instances or Savings Plans
- D. Dedicated Hosts

**Q8.** Which tool lets you **analyze and forecast your past and current AWS spending** with charts?
- A. AWS Pricing Calculator
- B. AWS Cost Explorer
- C. AWS Config
- D. AWS Artifact

### Domain 4 — Answers & Explanations

**Q1 -> C. AWS Pricing Calculator** estimates costs *before* building. Cost Explorer analyzes actual spend; Budgets alerts; CUR is detailed billing data.

**Q2 -> C. Spot Instances.** Interruptible + lowest cost = Spot. On-Demand is flexible but pricier; Reserved is for steady long-term; Dedicated Hosts are for licensing/compliance.

**Q3 -> D. Enterprise.** A *designated* TAM is an Enterprise feature. Enterprise On-Ramp gets a *pool* of TAMs; Developer/Business get none.

**Q4 -> B. AWS Budgets** sends alerts on spending thresholds. Pricing Calculator estimates; Trusted Advisor recommends; Organizations manages accounts.

**Q5 -> A and C.** Consolidated billing gives one bill and shares volume/RI/Savings Plan discounts. B, D, and E are false.

**Q6 -> C. Business.** 24/7 support + full Trusted Advisor without a dedicated TAM = Business. Basic/Developer lack 24/7 and full Trusted Advisor; Enterprise is more than needed (and costlier).

**Q7 -> C. Reserved Instances or Savings Plans.** Steady, long-term workloads get the biggest discount via commitment. Spot risks interruption; On-Demand and Dedicated Hosts cost more for this case.

**Q8 -> B. AWS Cost Explorer.** Visualize and forecast spend. Pricing Calculator is pre-deployment; Config is configuration compliance; Artifact is compliance reports.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Must-Know Service Comparison Tables

These tables are gold for the exam. If you only memorize one chapter, make it this one. Each table contrasts services that the exam loves to confuse.

## EC2 vs. Lambda vs. Elastic Beanstalk

| | Amazon EC2 | AWS Lambda | AWS Elastic Beanstalk |
|--|-----------|-----------|----------------------|
| Type | IaaS (virtual servers) | Serverless functions | PaaS (managed deploy) |
| You manage | OS, scaling, everything above hardware | Just your code | Just your code |
| Scaling | Manual or Auto Scaling | Automatic | Automatic |
| Billing | Per instance time | Per request + duration | Pay for underlying resources |
| Best for | Full control, legacy apps, custom OS | Event-driven, short tasks | Quick web app deploy without infra work |

## S3 vs. EBS vs. EFS

| | Amazon S3 | Amazon EBS | Amazon EFS |
|--|-----------|-----------|-----------|
| Storage type | Object | Block | File (shared) |
| Attaches to | Accessed via API/internet | One EC2 instance (1 AZ) | Many EC2 instances at once |
| Best for | Files, backups, static sites, data lakes | EC2 boot/data disks, databases | Shared file storage across instances |
| Keyword | "object storage," "buckets" | "block storage," "volume" | "shared file system" |

## RDS vs. DynamoDB vs. Redshift

| | Amazon RDS | Amazon DynamoDB | Amazon Redshift |
|--|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|
| Type | Relational (SQL) | NoSQL (key-value/document) | Data warehouse (analytics) |
| Workload | Transactional (OLTP) | High-scale key-value | Analytical (OLAP) / BI |
| Managed? | Yes (managed) | Yes (serverless) | Yes (managed) |
| Keyword | "managed relational/SQL" | "NoSQL," "key-value" | "data warehouse," "analytics" |

## CloudTrail vs. CloudWatch vs. Config

| | AWS CloudTrail | Amazon CloudWatch | AWS Config |
|--|----------------|-------------------|-----------|
| Answers | Who did what (API activity) | How is it performing (metrics/alarms) | What changed / is it compliant |
| Use case | Auditing, security investigation | Monitoring, alarms, dashboards | Configuration history & compliance |
| Keyword | "API calls," "user activity," "audit" | "metrics," "alarms," "monitor" | "configuration," "compliance," "changes" |

## WAF vs. Shield vs. GuardDuty vs. Inspector

| | AWS WAF | AWS Shield | Amazon GuardDuty | Amazon Inspector |
|--|---------|-----------|------------------|------------------|
| Protects against | Malicious web requests (SQLi, XSS) | DDoS attacks | Threats found in logs/activity | Software vulnerabilities |
| Layer | Application (web) | Network/transport | Account/behavior analysis | EC2/containers/Lambda scanning |
| Keyword | "SQL injection," "XSS," "web firewall" | "DDoS" | "threat detection," "suspicious activity" | "vulnerability assessment" |

## Pricing Calculator vs. Cost Explorer vs. Budgets

| | AWS Pricing Calculator | AWS Cost Explorer | AWS Budgets |
|--|------------------------|-------------------|-------------|
| When | Before deployment | During/after usage | Ongoing |
| Job | Estimate future cost | Analyze & forecast actual spend | Alert when crossing thresholds |
| Keyword | "estimate before building" | "analyze/forecast spend" | "alert," "budget limit" |

## IAM user vs. group vs. role vs. policy

| | IAM User | IAM Group | IAM Role | IAM Policy |
|--|----------|-----------|----------|-----------|
| What | Identity for a person/app | Collection of users | Temporary assumable identity | JSON permissions document |
| Credentials | Long-term | (uses users') | Temporary | None (it's rules) |
| Use for | A specific human/app | Apply same permissions to many users | Apps/EC2/services, cross-account, temporary access | Define what is allowed/denied |

## Security group vs. Network ACL

| | Security Group | Network ACL (NACL) |
|--|----------------|--------------------|
| Level | Instance | Subnet |
| State | Stateful (return traffic auto-allowed) | Stateless (must allow return traffic) |
| Rules | Allow only | Allow and deny |
| Use | Default instance firewall | Subnet-wide rules, explicit deny (e.g., block an IP) |

## CloudFront vs. Route 53

| | Amazon CloudFront | Amazon Route 53 |
|--|-------------------|-----------------|
| Category | CDN (content delivery) | DNS (name resolution) + domain registration |
| Job | Cache content at edge locations for low latency | Translate domain names; route by latency/geo/failover |
| Keyword | "CDN," "edge," "cache content globally" | "DNS," "domain," "route by latency/health" |

## Reserved Instances vs. Savings Plans vs. Spot Instances

| | Reserved Instances | Savings Plans | Spot Instances |
|--|--------------------|---------------|----------------|
| Commitment | 1 or 3 years, specific instance type | 1 or 3 years, $/hour usage (flexible) | None (uses spare capacity) |
| Discount | Up to ~72% | Up to ~72% | Up to ~90% |
| Risk | Locked-in commitment | Locked-in commitment | Can be interrupted/reclaimed |
| Best for | Steady, predictable workloads | Steady usage with flexibility | Interruptible, fault-tolerant workloads |

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Exam Keywords Decoder

This is the **fastest-scoring** technique on the exam. Many questions hinge on a single keyword that maps to one service. Drill this list until the mapping is automatic.

## Storage & databases

| "NoSQL, key-value, document" | **Amazon DynamoDB** |

# Common Exam Traps (Master List)

Read this section twice. These exact confusions cause the most lost points.

> **Trap 1 — AWS responsibility vs. customer responsibility.**
> AWS = security **of** the cloud (hardware, facilities, hypervisor, managed-service software). Customer = security **in** the cloud (data, IAM, OS patching on EC2, security group rules, encryption choices). You **always** own your data and access management.

> **Trap 2 — CloudTrail vs. CloudWatch vs. Config.**
> CloudTrail = who-did-what (API audit). CloudWatch = performance metrics/alarms. Config = configuration changes/compliance.

> **Trap 3 — S3 vs. EBS vs. EFS.**
> S3 = object storage. EBS = block storage for one instance. EFS = shared file storage for many instances.

> **Trap 4 — WAF vs. Shield (vs. GuardDuty vs. Inspector).**
> WAF = SQL injection/XSS (web requests). Shield = DDoS. GuardDuty = threat detection. Inspector = vulnerability scanning.

> **Trap 5 — Security group vs. NACL.**
> Security group = instance level, stateful, allow-only. NACL = subnet level, stateless, allow + deny. Need to explicitly **deny** an IP? NACL.

> **Trap 6 — RDS vs. DynamoDB vs. Redshift.**
> RDS = relational/SQL transactional. DynamoDB = NoSQL key-value. Redshift = data warehouse/analytics.

> **Trap 7 — Cost Explorer vs. Budgets vs. Pricing Calculator.**
> Pricing Calculator = estimate before. Cost Explorer = analyze/forecast actual. Budgets = alert on thresholds.

> **Trap 8 — Reserved Instances vs. Savings Plans vs. Spot.**
> Reserved/Savings Plans = steady workloads with commitment (Savings Plans more flexible). Spot = interruptible workloads only.

> **Trap 9 — IAM role vs. IAM user.**
> Role = temporary, for services/apps/cross-account (best practice for EC2 accessing other services). User = long-term identity for a person/app.

> **Trap 10 — High availability vs. fault tolerance vs. elasticity.**
> HA = minimal downtime (multi-AZ). Fault tolerance = no interruption during failure. Elasticity = auto-scale to match demand.

> **Trap 11 — Route 53 vs. CloudFront.**
> Route 53 = DNS/routing. CloudFront = CDN/edge caching.

> **Trap 12 — Direct Connect vs. VPN.**
> Direct Connect = private dedicated line (consistent, not over internet). VPN = encrypted over the public internet (quick, cheaper).

> **Trap 13 — SQS vs. SNS.**
> SQS = queue, pull, decouple/buffer. SNS = pub/sub, push, fan-out to many.

> **Trap 14 — Support plans & TAM.**
> Designated TAM = Enterprise. Full Trusted Advisor = Business/Enterprise (and Enterprise On-Ramp).

> **Trap 15 — Snow Family vs. network upload.**
> Huge data + limited bandwidth + deadline = Snow Family (ship a device), not internet upload.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>
# Memory Cheatsheets

These are your fast-revision pages. They are deliberately dense. Read them the night before and the morning of your exam. Do **not** try to learn brand-new things from these — use them to refresh what you already studied.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Cheat Sheet 1 — Core Services (one page)

**Compute**

- **EC2** — virtual servers. You manage the OS. Pick instance families for the job (compute/memory/storage optimized).
- **Lambda** — run code without servers. Pay per request + run time. Event-driven, short tasks.
- **Elastic Beanstalk** — upload your app, AWS handles the deploy (capacity, load balancing, scaling). You still own the resources.
- **ECS / EKS** — run containers (EKS = Kubernetes). **Fargate** = serverless containers (no servers to manage).
- **Auto Scaling** — add/remove EC2 automatically to match demand.
- **ELB** — spread traffic across healthy targets (works with Auto Scaling for HA).

**Storage**

- **S3** — object storage. Unlimited, durable, internet-accessible. Classes: Standard, Intelligent-Tiering, Standard-IA, One Zone-IA, Glacier Instant/Flexible/Deep Archive.
- **EBS** — block storage for **one** EC2 instance (a virtual hard drive). AZ-locked.
- **EFS** — shared file storage for **many** Linux instances at once.
- **FSx** — managed file systems (Windows File Server, Lustre, etc.).
- **AWS Backup** — central backup across services.

**Databases**

- **RDS** — managed relational/SQL (MySQL, PostgreSQL, etc.).
- **Aurora** — AWS's high-performance MySQL/PostgreSQL-compatible engine.
- **DynamoDB** — serverless NoSQL key-value, single-digit-millisecond, massive scale.
- **Redshift** — data warehouse for analytics on huge datasets.
- **ElastiCache** — in-memory cache (Redis/Memcached) for speed.

**Networking**

- **VPC** — your private network in AWS. **Subnets, route tables, IGW, NAT gateway** live here.
- **Security group** — instance-level firewall, stateful, allow-only.
- **NACL** — subnet-level firewall, stateless, allow **and** deny.
- **Route 53** — DNS + routing + domain registration.
- **CloudFront** — CDN, caches content at edge locations.
- **Direct Connect** — private dedicated line to AWS. **VPN** — encrypted tunnel over the internet.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Cheat Sheet 2 — Security (one page)

- **Shared Responsibility Model** — AWS = security **OF** the cloud (hardware, facilities, managed-service infra). Customer = security **IN** the cloud (your data, IAM, OS patching on EC2, configuration).
- **IAM** — **User** = a person/app (long-term). **Group** = bucket of users. **Role** = temporary credentials for services/apps/cross-account (best practice). **Policy** = JSON document of permissions.
- **Root user** — lock it down: enable MFA, don't use it for daily work, create an admin IAM user instead.
- **Least privilege** — grant only the permissions needed, nothing more.
- **MFA** — second factor on top of password.
- **IAM Identity Center** — single sign-on across multiple accounts/apps.
- **Organizations + SCPs** — manage many accounts; SCPs set permission **guardrails** (max permissions) across accounts.

**Logging / monitoring / auditing**

- **CloudTrail** — records **who did what** (API activity, auditing). Think "security camera."
- **CloudWatch** — **metrics, logs, alarms** (performance/health). Think "dashboard + alarm."
- **Config** — tracks **resource configuration changes** and compliance over time.

**Protection / detection**

- **Shield** — DDoS protection.
- **WAF** — filters web traffic (SQL injection, XSS).
- **GuardDuty** — intelligent threat detection (analyzes logs).
- **Inspector** — automated vulnerability scanning of workloads.
- **Security Hub** — central security posture dashboard.
- **Macie** — finds sensitive data (PII) in S3.
- **Detective** — investigates root cause of security findings.

**Data protection**

- **KMS** — create/manage encryption keys.
- **Secrets Manager** — store + rotate secrets (DB passwords, API keys).
- **ACM** — provision/manage SSL/TLS certificates.
- **Artifact** — download AWS compliance reports (SOC, PCI, ISO).
- Encryption **at rest** (stored data) vs **in transit** (moving data, TLS).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Cheat Sheet 3 — Billing & Pricing (one page)

**Pricing principles**

- Pay-as-you-go, pay less when you reserve, pay less per unit as you use more, save as AWS grows.
- Three cost drivers to remember: **compute, storage, and data transfer OUT**. (Inbound data transfer is generally free; data transfer **out** to the internet costs money.)

**EC2 purchasing options**

- **On-Demand** — pay by second/hour, no commitment. Short-term/unpredictable.
- **Reserved Instances** — 1- or 3-year commitment, big discount. Steady, predictable workloads.
- **Savings Plans** — commit to $/hour of usage for 1/3 years. More **flexible** than RIs.
- **Spot** — up to ~90% off spare capacity, can be interrupted. Fault-tolerant/flexible jobs only.
- **Dedicated Hosts** — physical server for you (licensing/compliance).

**Cost tools**

- **Pricing Calculator** — estimate costs **before** you build.
- **Cost Explorer** — visualize + **forecast** past/current spend.
- **Budgets** — set thresholds and get **alerts**.
- **Billing Dashboard** — overview of current charges.
- **Cost Allocation Tags** — label resources to break down costs.
- **Cost & Usage Report (CUR)** — most detailed billing data.
- **Consolidated billing** (via Organizations) — one bill for many accounts + volume discounts.

**Support plans**

- **Basic** (free) — docs, forums, limited Trusted Advisor.
- **Developer** — business-hours email to support associates.
- **Business** — 24/7 phone/chat/email, **full Trusted Advisor**, production support.
- **Enterprise On-Ramp** — adds pool of TAMs, faster response.
- **Enterprise** — **designated TAM**, 15-min critical response, concierge.

> **Remember:** Designated **TAM = Enterprise**. Full Trusted Advisor starts at **Business**.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Cheat Sheet 4 — Exam Keywords (one page)

| If you see these words... | Think of... |
|---|---|
| object storage, store files/images/backups | **S3** |
| block storage, attach to one EC2, virtual disk | **EBS** |
| shared file storage, many instances | **EFS** |
| virtual server, full OS control | **EC2** |
| serverless, run code, event-driven, pay per run | **Lambda** |
| just upload my app, AWS handles deploy | **Elastic Beanstalk** |
| containers, Kubernetes | **ECS / EKS** (Fargate = serverless) |
| managed relational/SQL database | **RDS** |
| NoSQL, key-value, single-digit ms | **DynamoDB** |
| data warehouse, analytics on huge data | **Redshift** |
| in-memory cache, speed up reads | **ElastiCache** |
| CDN, cache content near users | **CloudFront** |
| DNS, domain names, routing | **Route 53** |
| dedicated private connection to AWS | **Direct Connect** |
| who made this API call, audit trail | **CloudTrail** |
| metrics, alarms, monitor performance | **CloudWatch** |
| track config changes, compliance | **Config** |
| DDoS protection | **Shield** |
| SQL injection / XSS / filter web traffic | **WAF** |
| threat detection from logs | **GuardDuty** |
| vulnerability scan of workloads | **Inspector** |
| find PII / sensitive data in S3 | **Macie** |
| compliance reports (SOC, PCI, ISO) | **Artifact** |
| manage encryption keys | **KMS** |
| store + rotate DB passwords/secrets | **Secrets Manager** |
| SSL/TLS certificates | **ACM** |
| estimate cost before building | **Pricing Calculator** |
| analyze + forecast spend | **Cost Explorer** |
| alert me when spending hits a limit | **Budgets** |
| recommendations (cost, security, performance) | **Trusted Advisor** |
| move huge data, ship a physical device | **Snow Family** |
| infrastructure as code, templates | **CloudFormation** |
| message queue, decouple, buffer | **SQS** |
| pub/sub, push notifications, fan-out | **SNS** |

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Cheat Sheet 5 — Last Day Before the Exam

**The 10 things people most often mix up — get these right and you protect a lot of points:**

1. **CloudTrail = who did it (audit)** vs **CloudWatch = how is it doing (metrics/alarms)** vs **Config = what changed (configuration history)**.
2. **AWS secures OF the cloud; you secure IN the cloud.** Patching your EC2 OS = you. Patching the physical host = AWS.
3. **S3 = object, EBS = one instance's disk, EFS = shared file for many.**
4. **WAF = web attacks (SQLi/XSS); Shield = DDoS.**
5. **Security group = stateful, allow-only, instance level; NACL = stateless, allow+deny, subnet level.**
6. **RDS = SQL/relational; DynamoDB = NoSQL key-value; Redshift = analytics warehouse.**
7. **Pricing Calculator = before; Cost Explorer = analyze/forecast; Budgets = alerts.**
8. **Reserved/Savings Plans = commit for discount on steady use; Spot = cheap but interruptible.**
9. **IAM role = temporary (for services/apps, best practice); IAM user = long-term identity.**
10. **HA = minimal downtime; Fault tolerance = no interruption; Elasticity = auto scale to demand.**

**Reminders for the actual test:**

- 65 questions, 90 minutes — roughly **1 minute 20 seconds** each. Don't panic.
- Read the **last line** of the question first; it often tells you what's actually being asked.
- Watch for keywords: **MOST cost-effective, LEAST operational overhead, HIGHLY available, MOST secure.** They change the right answer.
- "Choose TWO/THREE" — select exactly that many.
- No penalty for wrong answers — **never leave a blank**. Flag and come back.
- Eliminate obviously wrong options first; you can usually cut it to a 50/50.
- Sleep, eat, hydrate. A calm brain reads traps better than a tired one.

> **Remember:** You don't need a perfect score. You need **700/1000**. Aim for understanding, stay calm, and trust your preparation.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Practice Questions

This is the largest part of the book, and the most important. Reading teaches you the material; **questions reveal whether you actually understand it.**

How to use this section:

- Do each quiz **closed-book** first, then check answers.
- For every question you miss, don't just read the right answer — read **why the wrong ones are wrong**. That's where the real learning is.
- Every answer is tagged with its **domain and topic** so you can spot your weak areas.
- These questions are **original**, written in AWS exam style. They are not real exam questions (using real exam content is against AWS policy and won't help you long-term anyway).

The five quizzes, in increasing difficulty:

1. **20-question Beginner Quiz** — warm-up, one concept at a time.
2. **40-question Domain-Mixed Quiz** — jumps between domains like the real exam.
3. **65-question Full Mock Exam 1** — full length, full timing.
4. **65-question Full Mock Exam 2** — full length, harder.
5. **65-question Final Readiness Exam** — your "am I ready?" checkpoint.

> **Exam Tip:** Time yourself on the three 65-question mocks: **90 minutes each.** If you finish comfortably in time and score consistently around **80%+**, you're in a strong position for exam day.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Quiz 1 — Beginner Quiz (20 questions)

**Q1.** What does Amazon S3 provide?

- A. Block storage attached to a single EC2 instance
- B. Object storage for files, images, and backups
- C. A managed relational database
- D. A content delivery network

**Q2.** Which AWS service lets you run code without provisioning or managing servers?

- A. Amazon EC2
- B. AWS Lambda
- C. Amazon RDS
- D. Amazon VPC

**Q3.** In the AWS Shared Responsibility Model, which task is the **customer's** responsibility?

- A. Securing the physical data centers
- B. Maintaining the hardware
- C. Configuring IAM users and permissions
- D. Patching the hypervisor

**Q4.** Which service is a managed relational database?

- A. Amazon DynamoDB
- B. Amazon RDS
- C. Amazon S3
- D. Amazon Redshift

**Q5.** A company wants to be alerted when its monthly AWS spending exceeds $500. Which service should it use?

- A. AWS Pricing Calculator
- B. AWS Cost Explorer
- C. AWS Budgets
- D. AWS Trusted Advisor

**Q6.** Which AWS service is a content delivery network (CDN)?

- A. Amazon Route 53
- B. Amazon CloudFront
- C. AWS Direct Connect
- D. Amazon VPC

**Q7.** What is the main benefit of the AWS "pay-as-you-go" pricing model?

- A. You pay a fixed yearly fee no matter what
- B. You pay only for the resources you actually use
- C. All AWS services are free
- D. You must commit to 3 years upfront

**Q8.** Which tool records API calls made in your AWS account for auditing?

- A. Amazon CloudWatch
- B. AWS CloudTrail
- C. AWS Config
- D. Amazon Inspector

**Q9.** Which service provides DDoS protection?

- A. AWS WAF
- B. AWS Shield
- C. Amazon GuardDuty
- D. Amazon Macie

**Q10.** What is an Availability Zone?

- A. A single physical server
- B. One or more discrete data centers within a Region
- C. A global edge cache location
- D. A virtual private network

**Q11.** A startup wants the lowest-cost option for a workload that can be interrupted and restarted. Which EC2 purchasing option fits?

- A. On-Demand Instances
- B. Reserved Instances
- C. Spot Instances
- D. Dedicated Hosts

**Q12.** Which service should you use to estimate the cost of an architecture **before** building it?

- A. AWS Cost Explorer
- B. AWS Budgets
- C. AWS Pricing Calculator
- D. AWS Billing Dashboard

**Q13.** Which database type is Amazon DynamoDB?

- A. Relational (SQL)
- B. NoSQL key-value
- C. Data warehouse
- D. In-memory cache

**Q14.** What does enabling MFA on the root user provide?

- A. Free support
- B. An extra layer of sign-in security beyond the password
- C. Automatic cost savings
- D. Faster network performance

**Q15.** Which service translates domain names into IP addresses (DNS)?

- A. Amazon CloudFront
- B. Amazon Route 53
- C. AWS Direct Connect
- D. Amazon VPC

**Q16.** Which Well-Architected pillar focuses on running and monitoring systems to deliver business value and continually improve?

- A. Operational Excellence
- B. Reliability
- C. Sustainability
- D. Cost Optimization

**Q17.** A company needs shared file storage that many Linux EC2 instances can access at the same time. Which service?

- A. Amazon S3
- B. Amazon EBS
- C. Amazon EFS
- D. Amazon FSx for Windows File Server

**Q18.** Which support plan provides a designated Technical Account Manager (TAM)?

- A. Basic
- B. Developer
- C. Business
- D. Enterprise

**Q19.** What is AWS Trusted Advisor?

- A. A service that runs your code serverlessly
- B. A tool that gives recommendations across cost, security, performance, and more
- C. A relational database
- D. A network firewall

**Q20.** Which deployment model connects an on-premises data center with AWS resources?

- A. Public cloud
- B. Private cloud
- C. Hybrid cloud
- D. Multi-Region

### Quiz 1 — Answers & Explanations

**Q1 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Storage / S3.)* S3 is object storage for files, images, backups, etc.
- A describes EBS. C describes RDS. D describes CloudFront.

**Q2 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Compute / Lambda.)* Lambda runs code serverlessly; no servers to manage.
- EC2 needs you to manage servers. RDS is a database. VPC is networking.

**Q3 -> C.** *(Domain 2 — Shared Responsibility.)* Customers configure IAM users/permissions ("in" the cloud).
- A, B, D are AWS responsibilities ("of" the cloud).

**Q4 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Databases / RDS.)* RDS is the managed relational database.
- DynamoDB is NoSQL; S3 is object storage; Redshift is a data warehouse.

**Q5 -> C.** *(Domain 4 — Cost tools / Budgets.)* Budgets sends alerts when spending crosses a threshold.
- Pricing Calculator estimates beforehand; Cost Explorer analyzes/forecasts; Trusted Advisor gives recommendations.

**Q6 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Networking / CloudFront.)* CloudFront is the CDN.
- Route 53 = DNS; Direct Connect = private link; VPC = network.

**Q7 -> B.** *(Domain 1 — Cloud economics.)* Pay-as-you-go means paying only for what you use.
- A, C, D are false.

**Q8 -> B.** *(Domain 2 — Logging / CloudTrail.)* CloudTrail logs API activity for auditing.
- CloudWatch = metrics/alarms; Config = config changes; Inspector = vulnerability scanning.

**Q9 -> B.** *(Domain 2 — Protection / Shield.)* Shield protects against DDoS.
- WAF = web attacks; GuardDuty = threat detection; Macie = sensitive-data discovery.

**Q10 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Global infrastructure.)* An AZ is one or more discrete data centers within a Region.
- Not a single server, not an edge location, not a VPN.

**Q11 -> C.** *(Domain 4 — EC2 pricing / Spot.)* Spot is cheapest and suited to interruptible workloads.
- On-Demand has no discount; Reserved needs commitment; Dedicated Hosts are for licensing/compliance.

**Q12 -> C.** *(Domain 4 — Cost tools / Pricing Calculator.)* Pricing Calculator estimates costs before building.
- Cost Explorer/Budgets/Billing Dashboard deal with actual spend.

**Q13 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Databases / DynamoDB.)* DynamoDB is NoSQL key-value.

**Q14 -> B.** *(Domain 2 — IAM / MFA.)* MFA adds a second sign-in factor.

**Q15 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Networking / Route 53.)* Route 53 is DNS.

**Q16 -> A.** *(Domain 1 — Well-Architected.)* Operational Excellence = running/monitoring/improving systems.

**Q17 -> C.** *(Domain 3 — Storage / EFS.)* EFS is shared file storage for many Linux instances.
- S3 is object; EBS attaches to one instance; FSx for Windows is for Windows workloads.

**Q18 -> D.** *(Domain 4 — Support plans.)* A designated TAM comes with Enterprise.

**Q19 -> B.** *(Domain 3 — Management / Trusted Advisor.)* It gives recommendations across several categories.

**Q20 -> C.** *(Domain 1 — Deployment models.)* Hybrid connects on-premises with AWS.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Quiz 2 — Domain-Mixed Quiz (40 questions)

This quiz jumps between domains, just like the real exam. Give yourself about **50 minutes**.

**Q1.** A company runs an unpredictable workload that may be interrupted without harm. Which EC2 purchasing option is MOST cost-effective?

- A. Reserved Instances
- B. On-Demand Instances
- C. Spot Instances
- D. Dedicated Hosts

**Q2.** Which service helps you centrally manage and govern multiple AWS accounts?

- A. AWS IAM
- B. AWS Organizations
- C. AWS Config
- D. Amazon Cognito

**Q3.** (Choose TWO) Which of the following are AWS responsibilities under the Shared Responsibility Model?

- A. Patching the guest operating system on an EC2 instance
- B. Physical security of data centers
- C. Maintaining the global network infrastructure
- D. Configuring security groups
- E. Managing customer IAM users

**Q4.** Which storage service is best for archiving data for years at the lowest cost, where retrieval can take hours?

- A. Amazon S3 Standard
- B. Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive
- C. Amazon EBS
- D. Amazon EFS

**Q5.** A solutions team wants to deploy infrastructure using reusable templates. Which service should they use?

- A. AWS CloudFormation
- B. AWS Config
- C. Amazon CloudWatch
- D. AWS CloudTrail

**Q6.** Which service automatically distributes incoming application traffic across multiple targets?

- A. Amazon Route 53
- B. Elastic Load Balancing
- C. Amazon CloudFront
- D. AWS Global Accelerator

**Q7.** What is the BEST practice for the AWS account root user?

- A. Use it for all daily administrative tasks
- B. Share its password with the team
- C. Enable MFA and avoid using it for everyday tasks
- D. Delete it entirely

**Q8.** A company needs a NoSQL database with single-digit-millisecond performance at any scale. Which service?

- A. Amazon RDS
- B. Amazon Aurora
- C. Amazon DynamoDB
- D. Amazon Redshift

**Q9.** Which AWS service provides recommendations to optimize cost, performance, security, and fault tolerance?

- A. AWS Config
- B. AWS Trusted Advisor
- C. Amazon Inspector
- D. AWS CloudTrail

**Q10.** Which pricing model offers the most flexibility while still giving a discount for a 1- or 3-year usage commitment?

- A. Spot Instances
- B. On-Demand Instances
- C. Savings Plans
- D. Dedicated Hosts

**Q11.** A web application is being targeted by SQL injection attacks. Which service helps protect it?

- A. AWS Shield
- B. AWS WAF
- C. Amazon GuardDuty
- D. AWS KMS

**Q12.** Which service lets you analyze and visualize your past AWS spending and forecast future costs?

- A. AWS Pricing Calculator
- B. AWS Budgets
- C. AWS Cost Explorer
- D. AWS Cost and Usage Report

**Q13.** Which compute option requires the LEAST operational overhead for running containers?

- A. EC2 with Docker installed manually
- B. Amazon ECS on EC2
- C. AWS Fargate
- D. Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling

**Q14.** A company wants a private, dedicated network connection from its data center to AWS that does not use the public internet. Which service?

- A. AWS VPN
- B. AWS Direct Connect
- C. Amazon VPC peering
- D. Amazon CloudFront

**Q15.** Which AWS service stores and automatically rotates database credentials?

- A. AWS KMS
- B. AWS Secrets Manager
- C. AWS Certificate Manager
- D. AWS Systems Manager

**Q16.** Which of the following is an example of horizontal scaling?

- A. Increasing the instance size from medium to large
- B. Adding more EC2 instances to handle load
- C. Attaching a larger EBS volume
- D. Adding more memory to a single server

**Q17.** Which support plan is the MINIMUM that includes 24/7 access to support engineers by phone, chat, and email, plus full Trusted Advisor checks?

- A. Basic
- B. Developer
- C. Business
- D. Enterprise On-Ramp

**Q18.** A company wants to detect threats by continuously analyzing account activity and network logs. Which service?

- A. Amazon Inspector
- B. Amazon GuardDuty
- C. AWS Config
- D. AWS WAF

**Q19.** Which service provides on-demand access to AWS compliance reports such as SOC and PCI?

- A. AWS Artifact
- B. AWS Config
- C. AWS Trusted Advisor
- D. Amazon Macie

**Q20.** What does Amazon CloudWatch primarily provide?

- A. A record of who made API calls
- B. Metrics, logs, and alarms for monitoring resources
- C. A history of configuration changes
- D. Vulnerability scanning

**Q21.** A company wants to migrate 80 TB of data to AWS but has limited network bandwidth. Which option is BEST?

- A. Upload over the internet to S3
- B. AWS Snowball (Snow Family)
- C. AWS Direct Connect
- D. Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration

**Q22.** Which service is used to register a domain name and route users to your application?

- A. Amazon CloudFront
- B. Amazon Route 53
- C. AWS Global Accelerator
- D. Amazon VPC

**Q23.** Which Well-Architected pillar focuses on using the minimum resources needed and reducing environmental impact?

- A. Cost Optimization
- B. Performance Efficiency
- C. Sustainability
- D. Reliability

**Q24.** A security group on an EC2 instance is described as "stateful." What does that mean?

- A. It logs all traffic to CloudWatch
- B. Return traffic for an allowed inbound request is automatically allowed out
- C. It can explicitly deny specific IP addresses
- D. It operates at the subnet level

**Q25.** Which service can run a managed MySQL- and PostgreSQL-compatible database with higher performance than standard engines?

- A. Amazon DynamoDB
- B. Amazon Aurora
- C. Amazon Redshift
- D. Amazon ElastiCache

**Q26.** (Choose TWO) Which tools help a company control and monitor AWS costs?

- A. AWS Budgets
- B. AWS CloudTrail
- C. AWS Cost Explorer
- D. Amazon Inspector
- E. AWS WAF

**Q27.** Which IAM feature provides temporary credentials and is the recommended way for an EC2 instance to access an S3 bucket?

- A. IAM user with access keys stored on the instance
- B. IAM role
- C. Root user credentials
- D. IAM group

**Q28.** A company wants single sign-on access to multiple AWS accounts and business applications. Which service?

- A. Amazon Cognito
- B. AWS IAM Identity Center
- C. AWS Organizations
- D. AWS Directory Service

**Q29.** Which statement about Regions and Availability Zones is correct?

- A. A Region is a single data center
- B. Each Region has exactly one Availability Zone
- C. A Region contains multiple, isolated Availability Zones
- D. Availability Zones are the same as edge locations

**Q30.** Which service is designed to discover and protect sensitive data such as personally identifiable information (PII) stored in Amazon S3?

- A. Amazon Macie
- B. Amazon GuardDuty
- C. AWS Shield
- D. AWS WAF

**Q31.** A company wants to reduce the operational burden of running a relational database (backups, patching, failover). Which service helps MOST?

- A. Install a database on EC2
- B. Amazon RDS
- C. Amazon S3
- D. Amazon EFS

**Q32.** Which networking component allows instances in a private subnet to access the internet for updates while remaining unreachable from the internet?

- A. Internet Gateway
- B. NAT Gateway
- C. Security group
- D. Route 53

**Q33.** Which message service uses a publish/subscribe model to push messages to many subscribers at once?

- A. Amazon SQS
- B. Amazon SNS
- C. AWS Step Functions
- D. Amazon MQ

**Q34.** A company needs to run a serverless query directly on data stored in Amazon S3 using standard SQL. Which service?

- A. Amazon Redshift
- B. Amazon Athena
- C. AWS Glue
- D. Amazon QuickSight

**Q35.** Which of the following BEST describes "elasticity" in the AWS Cloud?

- A. Storing data in multiple Regions
- B. Automatically scaling resources up and down to match demand
- C. Encrypting data at rest
- D. Distributing traffic across instances

**Q36.** Which service provides a managed business intelligence dashboard for visualizing data?

- A. Amazon Athena
- B. Amazon QuickSight
- C. AWS Glue
- D. Amazon Kinesis

**Q37.** What does the AWS Free Tier "12 months free" category mean?

- A. Everything in AWS is free for 12 months
- B. Certain services are free up to a limit for 12 months after sign-up
- C. You get a refund after 12 months
- D. Free only for enterprise customers

**Q38.** A company must encrypt data and manage the encryption keys centrally. Which service?

- A. AWS KMS
- B. AWS Artifact
- C. Amazon Inspector
- D. AWS Config

**Q39.** Which service tracks changes to the configuration of your AWS resources over time and evaluates them against rules?

- A. AWS CloudTrail
- B. AWS Config
- C. Amazon CloudWatch
- D. AWS Trusted Advisor

**Q40.** A retailer expects huge, unpredictable traffic spikes during a sale. Which combination BEST keeps the application available and cost-efficient?

- A. A single large EC2 instance running 24/7
- B. EC2 Auto Scaling behind an Elastic Load Balancer
- C. One Reserved Instance with no scaling
- D. Storing the website in Amazon Glacier

### Quiz 2 — Answers & Explanations

**Q1 -> C.** *(D4 — EC2 pricing.)* Interruptible + unpredictable = Spot, the cheapest.
- Reserved/Dedicated suit steady use; On-Demand has no discount.

**Q2 -> B.** *(D2 — Organizations.)* Organizations centrally manages multiple accounts.
- IAM is within an account; Config tracks config; Cognito is app user sign-in.

**Q3 -> B and C.** *(D2 — Shared Responsibility.)* AWS handles physical security and the global infrastructure.
- A, D, E are customer responsibilities ("in" the cloud).

**Q4 -> B.** *(D3 — Storage classes.)* Glacier Deep Archive = lowest cost, long-term archive, hours to retrieve.
- S3 Standard is for frequent access; EBS/EFS are not archival cold storage.

**Q5 -> A.** *(D3 — Management / CloudFormation.)* CloudFormation deploys infrastructure from reusable templates (IaC).
- Config/CloudWatch/CloudTrail don't provision infrastructure.

**Q6 -> B.** *(D3 — Networking / ELB.)* Elastic Load Balancing distributes traffic across targets.
- Route 53 = DNS; CloudFront = CDN; Global Accelerator = network routing, not the textbook answer here.

**Q7 -> C.** *(D2 — Root best practices.)* Enable MFA, don't use root for daily tasks.
- A, B are unsafe; you cannot simply delete the root user.

**Q8 -> C.** *(D3 — Databases / DynamoDB.)* DynamoDB = NoSQL, single-digit-ms at scale.
- RDS/Aurora are relational; Redshift is analytics.

**Q9 -> B.** *(D3/D4 — Trusted Advisor.)* Trusted Advisor gives recommendations across cost, performance, security, fault tolerance, and service limits.

**Q10 -> C.** *(D4 — Savings Plans.)* Savings Plans give commitment discounts with more flexibility than RIs.
- Spot is interruptible; On-Demand has no discount; Dedicated Hosts are for licensing.

**Q11 -> B.** *(D2 — WAF.)* WAF filters web attacks like SQL injection and XSS.
- Shield = DDoS; GuardDuty = detection; KMS = keys.

**Q12 -> C.** *(D4 — Cost Explorer.)* Cost Explorer visualizes and forecasts spend.
- Pricing Calculator = estimate before; Budgets = alerts; CUR = raw detail.

**Q13 -> C.** *(D3 — Fargate.)* Fargate runs containers serverlessly = least operational overhead.
- The others require managing servers/scaling.

**Q14 -> B.** *(D3 — Direct Connect.)* Direct Connect is a private dedicated link that bypasses the public internet.
- VPN is encrypted over the internet; peering connects VPCs; CloudFront is a CDN.

**Q15 -> B.** *(D2 — Secrets Manager.)* Secrets Manager stores and rotates credentials.
- KMS manages keys; ACM manages certs; Systems Manager manages resources/config.

**Q16 -> B.** *(D1 — Scalability.)* Adding more instances = horizontal scaling (scaling out).
- A, C, D are vertical scaling (making one resource bigger).

**Q17 -> C.** *(D4 — Support plans.)* Business is the minimum with 24/7 engineer access and full Trusted Advisor.
- Basic/Developer are below it; Enterprise On-Ramp is above Business.

**Q18 -> B.** *(D2 — GuardDuty.)* GuardDuty continuously analyzes logs for threats.
- Inspector = vulnerability scans; Config = config tracking; WAF = web filtering.

**Q19 -> A.** *(D2 — Artifact.)* Artifact provides compliance reports on demand.

**Q20 -> B.** *(D2/D3 — CloudWatch.)* CloudWatch = metrics, logs, alarms.
- A = CloudTrail; C = Config; D = Inspector.

**Q21 -> B.** *(D3 — Migration / Snow Family.)* Large data + limited bandwidth = ship a Snowball device.
- Internet upload is too slow; Direct Connect takes time to set up; Transfer Acceleration still uses the internet.

**Q22 -> B.** *(D3 — Route 53.)* Route 53 registers domains and routes users (DNS).

**Q23 -> C.** *(D1 — Well-Architected.)* Sustainability = minimizing resources and environmental impact.
- Cost Optimization is about money; the others are different pillars.

**Q24 -> B.** *(D3 — Security groups.)* Stateful = return traffic for an allowed request is automatically allowed.
- C and D describe NACLs.

**Q25 -> B.** *(D3 — Aurora.)* Aurora is the high-performance MySQL/PostgreSQL-compatible engine.

**Q26 -> A and C.** *(D4 — Cost tools.)* Budgets (alerts) and Cost Explorer (analysis) control/monitor cost.
- CloudTrail, Inspector, WAF are security/audit tools.

**Q27 -> B.** *(D2 — IAM roles.)* An IAM role gives temporary credentials and is best practice for EC2-to-S3 access.
- Storing user keys on an instance or using root is insecure; a group can't be assumed by an instance.

**Q28 -> B.** *(D2 — IAM Identity Center.)* Identity Center provides SSO across accounts and apps.
- Cognito is for app end-users; Organizations manages accounts; Directory Service provides managed AD.

**Q29 -> C.** *(D3 — Global infrastructure.)* A Region contains multiple isolated AZs.

**Q30 -> A.** *(D2 — Macie.)* Macie discovers and protects sensitive data (PII) in S3.

**Q31 -> B.** *(D3 — RDS.)* RDS is managed: backups, patching, failover handled for you.
- Installing on EC2 keeps the burden on you; S3/EFS aren't relational databases.

**Q32 -> B.** *(D3 — NAT Gateway.)* A NAT gateway lets private-subnet instances reach the internet outbound while staying unreachable inbound.
- IGW exposes resources publicly; security groups/Route 53 don't do this.

**Q33 -> B.** *(D3 — SNS.)* SNS uses pub/sub to push to many subscribers.
- SQS is a pull queue; Step Functions orchestrate workflows; MQ is a managed message broker.

**Q34 -> B.** *(D3 — Athena.)* Athena runs serverless SQL queries directly on S3 data.
- Redshift needs loading into a warehouse; Glue is ETL; QuickSight is BI dashboards.

**Q35 -> B.** *(D1 — Elasticity.)* Elasticity = auto scaling up and down with demand.

**Q36 -> B.** *(D3 — QuickSight.)* QuickSight is the managed BI/dashboard service.

**Q37 -> B.** *(D4 — Free Tier.)* "12 months free" = certain services free up to a limit for 12 months after sign-up.

**Q38 -> A.** *(D2 — KMS.)* KMS centrally creates and manages encryption keys.

**Q39 -> B.** *(D2 — Config.)* Config tracks resource configuration changes and evaluates compliance.
- CloudTrail logs API calls; CloudWatch monitors metrics; Trusted Advisor gives recommendations.

**Q40 -> B.** *(D1/D3 — Scaling & HA.)* Auto Scaling behind an ELB handles spikes and saves cost by scaling down afterward.
- A single instance can't scale; one RI doesn't scale; Glacier is archival storage.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Quiz 3 — Full Mock Exam 1 (65 questions)

This is a full-length, full-difficulty practice exam. **Set a timer for 90 minutes.** Don't check answers until you finish. Treat it like the real thing.

**Q1.** Which of the following is a benefit of cloud computing as described by AWS?

- A. Eliminating all customer responsibility for security
- B. Trading fixed expense for variable expense
- C. Guaranteeing applications never fail
- D. Removing the need to monitor anything

**Q2.** A company needs to store frequently accessed objects with millisecond access and high durability. Which service and class?

- A. S3 Glacier Deep Archive
- B. S3 Standard
- C. EBS Cold HDD
- D. EFS Infrequent Access

**Q3.** Which AWS service records who made an API call, when, and from where?

- A. Amazon CloudWatch
- B. AWS CloudTrail
- C. AWS Config
- D. AWS Trusted Advisor

**Q4.** (Choose TWO) Which are customer responsibilities under the Shared Responsibility Model?

- A. Encrypting customer data
- B. Securing the physical facilities
- C. Managing IAM permissions
- D. Maintaining the hypervisor
- E. Replacing failed hardware

**Q5.** A workload needs to run code in response to file uploads in S3, with no servers to manage. Which service?

- A. Amazon EC2
- B. AWS Lambda
- C. AWS Batch
- D. Amazon ECS on EC2

- B. Spot
- C. Reserved Instances (3-year, all upfront)

- D. AWS Batch

**Q44.** A company wants to reduce read latency for a database-heavy application by caching frequent queries in memory. Which service?

- A. Amazon RDS
- B. Amazon ElastiCache
- C. Amazon Redshift
- D. Amazon DynamoDB
