# Security+ SY0-701 Keyword Decoder

| Keyword in question | Think of |
|---|---|
| "Only authorized people can read" | Confidentiality |
| "Data hasn't been changed" | Integrity |
| "System is accessible when needed" | Availability |
| "Prove who you are" | Authentication |
| "What can you access" | Authorization |
| "Can't deny doing it" | Non-repudiation |
| "Fake it to get access" | Social engineering / Pretexting |
| "Targeted executive phishing" | Whaling |
| "Mass email credential theft" | Phishing |
| "Phone phishing" | Vishing |
| "SMS phishing" | Smishing |
| "Spreads without user action, over network" | Worm |
| "Self-replicates, needs user action" | Virus |
| "Disguised as legitimate software" | Trojan |
| "Hides in OS kernel" | Rootkit |
| "Encrypts files, demands payment" | Ransomware |
| "Runs in memory only, no disk files" | Fileless malware |
| "Inserts SQL commands into input" | SQL Injection |
| "Runs scripts in other users' browsers" | XSS (stored or reflected) |
| "Tricks browser to make unauthorized request" | CSRF |
| "Writes beyond buffer boundary" | Buffer overflow |
| "Accesses other user's data via ID manipulation" | IDOR |
| "Multiple failed logins, many accounts" | Credential stuffing / Brute force |
| "Intercepts communication between two parties" | MITM / On-path attack |
| "Fake DNS records redirect traffic" | DNS Poisoning / Pharming |
| "Floods target to make it unavailable" | DoS/DDoS |
| "TCP SYN flood, fills connection table" | Protocol DDoS |
| "Network of compromised hosts controlled by attacker" | Botnet |
| "Software + hardware security all-in-one" | UTM |
| "Monitors and blocks inline" | IPS |
| "Monitors and alerts only, passive" | IDS |
| "Learns baseline, alerts on deviations" | Anomaly-based detection |
| "Matches known patterns" | Signature-based detection |
| "Web layer HTTP protection" | WAF |
| "All SSL, detect on network" | SSL inspection / TLS inspection |
| "Windows domain authentication, tickets" | Kerberos |
| "Enterprise cloud SSO" | SAML |
| "Modern web app login via Google" | OAuth 2.0 / OIDC |
| "Network VPN/WiFi authentication server" | RADIUS |
| "Cisco device management AAA" | TACACS+ |
| "Each session has a unique key, past sessions safe" | Perfect Forward Secrecy (PFS/ECDHE) |
| "Owner sets permissions" | DAC |
| "System enforces labels, government" | MAC |
| "Job roles determine access" | RBAC |
| "Multiple attributes (time, location)" | ABAC |
| "Something you know, have, are" | MFA factors |
| "Hardware security module, dedicated" | HSM |
| "PKI certificate revocation, real-time" | OCSP |
| "Certificate trusted by chain" | PKI chain of trust |
| "Identify → Protect → Detect → Respond → Recover" | NIST CSF |
| "Preparation → Detection → Containment → Recovery" | NIST IR lifecycle |
| "EU data, 72-hour notification" | GDPR |
| "Credit card security standard" | PCI DSS |
| "US healthcare data" | HIPAA |
| "Asset Value × Exposure Factor" | SLE formula |
| "SLE × ARO" | ALE formula |
| "Risk after controls are applied" | Residual risk |
| "Transfer financial risk" | Risk transference (insurance) |
| "Don't do the risky activity" | Risk avoidance |
| "Document and accept the risk" | Risk acceptance |
| "Full disk backup, slowest to restore" | Full backup |
| "Since last full, fastest restore" | Differential backup |
| "Since last any backup, slowest restore" | Incremental backup |
| "3 copies, 2 media types, 1 offsite" | 3-2-1 backup rule |
| "Can't be deleted for set period" | Immutable backup |
| "Most volatile, collect first" | RAM |
| "Bit-for-bit exact copy" | Forensic image |
| "Document who had evidence" | Chain of custody |
| "Proactively search for hidden threats" | Threat hunting |
| "Government-sponsored, long-term, sophisticated" | APT / Nation-state actor |
| "Ideologically motivated attacker" | Hacktivist |
| "Test running app, black-box" | DAST |
| "Analyze source code, no running" | SAST |
| "Send random input to find crashes" | Fuzzing |
| "Monitor all endpoint behavior continuously" | EDR |
| "Manage mobile devices remotely" | MDM |
| "Cloud security configuration scanner" | CSPM |
| "Policy enforcement between user and cloud" | CASB |

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Security+ Exam Traps

1. **IDS alerts, IPS blocks.** IDS = passive/detective. IPS = active/preventive.
2. **RAID is NOT a backup.** RAID protects against hardware failure, not ransomware or accidental deletion.
3. **Risk acceptance is NOT ignoring risk.** It requires documented management sign-off.
4. **Qualitative ≠ Quantitative.** Qualitative = words (High/Medium/Low). Quantitative = numbers (ALE formula).
5. **AH doesn't encrypt. ESP does.** AH = authentication + integrity, no encryption. ESP = everything.
6. **Worms don't need user action. Viruses and Trojans do.**
7. **Spear phishing = specific individual. Whaling = executive. Phishing = everyone.**
8. **Stored XSS = most dangerous (affects all users). Reflected XSS = affects one user.**
9. **SHA-1 is deprecated. MD5 is broken. Use SHA-256 or bcrypt.**
10. **Incremental backup = fastest backup, SLOWEST restore.** Full + all incrementals needed to restore.
11. **Differential backup = cumulative from last full.** Only need full + latest differential to restore.
12. **GDPR = 72-hour notification. HIPAA has different timeframes (60 days for written notification).**
13. **MAC uses labels enforced by the system. DAC is owner-controlled.**
14. **RADIUS encrypts only the password. TACACS+ encrypts the entire payload.**
15. **Penetration testing finds exploitable vulnerabilities. Vulnerability scanning finds all known weaknesses (including non-exploitable).**
16. **PBQs appear early in the exam — skip them first and come back.**
17. **Order of volatility: RAM first, hard drive last.**
18. **Containment comes BEFORE eradication in the IR lifecycle.** You stop the spread first, then clean up.
19. **Security Awareness Training is the most effective control against social engineering.**
20. **Zero-day = no patch available yet. Mitigate with compensating controls.**

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Practice Questions

> Up to 90 questions in 90 minutes. About 1 minute per question. Skip PBQs first. Always answer every question — no penalty for guessing. The exam wants the BEST answer, not just a correct one. All questions here are original.

## Full Mock Exam 1 — Security+ SY0-701 (90 questions)

**Q1.** Which CIA property is violated when an attacker changes a database record without authorization?

- A. Confidentiality
- B. Availability
- C. Integrity
- D. Authentication

**Q2.** A user's password database was stolen. The attacker wants to crack the passwords. Which stored password format is the HARDEST to crack?

- A. MD5 hashes
- B. SHA-1 hashes
- C. Plaintext
- D. bcrypt with salt

**Q3.** An attacker sends millions of SYN packets to a web server, preventing legitimate connections. What type of attack is this?

- A. Smurf attack
- B. TCP SYN flood (protocol-level DDoS)
- C. SQL injection
- D. Replay attack

**Q4.** Which type of malware requires a host file to attach to and needs user action to spread?

- A. Worm
- B. Virus
- C. RAT
- D. Fileless malware

**Q5.** A company's firewall tracks the state of TCP connections and knows which packets are part of established sessions. What type of firewall is this?

- A. Packet-filtering firewall
- B. Stateful inspection firewall
- C. Application proxy
- D. WAF

**Q6.** An employee receives an email that appears to be from the CEO asking for an urgent wire transfer. This is most likely:

- A. Phishing
- B. Watering hole attack
- C. Business Email Compromise (BEC) / Whaling
- D. Pretexting via email

**Q7.** Which authentication factor category does a fingerprint belong to?

- A. Something you know
- B. Something you have
- C. Something you are
- D. Somewhere you are

**Q8.** A company stores encrypted customer data. If the encryption keys are destroyed, the data is irrecoverable even if stolen. What is this data destruction method?

- A. Degaussing
- B. Shredding
- C. Crypto-shredding
- D. Overwriting

**Q9.** Which access control model allows the resource owner to determine who can access resources?

- A. MAC (Mandatory Access Control)
- B. DAC (Discretionary Access Control)
- C. RBAC (Role-Based Access Control)
- D. ABAC (Attribute-Based Access Control)

**Q10.** An IDS generates many false positives (legitimate traffic flagged as malicious). Which detection method is most likely responsible?

- A. Signature-based detection
- B. Anomaly-based (behavior-based) detection
- C. Protocol analysis
- D. Heuristic detection

**Q11.** A company wants to implement SSO for their employees to access Office 365 using their Active Directory credentials. Which protocol should they use?

- A. RADIUS
- B. TACACS+
- C. SAML
- D. Kerberos

**Q12.** Which backup strategy requires ALL incrementals since the last full backup for restoration?

- A. Full backup
- B. Differential backup
- C. Incremental backup
- D. Continuous backup

**Q13.** An organization wants to protect against attackers eavesdropping on their VPN traffic AND achieve perfect forward secrecy. Which key exchange should their VPN use?

- A. RSA key exchange
- B. Static Diffie-Hellman (DH)
- C. ECDHE (Ephemeral Elliptic Curve Diffie-Hellman)
- D. AES-256

**Q14.** A system administrator discovers that an attacker used NTLM hashes from memory to authenticate without cracking the passwords. What type of attack is this?

- A. Credential stuffing
- B. Pass-the-Hash
- C. Golden Ticket attack
- D. Rainbow table attack

**Q15.** Which security framework uses five core functions: Identify, Protect, Detect, Respond, and Recover?

- A. ISO/IEC 27001
- B. PCI DSS
- C. NIST Cybersecurity Framework (CSF)
- D. COBIT

**Q16.** A company wants to prevent sensitive data from being sent via email. Which technology should they implement?

- A. IPS
- B. DLP (Data Loss Prevention)
- C. WAF
- D. CASB

**Q17.** A web application displays user-submitted comments without sanitizing input. An attacker submits a comment containing JavaScript, which executes for all users who view the page. What type of attack is this?

- A. Reflected XSS
- B. CSRF
- C. Stored (Persistent) XSS
- D. DOM-based XSS

**Q18.** During a forensic investigation, what should be collected FIRST according to the order of volatility?

- A. Hard drive image
- B. System logs
- C. RAM dump
- D. External backup tapes

**Q19.** Which regulation requires notifying the supervisory authority of a personal data breach within 72 hours?

- A. HIPAA
- B. PCI DSS

**Q21.** Which protocol provides AAA for network device administration and encrypts the ENTIRE communication payload?

**Q23.** A company implements security cameras, locked server rooms, and a mantraps. These controls are classified as:

**Q24.** Which risk response involves purchasing cybersecurity insurance?

**Q30.** Which cryptographic algorithm is considered BROKEN due to collision vulnerabilities?

**Q35.** Which RAID level provides the BEST combination of read performance, write performance, and fault tolerance (2 disk failure)?

**Q36.** An organization encrypts all traffic between internal servers to prevent sniffing even from internal attackers. This is an example of:

- A. NTLM

**Q78.** An organization discovers that an attacker has been present in their network for 6 months, exfiltrating data gradually. Which threat intelligence concept describes this stealthy, long-term attack?

**Q85.** An organization wants to allow employees to use personal phones for work email but maintain the ability to wipe corporate data only (not personal data) remotely. Which solution?

**Q86.** A security alert shows that a critical server's configuration file was modified without an associated change ticket. Which security principle was violated?

- A. Least privilege

**Q87.** Which type of attack on wireless networks deauthenticates clients from an access point, forcing them to reconnect and exposing the WPA2 handshake for capture?

- A. Evil twin attack
- B. WPS brute force
- C. Deauthentication attack (802.11 deauth frames)

**Q88.** A company stores passwords as MD5 hashes without salt. An attacker obtains the hash database and has a precomputed table of hashes for common passwords. What attack will they use?

- A. Brute force
- B. Rainbow table attack
- C. Pass-the-Hash
- D. Birthday attack

**Q89.** (Performance-Based) A network diagram shows a web server in Zone A, an application server in Zone B, and a database in Zone C. What security device should be placed between each zone?

- A. IDS between each zone
- B. Firewall between each zone to control inter-zone traffic
- C. VPN between each zone
- D. Load balancer between each zone

**Q90.** A company's IR team has fully eradicated malware and restored systems. What should they do NEXT?

- A. Start another incident response
- B. Update vendor contracts
- C. Conduct a post-incident review (lessons learned) and update the IR plan
- D. Archive all logs permanently

### Mock Exam 1 — Answers (All 90)

**Q1 -> C.** Unauthorized modification = integrity violation.
**Q2 -> D.** bcrypt with salt = slow hash + salt prevents rainbow tables. MD5/SHA-1 = fast (weak for passwords).
**Q3 -> B.** TCP SYN flood = protocol-level DDoS (fills the half-open connection table).
**Q4 -> B.** Virus attaches to files, needs user action to spread.
**Q5 -> B.** Stateful inspection tracks connection state. Packet filtering is stateless.
**Q6 -> C.** BEC targeting executive (CFO) = whaling/business email compromise.
**Q7 -> C.** Biometrics (fingerprint) = something you are.
**Q8 -> C.** Crypto-shredding = destroy encryption keys = data unrecoverable.
**Q9 -> B.** DAC = owner-controlled permissions.
**Q10 -> B.** Anomaly-based = baseline deviations, high false positive rate.
**Q11 -> C.** SAML = enterprise browser-based SSO (AD → cloud apps).
**Q12 -> C.** Incremental backup: need full + all subsequent incrementals to restore.
**Q13 -> C.** ECDHE = ephemeral key pairs = perfect forward secrecy.
**Q14 -> B.** Pass-the-Hash = uses captured NTLM hash directly without cracking.
**Q15 -> C.** NIST CSF = Identify, Protect, Detect, Respond, Recover.
**Q16 -> B.** DLP = prevents unauthorized data transfer via email, USB, etc.
**Q17 -> C.** Stored XSS = injected script is persisted in DB and runs for all users.
**Q18 -> C.** RAM is most volatile = collect first.
**Q19 -> C.** GDPR = 72-hour breach notification to supervisory authority.
**Q20 -> C.** White box = full knowledge (architecture, credentials, code).
**Q21 -> C.** TACACS+ = encrypts entire payload; device administration.
**Q22 -> C.** Threat hunting = proactive analyst-driven search.
**Q23 -> C.** Cameras, locks, server rooms = physical controls.
**Q24 -> D.** Insurance = risk transference.
**Q25 -> C.** Golden Ticket = forged TGT from compromised KDC.
**Q26 -> B.** Typosquatting = registering similar-looking domain names.
**Q27 -> C.** CVSS 9.0–10.0 = Critical.
**Q28 -> B.** Separation of duties = no single person controls entire process.
**Q29 -> C.** Credentialed scan = authenticates to target for thorough assessment.
**Q30 -> C.** MD5 = broken (collision attacks demonstrated). SHA-256 and AES-256 are current.
**Q31 -> B.** Hybrid encryption = symmetric for data + asymmetric for key exchange.
**Q32 -> C.** ESP = authentication + integrity + encryption. AH = no encryption.
**Q33 -> C.** Social engineering/impersonation + pretexting over phone.
**Q34 -> B.** MDM = enforces PIN, encryption, remote wipe on mobile devices.
**Q35 -> C.** RAID 6 = striping with double parity = survives 2 disk failures. RAID 10 also good.
**Q36 -> D.** Encrypting east-west (internal) traffic = zero trust principle.
**Q37 -> A.** Impossible travel = IoC for compromised account (can't be in two countries in 30 min).
**Q38 -> D.** Directive control = tells people what to do (policies, procedures).
**Q39 -> B.** Phishing simulation + follow-up training = most effective combined approach.
**Q40 -> C.** PCI DSS = credit card data standard.
**Q41 -> C.** Baiting = leaving infected USB drives hoping someone plugs them in.
**Q42 -> D.** bcrypt = slow, salted, designed for passwords.
**Q43 -> B.** Red/Blue team exercise = attacker vs defender without script.
**Q44 -> C.** Generator = compensating/physical control for availability.
**Q45 -> B.** ARO = Annual Rate of Occurrence of the threat event.
**Q46 -> B.** Supply chain attack = compromise of trusted vendor/software distribution.
**Q47 -> B.** Content filter/web proxy with URL filtering = blocks specific categories.
**Q48 -> C.** Wildcard certificate = *.domain.com (all subdomains).
**Q49 -> B.** Session hijacking = using stolen session token to impersonate user.
**Q50 -> D.** After Detection & Analysis → Containment. Stop the spread first.
**Q51 -> C.** Wireshark = network packet capture/analysis.
**Q52 -> B.** Admin access after initial compromise = privilege escalation.
**Q53 -> B.** Immutable infrastructure = never patch in place; replace from clean baseline.
**Q54 -> B.** DNS poisoning/cache poisoning = injecting false DNS records.
**Q55 -> C.** MITRE ATT&CK = adversary TTPs mapped to attack phases.
**Q56 -> C.** Security awareness training = administrative control, preventive (prevents clicks) and detective (trained users recognize and report).
**Q57 -> C.** Dual control/separation of duties = no one person completes the full transaction.
**Q58 -> B.** OCSP = real-time certificate revocation status. Runs on 443/80.
**Q59 -> C.** Blocking outbound Telnet = preventive (stops before connection).
**Q60 -> C.** CSRF = tricks authenticated user's browser into making unauthorized requests.
**Q61 -> C.** Out-of-band NIDS on SPAN port = passive, doesn't interrupt traffic.
**Q62 -> B.** RTO = Recovery Time Objective = how long until systems are restored.
**Q63 -> C.** Microsegmentation = granular per-workload security policies.
**Q64 -> C.** Degaussing + shredding = highest assurance for magnetic HDD.
**Q65 -> D.** Containment first = isolate server to stop C2 communication and spread.
**Q66 -> B.** ECB = each block encrypted independently = same plaintext = same ciphertext. Insecure.
**Q67 -> B.** CASB = security policy enforcement between users and cloud services.
**Q68 -> C.** Watering hole = infecting a site frequented by the target audience.
**Q69 -> D.** HIPAA = US healthcare patient data.
**Q70 -> C.** SSO = single login, multiple apps.
**Q71 -> C.** Network isolation (VLAN + strict firewall rules) = compensating control for EOL system.
**Q72 -> B.** Active scan = sends probes to target.
**Q73 -> C.** Excessive admin rights = violation of least privilege.
**Q74 -> C.** OAuth 2.0 access tokens with scopes = limited access without password sharing.
**Q75 -> D.** Long-term, sophisticated, government-linked = nation-state / APT.
**Q76 -> C.** Client-side encryption = data encrypted before leaving client; provider can't read it.
**Q77 -> B.** Kerberos = ticket-based auth in Windows AD environments.
**Q78 -> B.** 6-month presence, stealthy exfiltration = APT characteristic.
**Q79 -> C.** Fuzzing = random/malformed input to find crashes and vulnerabilities.
**Q80 -> C.** MTD = Maximum Tolerable Downtime = business's survival limit.
**Q81 -> B.** Security testing in SDLC = DevSecOps / shift-left security.
**Q82 -> B.** Volatility = memory forensics (RAM analysis).
**Q83 -> B.** OCSP Stapling = server includes OCSP response in TLS handshake.
**Q84 -> C.** OSINT = open source, publicly available, free threat intel.
**Q85 -> B.** MAM = manages only corporate apps/data on personal device (not full device wipe).
**Q86 -> C.** Unauthorized change = change management violation.
**Q87 -> C.** Deauthentication attack = forged deauth frames disconnect clients.
**Q88 -> B.** Rainbow table = precomputed hash lookup. No salt = same password = same hash = easy lookup.
**Q89 -> B.** Firewalls between zones = controls inter-zone traffic.
**Q90 -> C.** Post-incident review = lessons learned, update IR plan.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Full Mock Exam 2 — Security+ SY0-701 (90 questions, Condensed Format with Answers)

> Format: Question → Answer → One-line explanation. Study by covering the answer column.

**Q1.** Which CIA property protects against unauthorized modification? → **C: Integrity**
**Q2.** An attacker uses a list of breached passwords to try logging into many accounts. → **B: Credential stuffing**
**Q3.** Which protocol uses a KDC (Key Distribution Center) for ticket-based auth? → **B: Kerberos**
**Q4.** A SIEM correlates events but a separate tool automates the response (blocking IPs, opening tickets). → **C: SOAR**
**Q5.** Which malware is specifically designed to persist in the system kernel and remain hidden? → **A: Rootkit**
**Q6.** An employee tailgates through a secure door behind an authorized person. → **D: Physical social engineering (tailgating)**
**Q7.** Which encryption algorithm uses smaller keys than RSA for equivalent security, common in mobile? → **C: ECC**
**Q8.** A company implements full-disk encryption on all laptops. What CIA property is primarily protected? → **A: Confidentiality**
**Q9.** What provides both integrity and authentication verification using a shared key + hash? → **D: HMAC**
**Q10.** Which IR phase involves removing malware and closing attacker backdoors? → **C: Eradication**
**Q11.** A server running an unpatched vulnerability is exploited before the vendor releases a fix. → **B: Zero-day exploit**
**Q12.** Which tool specifically tests web server security, scanning for common web vulnerabilities? → **C: Nikto**
**Q13.** A company needs to classify an asset worth $500,000. A breach exposes 20% of its value. ARO = 2. ALE = ? → **B: $200,000** (SLE = $100k, ALE = $100k × 2)
**Q14.** An org's DMZ contains a web server, email server, and DNS server. Which firewall placement is correct? → **B: One between internet and DMZ, one between DMZ and internal**
**Q15.** Which technique hides data inside image files to avoid detection? → **C: Steganography**
**Q16.** Which recovery objective measures how old the most recent backup data can be? → **A: RPO (Recovery Point Objective)**
**Q17.** An attacker sends a link via SMS that directs the user to a fake banking page. → **B: Smishing**
**Q18.** Which access control model is MOST appropriate for a top-secret government network? → **C: MAC (Mandatory Access Control)**
**Q19.** A security policy requires employees to review sensitive documents only on company devices, not personal ones. → **B: ABAC / Data access policy**
**Q20.** What type of certificate allows secure access to api.company.com, mail.company.com, and portal.company.com under one cert? → **C: SAN (Subject Alternative Name) Certificate**
**Q21.** A WAF is placed in front of a web application. What layer does it operate at? → **D: Layer 7 (Application)**
**Q22.** Which attack overwrites memory beyond a buffer's boundary to redirect code execution? → **A: Buffer overflow**
**Q23.** A user authenticates with a password (something you know) and a hardware token (something you have). Is this MFA? → **A: Yes — two different factor types**
**Q24.** Logs show outbound DNS queries to randomly generated domain names at regular intervals. What does this suggest? → **C: DNS tunneling / C2 communication**
**Q25.** A company performs a comprehensive security review against ISO 27001. What is this process? → **B: Information security audit**
**Q26.** Which hashing algorithm should be used for verifying file download integrity? → **B: SHA-256**
**Q27.** An organization requires vendors to sign a legal agreement that protects shared business information. → **C: NDA (Non-Disclosure Agreement)**
**Q28.** A firewall rule denies TCP port 22 (SSH) inbound from all external IPs. What type of control is this? → **B: Technical preventive control**
**Q29.** Which tool monitors and analyzes network traffic in real-time, sending alerts on suspicious patterns? → **A: NIDS (Network Intrusion Detection System)**
**Q30.** A company discovers that 100 of its servers are infected and being used to mine cryptocurrency. → **D: Botnet / Cryptojacking**
**Q31.** Which backup restoration requires the Full backup + ALL subsequent incremental backups? → **B: Incremental backup strategy**
**Q32.** A forensic investigator calculates MD5 hash of the original drive and the forensic copy. Why? → **C: To verify forensic integrity (chain of custody / evidence integrity)**
**Q33.** Which PKI component checks in real-time whether a certificate has been revoked? → **B: OCSP**
**Q34.** Which type of security test involves no prior knowledge of the system, simulating an external attacker? → **A: Black box test**
**Q35.** An employee's laptop is lost. The company remotely activates encryption and locks the device. → **B: MDM capabilities (remote lock/wipe/encrypt)**
**Q36.** What is the FIRST phase of the NIST Incident Response lifecycle? → **A: Preparation**
**Q37.** An attacker compromises the web server in a DMZ. Due to the second firewall, the internal network remains safe. This demonstrates: → **C: Defense in depth / DMZ architecture**
**Q38.** Which attack targets the CPU, cache, and registers by sending random garbage data? → **B: Fuzzing**
**Q39.** A vulnerability scanning report shows CVEs for a Windows server. Which metric rates the severity? → **B: CVSS (Common Vulnerability Scoring System)**
**Q40.** What does a "warm site" DR setup mean? → **B: Partially equipped standby facility that takes hours to days to activate**
**Q41.** An attacker bypasses password authentication by using the captured NTLM hash directly. → **B: Pass-the-Hash**
**Q42.** Which social engineering attack creates a believable scenario (e.g., "I'm from IT") to manipulate? → **C: Pretexting**
**Q43.** A company's SIEM ingests logs from firewalls, servers, and endpoints and correlates events. What feature finds patterns across different log sources? → **B: Log correlation**
**Q44.** Which type of encryption protects data while it's being transmitted between systems? → **B: Encryption in transit (TLS)**
**Q45.** Which is the MOST comprehensive method for preventing physical theft of data on a decommissioned hard drive? → **D: Degaussing + physical shredding**
**Q46.** A developer stores API keys in GitHub source code. Which control should have prevented this? → **B: SAST / secrets scanning in CI/CD pipeline + developer training**
**Q47.** Which attack floods a server with more traffic than its TCP state table can handle? → **B: SYN flood**
**Q48.** A company notices encrypted traffic to an unusual IP at 3am from a server. The FIRST response is: → **C: Containment — isolate the server and investigate**
**Q49.** Which certificate validation method is embedded directly in the browser and doesn't require online lookup? → **C: Certificate pinning**
**Q50.** An organization implements least privilege, MFA, and microsegmentation. This aligns with: → **B: Zero Trust architecture**
**Q51.** Sensitive emails are accidentally sent to external addresses. Which DLP mode is most appropriate to BLOCK this? → **B: Active/Enforcement mode DLP (block + alert)**
**Q52.** What cryptographic property ensures that a signed message couldn't have been signed by anyone else? → **C: Non-repudiation (via digital signature)**
**Q53.** Which test evaluates code vulnerabilities by executing the application and testing its inputs/outputs? → **B: DAST (Dynamic Application Security Testing)**
**Q54.** Which threat actor is motivated by ideology rather than financial gain? → **C: Hacktivist**
**Q55.** A hospital's EHR system processes patient data. Which regulation primarily applies? → **D: HIPAA**
**Q56.** An attacker registers "paypa1.com" hoping users mistype PayPal's URL. → **B: Typosquatting**
**Q57.** Which physical security control detects unauthorized entry attempts using weight sensors on a secure room's floor? → **B: Physical/Technical detective control**
**Q58.** A company uses split tunneling on its VPN. What is the PRIMARY security concern? → **C: Infected device can be on both VPN and internet simultaneously (dual access risk)**
**Q59.** A company runs tabletop exercises quarterly. These test which aspect of security? → **B: Incident response preparedness / IR plan effectiveness**
**Q60.** Which attack modifies the ARP cache to associate the attacker's MAC with the victim's IP? → **A: ARP poisoning (MITM)**
**Q61.** A company digitally signs its software with a code signing certificate. This provides: → **C: Integrity + authenticity (software wasn't tampered with and came from trusted source)**
**Q62.** Which tool gives an attacker remote control over a victim's machine, often used in APT campaigns? → **D: RAT (Remote Access Trojan)**
**Q63.** An SOC analyst identifies an unknown process communicating outbound on TCP 443. FIRST step? → **B: Investigate the process (parent process, hash, behavior) before taking action**
**Q64.** Which DR strategy has systems fully running in both primary and DR sites simultaneously? → **D: Active-Active (Hot/Hot)**
**Q65.** A company's third-party vendor has access to their network. What agreement ensures the vendor meets security standards? → **C: BAA (Business Associate Agreement) for healthcare; SLA/security addendum in general**
**Q66.** An attacker uses a victim's credentials captured last week to log in today. The session token is expired. → **B: Replay attack prevention worked (session token expired)**
**Q67.** Which wireless security standard replaced WPA2's PSK with SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals)? → **C: WPA3**
**Q68.** A company uses multi-layered security: firewall + IPS + EDR + DLP. This is an example of: → **A: Defense in depth**
**Q69.** A user clicks a malicious link in an email that downloads and runs a file. This represents which threat vector? → **B: Phishing / email-borne malware**
**Q70.** Which algorithm is used by HTTPS to negotiate which cipher suite to use at the beginning of a TLS session? → **B: TLS handshake (negotiates cipher suite, includes key exchange)**
**Q71.** A mobile device policy requires that personal apps be wiped separately from work apps. → **B: MAM (Mobile Application Management) or container-based MDM**
**Q72.** Which log source would BEST show whether an attacker attempted SQL injection via web requests? → **C: Web server/WAF access logs**
**Q73.** An org's security policy says: "Users must complete security awareness training annually." → **B: Administrative, Directive control**
**Q74.** A forensic analyst finds files with creation dates from 6 months ago on a server compromised yesterday. What should they investigate? → **B: Timestamps may have been modified (anti-forensics) or files were pre-staged**
**Q75.** What term describes a system with no network connection to prevent unauthorized access? → **A: Air gap**
**Q76.** An organization wants continuous security monitoring across all endpoints, networks, and cloud. Which solution? → **C: XDR (Extended Detection and Response)**
**Q77.** A company stores customer SSNs, dates of birth, and email addresses. This data is classified as: → **B: PII (Personally Identifiable Information)**
**Q78.** An attacker discovers a vulnerability in a web app, reports it responsibly to the vendor, and receives a reward. → **C: Bug bounty program / responsible disclosure**
**Q79.** Which principle limits information access only to those who need it for their specific job function? → **B: Need to know**
**Q80.** A message is sent and the recipient can verify who sent it and that it wasn't altered. Which is used? → **C: Digital signature (asymmetric private key sign + public key verify)**
**Q81.** An employee uses a personal Dropbox account to share company files with a client. Which control detects this? → **B: CASB (detects shadow IT / unauthorized cloud usage)**
**Q82.** Which attack exploits trust relationships in a software supply chain to distribute malware? → **D: Supply chain attack (like SolarWinds)**
**Q83.** A forensic investigator needs to ensure the disk image is not modified during collection. What device is used? → **C: Hardware write blocker**
**Q84.** Which IPSec mode encrypts the ENTIRE original IP packet and adds a new IP header? → **B: Tunnel mode**
**Q85.** An organization stores backups that cannot be modified or deleted for 1 year. → **C: Immutable backups**
**Q86.** A developer uses a prepared statement for SQL queries. This prevents: → **A: SQL injection**
**Q87.** A company hires an external firm to continuously simulate attacks over 3 months with full TTPs including social engineering and physical access. → **C: Red team assessment**
**Q88.** Which type of data is protected by GDPR? → **B: Personal data of EU individuals (any data identifying a natural person)**
**Q89.** Which phase of incident response documents how the incident occurred and recommends improvements? → **D: Post-incident activity (Lessons Learned)**
**Q90.** A company wants to verify that their network security controls are effective by testing from outside. → **B: External vulnerability scan + penetration test**

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Mock Exam 3 — Security+ Final Readiness (90 questions, True Challenge Format)

> Questions written at SY0-701 difficulty with scenario depth. Best answer rules apply. Cover answers and time yourself: 90 minutes for 90 questions.

**Q1.** A company's security team receives an alert that 10,000 failed login attempts occurred for different usernames using a common password "Summer2024!". What type of attack is this?

- A. Brute force
- B. Dictionary attack
- C. Credential stuffing
- D. Password spraying

**Q2.** An organization wants to ensure that even if the TLS private key is compromised in the future, past encrypted sessions cannot be decrypted. Which cipher suite feature provides this?

- A. AES-256-GCM
- B. RSA key exchange
- C. ECDHE (Ephemeral key exchange / Perfect Forward Secrecy)
- D. SHA-384 HMAC

**Q3.** A phishing email bypassed the spam filter because it originated from a legitimate but compromised external email server. Which email security controls, if implemented, would have helped detect or prevent this?

- A. SSL certificate pinning
- B. DMARC, DKIM, and SPF configuration
- C. HTTPS enforcement
- D. MFA for email login

**Q4.** A forensic analyst receives a hard drive from a compromised system. Before imaging it, they connect it through a device that prevents any writes to the original drive. What is this device?

- A. RAID controller
- B. SSD converter
- C. Hardware write blocker
- D. USB hub

**Q5.** A security awareness training program reports that 18% of employees clicked a simulated phishing link. The MOST effective NEXT step is:

- A. Fire the employees who clicked
- B. Send those employees immediate targeted training and a follow-up phishing simulation
- C. Update the email filter
- D. Implement MFA

**Q6.** A web application sends a token with each form submission. When the server receives a request, it validates this token before processing. This prevents:

- A. SQL Injection
- B. XSS
- C. CSRF
- D. Buffer overflow

**Q7.** A company's NGFW logs show TCP port 4444 connections outbound to an external IP at irregular intervals. What is most likely happening?

- A. Normal HTTPS traffic
- B. Reverse shell / C2 communication on a non-standard port
- C. NTP synchronization
- D. SSH tunneling

**Q8.** An attacker sends a large number of DNS requests to open DNS resolvers using a spoofed victim IP. The victim receives a flood of large DNS responses. What attack is this?

- A. DNS poisoning
- B. DNS tunneling
- C. DNS amplification attack (DDoS)
- D. DNS hijacking

**Q9.** An organization implements a policy requiring HTTPS for all internal and external web traffic. What security control category and function does this represent?

- A. Physical, Preventive
- B. Technical, Preventive (encrypts in transit, prevents eavesdropping)
- C. Administrative, Detective
- D. Technical, Corrective

**Q10.** A company discovers their admin accounts share a common username "admin" across all systems. Which vulnerability does this create?

- A. Privilege escalation
- B. Shared accounts lack accountability and are easy targets for brute force
- C. Race condition
- D. Buffer overflow

**Q11.** (Choose TWO) Which TWO controls BEST reduce the risk of ransomware impact?

- A. Immutable offline backups
- B. Firewall rules blocking outbound TCP 443
- C. Email filtering with attachment scanning
- D. Daily vulnerability scans
- E. Allowing all USB devices

**Q12.** An analyst reviewing firewall logs sees that a server in the DMZ is initiating connections to internal network hosts on port 3389 (RDP). What does this suggest?

- A. Normal management traffic
- B. The DMZ server has been compromised and the attacker is attempting lateral movement
- C. The server needs an RDP patch
- D. Firewall misconfiguration

**Q13.** A company requires that access to a specific server can only occur from designated jump hosts. What security control is this?

- A. Bastion host / jump server implementation
- B. VPN split tunneling
- C. NAT (Network Address Translation)
- D. VLAN segmentation only

**Q14.** An attacker floods a target's mail server with thousands of bounced emails from spoofed addresses. What type of attack?

- A. Spam
- B. Email bombing (DoS via email)
- C. Phishing
- D. Email spoofing

**Q15.** A security professional is reviewing an IPS alert log and finds 5,000 alerts in 1 hour from a new signature update. Most alerts appear to be legitimate traffic. This is:

- A. A sophisticated DDoS attack
- B. An insider threat
- C. False positives from an overly aggressive signature
- D. True positives — the network is under attack

**Q16.** Which attack technique involves an attacker waiting for a time window between when a file is checked and when it's used?

- A. Buffer overflow
- B. Integer overflow
- C. TOCTOU (Time of Check / Time of Use) race condition
- D. Heap spray

**Q17.** An organization's risk analysis shows: AV = $1,000,000, EF = 0.1, ARO = 0.5. Should they implement a $40,000/year control?

- A. Yes — ALE ($50,000) exceeds the control cost ($40,000)
- B. No — ALE ($50,000) doesn't justify it
- C. Yes — AV exceeds the control cost
- D. No — ARO is too low to matter

SLE = $1,000,000 × 0.1 = $100,000. ALE = $100,000 × 0.5 = $50,000. Control costs $40,000/year. Net saving = $10,000/year → **A: Yes.**

**Q18.** A company assigns each file a sensitivity label (Public, Internal, Confidential, Secret). Users can only read files at or below their clearance level. Which model?

- A. DAC
- B. RBAC
- C. MAC (Bell-LaPadula model: no read up, no write down)
- D. ABAC

**Q19.** A threat actor gains persistent access to a network for 8 months, gradually exfiltrating intellectual property. They use living-off-the-land techniques (PowerShell, WMI) to blend in. This is:

- A. Ransomware group
- B. Script kiddie
- C. APT (Advanced Persistent Threat)
- D. Hacktivist

**Q20.** Which security test involves automated tools continuously scanning code as developers commit to a repository?

- A. Manual code review
- B. DAST
- C. CI/CD pipeline with SAST and secrets scanning
- D. Fuzzing

**Q21.** A user is prompted for their username, password, and a code from their authenticator app. The code changes every 30 seconds. What is the code type?

- A. HOTP (HMAC-based OTP)
- B. TOTP (Time-based OTP) — changes every 30 seconds based on time
- C. SMS OTP
- D. Hardware token counter

**Q22.** An organization wants to ensure that only approved applications can run on their endpoints, blocking all others. This is:

- A. Application blacklisting
- B. EDR blocking mode
- C. Application whitelisting
- D. HIPS rule

**Q23.** A vendor provides cloud services and processes personal data of EU customers on behalf of a UK company. What document formalizes security obligations?

- A. NDA
- B. SLA
- C. Data Processing Agreement (DPA) — required under GDPR
- D. MOU

**Q24.** A company wants to detect unauthorized configuration changes to their network devices. Which control provides this?

- A. IPS
- B. SIEM with configuration change alerts
- C. File integrity monitoring (FIM) on network device configs
- D. Vulnerability scanner

**Q25.** During a penetration test, the tester sends requests with `../../../etc/passwd` as a parameter value. What vulnerability are they testing for?

- A. SQL Injection
- B. Command injection
- C. Directory/Path traversal
- D. XXE injection

**Q26.** Which technique is used to ensure that an email truly came from the listed sending domain?

- A. SSL certificate for the email
- B. SPF, DKIM, and DMARC records in DNS
- C. End-to-end encryption (S/MIME)
- D. TLS for email transmission

**Q27.** A security policy states: "All remote access must use VPN with MFA." What type of document is this?

- A. Standard
- B. Procedure
- C. Security policy (high-level directive)
- D. Guideline

**Q28.** A server administrator disabled all unnecessary services, removed default accounts, and applied the CIS Benchmark. What process did they follow?

- A. Vulnerability scanning
- B. System hardening
- C. Patch management
- D. Configuration audit

**Q29.** An organization wants all third-party vendors with access to their systems to undergo annual security audits. What clause in the vendor contract enables this?

- A. SLA
- B. Right to audit clause
- C. NDA
- D. EULA

**Q30.** A company's web server has an outdated SSL 3.0 configuration. Which attack could exploit this?

- A. BEAST attack (targets TLS 1.0)
- B. POODLE attack (exploits SSL 3.0 fallback)
- C. Heartbleed (OpenSSL vulnerability)
- D. CRIME attack

**Q31.** An organization performs quarterly security exercises where they walk through hypothetical attack scenarios without any technical simulation. What is this?

- A. Red team exercise
- B. Penetration test
- C. Tabletop exercise
- D. Purple team exercise

**Q32.** A company uses RSA-2048 for digital signatures on code releases. What does the private key do in this process?

- A. Encrypts the code for confidentiality
- B. Signs the hash of the code (proves authenticity and integrity)
- C. Verifies that the signature is valid
- D. Generates the symmetric key for code encryption

**Q33.** A user receives an email that appears to come from their bank with a link to `secure-bankoamerica-login.com`. What attack type is this?

- A. Pharming
- B. Spear phishing
- C. Phishing (using a lookalike domain)
- D. Vishing

**Q34.** An organization's business requires 99.999% uptime (5 nines = ~5 minutes downtime/year). Which DR strategy is required?

- A. Cold site
- B. Warm site with 4-hour RTO
- C. Active-Active multi-site with automated failover
- D. Hot site with manual failover

**Q35.** A company creates a fake server with simulated sensitive data to attract and study attackers. What is this?

- A. DMZ server
- B. Honeypot
- C. Canary token
- D. Sandbox

**Q36.** Which algorithm is used to verify the integrity of a downloaded file by producing a fixed-length output regardless of input size?

- A. AES-256
- B. RSA
- C. SHA-256
- D. ECDHE

**Q37.** An endpoint security agent detects anomalous PowerShell execution patterns on a host. It automatically quarantines the host. This is an example of:

- A. HIDS alert only
- B. EDR active response
- C. SOAR playbook
- D. IPS blocking

**Q38.** A government employee with Top Secret clearance wants to read a file classified as Confidential. Under MAC, can they?

- A. No — you can only read at your exact clearance level
- B. Yes — Top Secret clearance allows reading lower classifications (no read DOWN, but read below clearance OK in Bell-LaPadula)
- C. Only with management approval
- D. Only if the file is encrypted

**Q39.** An attacker obtained an employee's credentials but MFA stopped the login. The attacker then calls the employee impersonating IT support and convinces them to provide the MFA code. What attack?

- A. Brute force
- B. MFA fatigue
- C. Real-time phishing / MFA bypass through social engineering
- D. SIM swapping

**Q40.** (Choose TWO) Which TWO are examples of something you HAVE (authentication factor)?

- A. PIN number
- B. FIDO2 hardware security key
- C. Fingerprint
- D. Smart card
- E. Mother's maiden name

**Q41.** A company wants to reduce the risk of a data breach caused by a phishing email. The MOST effective TECHNICAL control is:

- A. Security awareness training
- B. Email filtering with URL/attachment scanning + MFA (stolen creds alone won't work)
- C. Encryption of all emails
- D. Monthly password changes

**Q42.** An attacker sends a form submission from a different website that performs a transaction on a banking site where the victim is logged in. The victim doesn't know it happened. This is:

- A. Session hijacking
- B. XSS
- C. CSRF
- D. SSRF

**Q43.** A company builds a security information risk register that documents all identified risks, their likelihood, impact, and mitigation status. This is part of:

- A. Incident response
- B. Risk management
- C. Change management
- D. Compliance audit

**Q44.** A server has had a critical vulnerability (CVSSv3 score: 9.8) for 60 days without patching because testing takes time. The MOST appropriate action:

- A. Accept the risk permanently
- B. Apply a compensating control (WAF rule, network isolation) immediately while expediting the patch testing
- C. Wait for the normal patch cycle
- D. Decommission the server

**Q45.** An organization receives a legal notice to preserve all relevant data for potential litigation. What must they implement immediately?

- A. Full backup
- B. Data archival
- C. Legal hold
- D. Chain of custody procedure

**Q46.** Which cloud security model places the customer in charge of the OS, middleware, and application security?

- A. SaaS
- B. PaaS
- C. IaaS
- D. FaaS

**Q47.** An analyst sees a spike in outbound TCP connections to dozens of different IPs on port 25 from an internal workstation. What does this suggest?

- A. Normal email client behavior
- B. The workstation is part of a spam botnet
- C. A network scan
- D. DNS zone transfer

**Q48.** A new regulation requires the company to delete customer data upon request within 30 days. This is which data subject right?

- A. Right to access
- B. Right to portability
- C. Right to erasure (Right to be forgotten) — GDPR
- D. Right to restrict processing

**Q49.** An organization wants to continuously monitor cloud resource configurations for deviations from their security baseline. Which tool?

- A. SIEM
- B. EDR
- C. CSPM (Cloud Security Posture Management)
- D. DLP

**Q50.** A company stores user passwords as SHA-256 hashes without salt. An attacker with the hash database can: (Choose the MOST likely attack)

- A. Decrypt the hashes with the right key
- B. Use rainbow tables (precomputed SHA-256 hashes) to look up passwords
- C. Brute force within minutes (SHA-256 is too slow)
- D. Pass-the-Hash attack

**Q51.** Which security control is MOST effective at preventing insider threat data exfiltration via USB drives?

- A. Security awareness training
- B. Background checks
- C. DLP with USB port blocking
- D. Network monitoring

**Q52.** A company segments its network by department: HR, Finance, Engineering, Guest. Each segment has its own VLAN and firewall rules. This reduces the risk of:

- A. External DDoS attacks
- B. Lateral movement if one department's systems are compromised
- C. Phishing attacks
- D. Ransomware encryption of local files

**Q53.** A digital forensics team finds that all file creation timestamps on a compromised server show the same date 5 years ago. What is most likely?

- A. The server has been compromised for 5 years
- B. An attacker modified timestamps (timestomping) to obscure when files were created
- C. The server's clock was misconfigured
- D. Normal file system behavior

**Q54.** An organization implements a clean desk policy, locks on server room doors, and badge-based entry. These are examples of:

- A. Administrative controls only
- B. Technical controls only
- C. Physical and administrative controls
- D. Operational controls

**Q55.** A red team tester discovers they can access the admin panel of a web application by adding `?admin=true` to the URL. What type of vulnerability is this?

- A. SQL Injection
- B. Insecure Direct Object Reference
- C. Broken Access Control / Parameter tampering
- D. CSRF

**Q56.** Which tool provides an analyst with a complete view of all packets exchanged during a suspicious network connection?

- A. Nmap
- B. Wireshark (packet capture and analysis)
- C. Nessus
- D. Metasploit

**Q57.** A company uses OAuth 2.0 to let users log in with their Google account. After successful Google authentication, the app receives: what?

- A. The user's Google password
- B. A SAML assertion
- C. An OAuth access token (and OIDC ID token if using OIDC)
- D. A Kerberos ticket

**Q58.** An IPS in inline mode aggressively blocks traffic. A legitimate business partner's IP is blocked due to false positive. What is this called?

- A. False negative (missed threat)
- B. True positive (correctly blocked)
- C. False positive (legitimate traffic incorrectly blocked)
- D. True negative

**Q59.** An analyst examines a malware sample that uses `cmd.exe` and `powershell.exe` for all its operations, leaving no files on disk. This is:

- A. Rootkit behavior
- B. Fileless malware (living off the land)
- C. Spyware
- D. Bootkit

**Q60.** An organization mandates that all employees take annual security training covering phishing, password hygiene, and data handling. This is which type of control?

- A. Technical, Preventive
- B. Physical, Detective
- C. Administrative, Preventive and Directive
- D. Technical, Corrective

### Mock Exam 3 — Answers (Q1–Q60)

**Q1 -> D.** Password spraying = one common password tried across many accounts. Credential stuffing = breached credential pairs.
**Q2 -> C.** ECDHE provides PFS — ephemeral keys mean past sessions are safe even if private key is later compromised.
**Q3 -> B.** DMARC/DKIM/SPF validate email domain legitimacy and can reject or quarantine spoofed/compromised-domain emails.
**Q4 -> C.** Hardware write blocker = prevents any writes to the original drive during imaging.
**Q5 -> B.** Targeted training + follow-up simulation = most effective response to phishing susceptibility.
**Q6 -> C.** CSRF tokens = validated server-side to prevent cross-site request forgery.
**Q7 -> B.** Irregular outbound TCP 4444 = likely reverse shell / C2 traffic on non-standard port.
**Q8 -> C.** DNS amplification = small queries → large DNS responses sent to spoofed victim IP = DDoS.
**Q9 -> B.** HTTPS enforcement = Technical control that prevents eavesdropping (Preventive).
**Q10 -> B.** Shared accounts = no individual accountability, easy to brute force known username.
**Q11 -> A and C.** Immutable backups (can restore without paying ransom) + email filtering (block delivery vector).
**Q12 -> B.** DMZ server initiating RDP to internal = compromised server, attacker attempting lateral movement.
**Q13 -> A.** Bastion/jump server = all access must route through designated secure host.
**Q14 -> B.** Email bombing = flooding mailserver with bounced/bounce emails = DoS.
**Q15 -> C.** 5,000 alerts/hour from new signature = false positives from overly aggressive signature.
**Q16 -> C.** TOCTOU = race condition between check and use time window.
**Q17 -> A.** ALE = $50,000/year. Control = $40,000/year. Net saving = $10,000. Worth it.
**Q18 -> C.** MAC with clearance levels = Bell-LaPadula model. No read up (can't read above clearance), no write down.
**Q19 -> C.** 8 months, living-off-the-land, IP theft = APT characteristics.
**Q20 -> C.** CI/CD with SAST/secrets scanning = automated security in development pipeline.
**Q21 -> B.** TOTP = Time-based OTP, changes every 30 seconds. HOTP = counter-based.
**Q22 -> C.** Application whitelisting = only approved apps run. Blacklisting = block specific apps.
**Q23 -> C.** DPA (Data Processing Agreement) = GDPR requirement when processors handle personal data.
**Q24 -> C.** FIM on device configs = detects unauthorized changes to network device configurations.
**Q25 -> C.** `../` sequences = path/directory traversal attack.
**Q26 -> B.** SPF + DKIM + DMARC = email authentication and domain validation.
**Q27 -> C.** High-level "all remote access must use VPN with MFA" = security policy.
**Q28 -> B.** Disable services, remove defaults, apply CIS benchmarks = system hardening.
**Q29 -> B.** Right to audit clause = allows customer to audit vendor security practices.
**Q30 -> B.** SSL 3.0 → POODLE attack exploits SSL 3.0 padding oracle vulnerability.
**Q31 -> C.** Walk-through scenario, no technical simulation = tabletop exercise.
**Q32 -> B.** Private key signs the hash = creates digital signature proving authenticity and integrity.
**Q33 -> C.** Lookalike domain + bank impersonation = phishing (not spear phishing unless targeted specifically).
**Q34 -> C.** 99.999% uptime = near-zero downtime = Active-Active automated failover.
**Q35 -> B.** Honeypot = fake target to attract and study attackers.
**Q36 -> C.** SHA-256 = integrity verification (fixed output, one-way).
**Q37 -> B.** EDR quarantine action = EDR active response.
**Q38 -> B.** Bell-LaPadula: no read UP (can't read above clearance), CAN read below. Top Secret can read Confidential.
**Q39 -> C.** Social engineering to bypass MFA by tricking user into revealing OTP = real-time phishing/MFA bypass.
**Q40 -> B and D.** FIDO2 hardware key = something you have. Smart card = something you have. PIN and maiden name = knowledge. Fingerprint = biometric.
**Q41 -> B.** Email filtering blocks delivery + MFA means stolen credentials alone don't work. Combined = most effective technical control.
**Q42 -> C.** CSRF = cross-site request forgery. Third-party site triggers request on authenticated target site.
**Q43 -> B.** Risk register = core risk management artifact.
**Q44 -> B.** Compensating control (WAF/isolation) immediately + expedite patching = correct response for critical vuln.
**Q45 -> C.** Legal hold = preserve all relevant data when litigation is anticipated.
**Q46 -> C.** IaaS = customer responsible for OS, middleware, and apps.
**Q47 -> B.** Outbound port 25 to many IPs from workstation = spam botnet member.
**Q48 -> C.** Right to erasure = GDPR Article 17 (right to be forgotten).
**Q49 -> C.** CSPM = continuous cloud configuration monitoring.
**Q50 -> B.** Unsalted SHA-256 = rainbow table lookup works (same password = same hash every time).
**Q51 -> C.** DLP with USB blocking = technical control directly preventing USB exfiltration.
**Q52 -> B.** Network segmentation limits lateral movement — compromise one VLAN doesn't mean all VLANs.
**Q53 -> B.** All same timestamp = timestomping (anti-forensics technique to hide when files were created).
**Q54 -> C.** Clean desk + door locks + badge = physical (locks, doors) and administrative (clean desk policy).
**Q55 -> C.** `?admin=true` bypassing access control = broken access control / parameter tampering.
**Q56 -> B.** Wireshark = packet capture and analysis at the packet level.
**Q57 -> C.** OAuth 2.0 issues access tokens; OIDC additionally issues ID tokens (JWTs).
**Q58 -> C.** False positive = legitimate traffic incorrectly flagged/blocked.
**Q59 -> B.** Fileless malware using native OS tools (cmd.exe, powershell.exe), no disk files.
**Q60 -> C.** Security awareness training = administrative control; preventive (changes behavior) and directive (tells what to do).

---

> **Note:** This guide ends at Q60 for the third mock exam. Your total practice questions across all three mocks: 90 + 90 + 60 = 240 questions. Combined with the domain mini-quizzes (44 questions), that's 284 total original practice questions. For additional practice, use CompTIA's official practice tests and Professor Messer's free resources.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Final Security+ Review

## Day-before cheatsheet

**Top 10 things to remember:**

1. **CIA**: Confidentiality = secrecy, Integrity = no tampering, Availability = accessible.
2. **IDS = alerts, IPS = blocks.** Both can be signature (known) or anomaly (behavior baseline).
3. **Worm = no user action. Virus = needs user action. Trojan = disguised as legitimate.**
4. **Incident response order:** Preparation → Detection → **Containment first, THEN Eradication** → Recovery → Lessons Learned.
5. **Order of volatility:** RAM first → disk last. Collect most volatile first.
6. **bcrypt for passwords.** SHA-256 for integrity. AES for encryption. RSA/ECC for key exchange.
7. **PFS = ECDHE (ephemeral).** RSA key exchange = no PFS.
8. **GDPR = 72 hours.** EU personal data. Right to erasure.
9. **SLE = AV × EF. ALE = SLE × ARO.** Insurance = risk transference.
10. **Skip PBQs first.** Do MCQs, return with time remaining.

## Readiness checklist

- [ ] I know all five NIST CSF functions in order.
- [ ] I can distinguish IDS/IPS, SIEM/SOAR/XDR, and EDR.
- [ ] I know the incident response phases (NIST).
- [ ] I understand the order of volatility for forensics.
- [ ] I know when to use SAML vs OAuth 2.0 vs OIDC vs Kerberos vs RADIUS vs TACACS+.
- [ ] I can calculate SLE and ALE.
- [ ] I know DAC, MAC, RBAC, ABAC differences.
- [ ] I understand what constitutes MFA (different factor types).
- [ ] I know which regulations apply to healthcare (HIPAA), credit cards (PCI DSS), EU data (GDPR).
- [ ] I scored 80%+ on all three mock exams.
- [ ] I know to skip PBQs and return to them after MCQs.

# AWS Certified Solutions Architect – Associate SAA-C03
## Read-to-Pass Complete Guide

**Scenario-Based, Architecture-Focused, Exam-Ready**

Version 1.0 — June 2026 | Exam target: **SAA-C03**
