# SAA-C03 Keyword Decoder

| Keyword in question | Think of |
|---|---|
| "stateful firewall, instance level" | Security group |
| "stateless firewall, subnet level, can deny" | NACL |
| "private S3 access, no internet, free" | S3 Gateway Endpoint |
| "private access to other AWS services (not S3/DynamoDB)" | Interface Endpoint (PrivateLink) |
| "many VPCs connected, transitive routing" | Transit Gateway |
| "two VPCs private, non-transitive" | VPC Peering |
| "dedicated private line to AWS" | Direct Connect |
| "encrypted tunnel over internet to VPC" | Site-to-Site VPN |
| "private + encrypted + dedicated" | VPN over Direct Connect |
| "auto failover for RDS" | RDS Multi-AZ |
| "scale RDS reads" | Read Replicas |
| "highest performance AWS relational DB" | Aurora |
| "cross-Region DB replication, <1s, failover <1 min" | Aurora Global Database |
| "serverless relational DB" | Aurora Serverless v2 |
| "NoSQL, millisecond, serverless, key-value" | DynamoDB |
| "microsecond DynamoDB reads" | DAX |
| "DynamoDB real-time changes trigger Lambda" | DynamoDB Streams |
| "data warehouse, petabytes, SQL analytics" | Redshift |
| "query S3 from Redshift without loading" | Redshift Spectrum |
| "in-memory cache, complex data types, persistence, HA" | ElastiCache Redis |
| "simple cache, no persistence, multi-threaded" | ElastiCache Memcached |
| "serverless functions, event-driven" | Lambda |
| "long-running containers, no servers" | ECS/EKS with Fargate |
| "path-based or host-based routing" | ALB |
| "static IP load balancer" | NLB |
| "CDN, edge caching" | CloudFront |
| "restrict S3 to CloudFront only" | OAC (Origin Access Control) |
| "signed URL for single file, time-limited" | CloudFront Signed URL |
| "signed cookie for multiple files" | CloudFront Signed Cookie |
| "global static IPs for application" | Global Accelerator |
| "route 80%/20% traffic" | Route 53 Weighted |
| "failover DNS" | Route 53 Failover |
| "route by country" | Route 53 Geolocation |
| "route to lowest latency Region" | Route 53 Latency |
| "decouple services, buffer messages" | SQS |
| "fan-out to multiple subscribers" | SNS |
| "event-driven between AWS services" | EventBridge |
| "multi-step workflow, orchestration" | Step Functions |
| "fan-out + buffer" | SNS → multiple SQS queues |
| "rotate DB password automatically" | Secrets Manager |
| "store config values, non-sensitive" | Parameter Store (SSM) |
| "detect threats from logs, ML" | GuardDuty |
| "scan EC2/containers for vulnerabilities" | Inspector |
| "find PII in S3" | Macie |
| "central security dashboard" | Security Hub |
| "SSL/TLS certs, free" | ACM |
| "compliance reports SOC, PCI" | Artifact |
| "hardware HSM, you own keys entirely" | CloudHSM |
| "interruptible batch jobs, cheapest" | Spot Instances |
| "steady workload, 1-3 year commit" | Reserved Instances or Savings Plans |
| "flexible commit across EC2+Lambda" | Compute Savings Plans |
| "right-sizing ML recommendations" | Compute Optimizer |
| "on-premises data to AWS S3/EFS, automated" | DataSync |
| "large physical data shipment" | Snow Family |
| "migrate DB to RDS, minimal downtime" | DMS |
| "hybrid on-prem file shares to S3" | Storage Gateway File Gateway |
| "virtual tape backup" | Storage Gateway Tape Gateway |
| "setup multi-account governance" | Control Tower |
| "permission guardrails across accounts" | SCPs in Organizations |
| "share resources across accounts" | RAM |
| "temporary credentials for third-party audit" | IAM role with trust policy |
| "mobile users sign in, authenticate" | Cognito User Pools |
| "mobile users access AWS directly" | Cognito Identity Pools |
| "single sign-on across accounts" | IAM Identity Center |

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Common SAA-C03 Exam Traps

1. **VPC peering is NOT transitive.** A↔B and B↔C does not mean A can reach C. Use Transit Gateway.
2. **NAT Gateway is NOT free.** Routing S3/DynamoDB through NAT costs money. Use Gateway Endpoints (free) instead.
3. **RDS Multi-AZ standby is NOT readable.** Only Read Replicas are readable for scaling reads.
4. **Direct Connect is NOT encrypted by default.** Add VPN over DX for encryption.
5. **S3 CRR only replicates NEW objects.** Existing objects need S3 Batch Operations.
6. **CloudFront doesn't have static IPs.** Use Global Accelerator for static IPs.
7. **ALB doesn't support static IPs.** Use NLB for static IP / Elastic IP.
8. **Spot Instances give 2-minute notice, NOT 5 minutes or immediate.**
9. **Standard RI cannot change instance family.** Use Convertible RI or Savings Plan for flexibility.
10. **DynamoDB On-Demand is more expensive per request** than provisioned, but never wastes idle capacity.
11. **SQS FIFO has lower throughput** (3,000 msg/sec) than Standard. Don't use FIFO if you just need high throughput.
12. **Lambda max execution time is 15 minutes.** For longer tasks, use ECS/Fargate or Step Functions.
13. **EBS volumes are AZ-locked.** To move to another AZ, create a snapshot, then restore in the target AZ.
14. **CloudFront distributions take up to 15 minutes to deploy changes.** Cache invalidation costs money.
15. **Route 53 Multivalue Answer is NOT a replacement for ELB** — it just returns multiple IPs from DNS.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Memory Cheatsheets

## SAA-C03 One-Page Service Cheat Sheet

**Choose ALB when:** path/host-based routing, HTTP/2, WebSocket, Lambda target, WAF integration.
**Choose NLB when:** static IP needed, ultra-low latency TCP/UDP, client IP preservation.
**Choose GWLB when:** routing traffic through network appliances (firewall, IDS).

**Choose S3 when:** object storage, static website, backups, data lake, unlimited scale.
**Choose EBS when:** persistent block storage for one EC2 instance, database volumes.
**Choose EFS when:** shared file storage for multiple Linux instances.
**Choose FSx for Windows when:** SMB share for Windows instances, Active Directory integration.
**Choose FSx for Lustre when:** HPC, ML training, high-throughput parallel file system.

**Choose RDS when:** relational SQL, managed, up to 5 read replicas, familiar engines.
**Choose Aurora when:** highest-performance relational, Aurora-specific features, serverless option, global.
**Choose DynamoDB when:** NoSQL, serverless, any scale, key-value, document.
**Choose Redshift when:** data warehouse, analytical SQL queries, petabyte scale.
**Choose ElastiCache Redis when:** caching + persistence + complex types + HA.
**Choose ElastiCache Memcached when:** simple in-memory caching, multi-threaded, no persistence.

**Choose SQS when:** decoupling, buffering, asynchronous processing, retry logic.
**Choose SNS when:** fan-out, push notifications, multiple subscriber types.
**Choose EventBridge when:** event-driven routing between AWS services or SaaS.
**Choose Step Functions when:** orchestrating multi-step workflows with error handling.

## Last-Day SAA-C03 Review

**10 most missed concepts on SAA-C03:**

1. **VPC peering = non-transitive.** TGW = transitive hub.
2. **NLB for static IP, ALB for content routing** — never swap them.
3. **RDS Multi-AZ = HA (auto failover), Read Replicas = read performance scaling** — not the same.
4. **Spot = interruptible (2-min notice), cheapest.** Never for stateful or critical workloads.
5. **S3 Gateway Endpoint (free) vs Interface Endpoint (paid)** — S3/DynamoDB always use Gateway.
6. **Aurora Global Database = cross-region, <1s replication, <1min failover.**
7. **CloudFront = caching CDN. Global Accelerator = network routing, static IPs, non-HTTP.**
8. **DAX = microsecond DynamoDB reads.** ElastiCache = general caching in front of any DB.
9. **Secrets Manager = auto-rotation. Parameter Store = config values, cheaper/free.**
10. **Compute Savings Plans = most flexible (EC2 + Lambda + Fargate). EC2 Instance SP = family-specific.**

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Practice Questions

> SAA-C03 questions are scenario-based. Read the last sentence first (it tells you what's being asked), eliminate obviously wrong options, then pick the BEST fit for the stated constraint (cost, performance, resilience, security, operational overhead).
>
> This book contains three full 65-question mock exams plus a 30-question rapid-fire warm-up. All questions are original.

## Quick-Fire Warm-Up (30 questions)

**Q1.** A company wants to run event-driven code only when an image is uploaded to S3. No servers should be managed. Which service?

- A. EC2 Auto Scaling
- B. AWS Lambda
- C. ECS on EC2
- D. AWS Elastic Beanstalk

**Q2.** An application stores session data that must be shared across multiple EC2 instances behind an ALB. The data must persist if the ElastiCache node restarts. Which caching solution?

- A. ElastiCache for Memcached
- B. ElastiCache for Redis with Multi-AZ
- C. EC2 instance store
- D. DynamoDB with DAX

**Q3.** A company needs to block traffic from specific countries to their API Gateway. Which service provides this?

- A. Security groups
- B. NACLs
- C. AWS WAF with geo-match rules
- D. Route 53 failover routing

**Q4.** A solutions architect needs to migrate 10 TB of data from an on-premises database to Amazon RDS with minimal downtime. Which service?

- A. AWS Snowball
- B. AWS Database Migration Service (DMS)
- C. AWS DataSync
- D. AWS Transfer Family

**Q5.** A company runs a microservices application on Amazon ECS. They want the LEAST operational overhead (no cluster management). Which launch type?

- A. EC2 launch type
- B. Fargate launch type
- C. On-premises ECS
- D. Serverless on EC2

**Q6.** (Choose TWO) A company wants to improve the resilience of their web application. Which two actions help?

- A. Deploy EC2 instances in multiple AZs using Auto Scaling
- B. Use a single large EC2 instance with enhanced networking
- C. Place an Elastic Load Balancer in front of the Auto Scaling group
- D. Use Spot Instances exclusively
- E. Disable CloudWatch monitoring

**Q7.** Which S3 feature ensures that once an object is written, it cannot be overwritten or deleted by anyone, including root?

- A. S3 Versioning
- B. S3 MFA Delete
- C. S3 Object Lock in Compliance mode
- D. S3 Block Public Access

**Q8.** A company has an Aurora database cluster. They want to offload read traffic from the primary writer. What should they create?

- A. RDS Read Replica
- B. Aurora Read Replicas (up to 15)
- C. A second Aurora cluster
- D. Redshift Spectrum

**Q9.** A company needs to automatically transition S3 objects to cheaper storage after 30 days and delete them after 180 days. Which feature?

- A. S3 Intelligent-Tiering
- B. S3 Versioning
- C. S3 Lifecycle policies
- D. S3 CRR

**Q10.** A workload requires 50,000 IOPS for a database volume. Which EBS volume type?

- A. gp3
- B. gp2
- C. io2
- D. st1

**Q11.** An EC2 instance in a private subnet needs to download software updates from the internet. What should be deployed?

- A. Internet Gateway (IGW)
- B. NAT Gateway in a public subnet
- C. VPC endpoint
- D. AWS Direct Connect

**Q12.** A company wants to decouple a web front-end from a backend order processor. Orders must not be lost if the processor is temporarily down. Which service?

- A. Amazon SNS
- B. Amazon SQS
- C. AWS EventBridge
- D. AWS Step Functions

**Q13.** Which Route 53 routing policy should be used to implement a blue/green deployment (gradually shift traffic from old to new)?

- A. Failover
- B. Geolocation
- C. Weighted
- D. Multivalue

**Q14.** A company wants to stop paying for NAT Gateway data processing costs when EC2 instances access S3. What is the BEST solution?

- A. Use S3 Transfer Acceleration
- B. Use an S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint
- C. Move EC2 to a public subnet
- D. Use Direct Connect

**Q15.** A Lambda function needs to access an RDS database in a private subnet. The function also needs internet access for calling an external API. What must be configured?

- A. Attach an Elastic IP to the Lambda function
- B. Put Lambda in the VPC with a NAT Gateway for internet traffic
- C. Make RDS publicly accessible
- D. Lambda cannot access both VPC resources and the internet

**Q16.** (Choose TWO) Which two services can distribute incoming web traffic across EC2 instances while performing health checks?

- A. Amazon Route 53 with latency routing
- B. Application Load Balancer
- C. Network Load Balancer
- D. AWS Global Accelerator
- E. Amazon CloudFront

**Q17.** A company needs to share a file system between 50 Linux EC2 instances in different AZs. Which service?

- A. EBS with Multi-Attach
- B. Amazon EFS
- C. Amazon S3
- D. Amazon FSx for Windows

**Q18.** A security team needs to centrally aggregate security findings from GuardDuty, Inspector, and Macie across multiple accounts. Which service?

- A. AWS Config
- B. AWS Security Hub
- C. Amazon Macie
- D. AWS CloudTrail

**Q19.** A retail company expects a 10x traffic spike during Black Friday. They want to automatically scale EC2 based on CPU usage keeping it at 50%. Which Auto Scaling policy?

- A. Step Scaling
- B. Scheduled Scaling
- C. Target Tracking Scaling
- D. Predictive Scaling

**Q20.** A company wants to use AWS Direct Connect for low-latency connectivity to AWS and also needs the data to be encrypted in transit. What should they do?

- A. Direct Connect provides encryption automatically
- B. Configure a Site-to-Site VPN over the Direct Connect connection
- C. Use CloudFront in front of Direct Connect
- D. Enable HTTPS on Direct Connect

**Q21.** An application uses DynamoDB and experiences very high read traffic. Response time is too slow. What should the architect add?

- A. DynamoDB Global Tables
- B. DynamoDB On-Demand mode
- C. ElastiCache for Redis
- D. DynamoDB DAX

**Q22.** A company wants to give their data analysts the ability to run SQL queries on S3 data without setting up any infrastructure. Which service?

- A. Amazon Redshift
- B. Amazon Athena
- C. AWS Glue
- D. Amazon EMR

**Q23.** A company needs CloudFront to serve content from a private S3 bucket (not publicly accessible). What should they configure?

- A. Make the S3 bucket public
- B. Create a CloudFront Origin Access Control (OAC) and update the S3 bucket policy
- C. Use S3 website endpoint as the origin
- D. Enable S3 Transfer Acceleration

**Q24.** A company wants to run a Docker container for a one-time data processing job that will run for 4 hours. Which compute option is MOST appropriate?

- A. AWS Lambda (15-min max)
- B. AWS Fargate task
- C. EC2 Reserved Instance
- D. EC2 Spot (risk of interruption)

**Q25.** A company needs to ensure messages in SQS are processed in exactly the same order they arrive, with no duplicate processing. Which SQS feature?

- A. Standard Queue with long polling
- B. SQS FIFO Queue
- C. Standard Queue with visibility timeout
- D. SQS with Dead Letter Queue

**Q26.** A website is served from S3 and distributed globally via CloudFront. The company occasionally needs to remove an outdated object from all edge locations immediately. What should they use?

- A. S3 Lifecycle Policy
- B. CloudFront cache invalidation
- C. CloudFront TTL = 0
- D. Re-upload the object to S3

**Q27.** A company runs a steady-state production database on EC2 and RDS. Which purchasing strategy gives the MOST savings over 3 years?

- A. On-Demand for flexibility
- B. Spot Instances for both
- C. Reserved Instances (3-year all upfront) for both
- D. Compute Savings Plans

**Q28.** A company's application is deployed in us-east-1. To meet a compliance requirement, all data must remain within the US. An architect is considering a DR strategy. Which Region to use?

- A. ap-northeast-1 (Tokyo)
- B. eu-west-1 (Ireland)
- C. us-west-2 (Oregon)
- D. Any edge location

**Q29.** A company wants to run ML inference (not training) with GPU acceleration on EC2. Which instance family?

- A. R-family (memory optimized)
- B. C-family (compute optimized)
- C. G or Inf instances (accelerated computing)
- D. I-family (storage optimized)

**Q30.** (Choose TWO) A company wants to design a highly available architecture with no single point of failure. Which two actions are MOST important?

- A. Deploy EC2 instances in a single large AZ
- B. Use ELB to distribute traffic across multiple AZs
- C. Configure Auto Scaling across at least two AZs
- D. Use one large Reserved Instance
- E. Use Spot Instances only

### Warm-Up Answers

**Q1 -> B.** Lambda is triggered by S3 events, serverless.
**Q2 -> B.** Redis with Multi-AZ provides persistence + failover. Memcached has no persistence.
**Q3 -> C.** WAF geo-match rules block by country. Works with API Gateway.
**Q4 -> B.** DMS migrates running databases with minimal downtime. Snowball/DataSync are for file data, not live DBs.
**Q5 -> B.** Fargate = no cluster management. EC2 launch type = you manage the EC2.
**Q6 -> A and C.** Multi-AZ Auto Scaling + ELB = HA. Single large instance = SPOF. Spot = interruptible.
**Q7 -> C.** Compliance mode Object Lock = no one can delete, including root, until retention expires.
**Q8 -> B.** Aurora supports up to 15 read replicas. Not RDS replicas (those are for RDS, not Aurora).
**Q9 -> C.** S3 Lifecycle policies automate tiering and deletion. Intelligent-Tiering is continuous, not time-based.
**Q10 -> C.** io2 supports up to 256,000 IOPS. gp3 maxes at 16,000.
**Q11 -> B.** NAT Gateway in a public subnet allows private subnet instances to reach the internet outbound.
**Q12 -> B.** SQS buffers messages — they're not lost if the consumer is down. SNS pushes instantly and doesn't store.
**Q13 -> C.** Weighted routing splits % of traffic. 90/10 → 80/20 → 0/100 = gradual blue/green.
**Q14 -> B.** S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint routes S3 traffic within AWS — no NAT Gateway charges.
**Q15 -> B.** Lambda in VPC + NAT Gateway for internet. Private subnets route internet traffic through NAT.
**Q16 -> B and C.** ALB and NLB both distribute traffic and perform health checks.
**Q17 -> B.** EFS = shared NFS file system for many Linux instances across AZs.
**Q18 -> B.** Security Hub aggregates findings from multiple security services.
**Q19 -> C.** Target Tracking keeps a specific metric (CPU at 50%) — simplest, most automatic.
**Q20 -> B.** Direct Connect is private but NOT encrypted. VPN over DX adds encryption.
**Q21 -> D.** DAX is the in-memory cache specifically for DynamoDB with microsecond reads.
**Q22 -> B.** Athena = serverless SQL on S3, no infrastructure needed.
**Q23 -> B.** OAC restricts S3 access to CloudFront only. Update bucket policy to allow the OAC.
**Q24 -> B.** Fargate task = container, 4 hours fine (no Lambda 15-min limit). Spot is cheap but risky for important jobs.
**Q25 -> B.** SQS FIFO = exactly-once, ordered processing.
**Q26 -> B.** CloudFront cache invalidation removes objects from edge immediately (costs per path).
**Q27 -> C.** 3-year all-upfront RIs = highest discount for steady production workloads.
**Q28 -> C.** us-west-2 keeps data within the US for compliance.
**Q29 -> C.** G (GPU) or Inf (AWS Inferentia) instances for ML inference with acceleration.
**Q30 -> B and C.** ELB across AZs + Auto Scaling across AZs = no single point of failure.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Full Mock Exam 1 — SAA-C03 (65 questions, 130 minutes)

**Q1.** A company wants to migrate a MySQL database to AWS with minimal code changes. They need automated backups, Multi-AZ, and read replicas. Which is the BEST service?

- A. Amazon DynamoDB
- B. Amazon RDS for MySQL
- C. Amazon Redshift
- D. Amazon Aurora MySQL (same compatibility but not "minimal change")

**Q2.** A web application needs to cache database query results to improve performance. The cache must support complex data structures, persistence, and automatic failover. Which solution?

- A. ElastiCache for Memcached
- B. ElastiCache for Redis with Multi-AZ
- C. DynamoDB DAX
- D. Amazon S3 with caching

**Q3.** (Choose TWO) A company wants to reduce the cost of running EC2 instances for a steady-state workload that will run for 2 years. Which TWO options save the most money?

- A. Use Spot Instances
- B. Purchase 1-year Reserved Instances All Upfront
- C. Purchase 2-year Compute Savings Plans
- D. Use On-Demand Instances
- E. Use Dedicated Hosts

**Q4.** A startup wants to deploy a React web app with static HTML/JS/CSS. They want the LOWEST cost and HIGHEST availability. What is BEST?

- A. EC2 web servers in multiple AZs
- B. S3 static website with CloudFront distribution
- C. Elastic Beanstalk on EC2
- D. Lambda function with API Gateway

**Q5.** A company processes financial records that must never be deleted for 7 years due to regulatory requirements. Even administrators must not be able to delete them. Which S3 feature?

- A. S3 Versioning
- B. S3 Object Lock in Governance mode
- C. S3 Object Lock in Compliance mode
- D. S3 MFA Delete

**Q6.** An application running on EC2 needs to access DynamoDB and S3. The architect wants to avoid long-term access keys. What should they configure?

- A. Create IAM user, store access keys in /etc/environment
- B. Store access keys in AWS Secrets Manager and have the app retrieve them
- C. Attach an IAM role to the EC2 instance with the required permissions
- D. Use the root account access key

**Q7.** A company's on-premises application sends batch jobs to AWS. Jobs must be processed in the order submitted, with no duplicate processing. Which service?

- A. Amazon SQS Standard Queue
- B. Amazon SNS
- C. Amazon SQS FIFO Queue
- D. Amazon EventBridge

**Q8.** A company has an application in us-east-1. They want a DR site in us-west-2 with an RTO of less than 1 minute. Which DR strategy?

- A. Backup & Restore
- B. Pilot Light
- C. Warm Standby
- D. Active-Active Multi-Region

**Q9.** A company has a fleet of EC2 instances that occasionally need to run intensive workloads. They want instances to scale out when CPU > 70% and scale in when CPU < 30%. Which Auto Scaling policy?

- A. Scheduled Scaling
- B. Simple Scaling
- C. Step Scaling (different step sizes for different thresholds)
- D. Target Tracking (set CPU target at 50% as a balance)

**Q10.** A company needs low-latency connectivity from their data center to AWS for a consistent workload of 5 Gbps. They also need private connectivity. What should they use?

- A. Site-to-Site VPN
- B. AWS Direct Connect (1 Gbps or 10 Gbps connections)
- C. Amazon CloudFront
- D. AWS Global Accelerator

**Q11.** An application's Lambda functions are experiencing cold starts that cause unacceptable latency spikes. How can the architect eliminate cold starts for these critical functions?

- A. Increase Lambda memory
- B. Use Lambda Layers
- C. Enable Lambda Provisioned Concurrency
- D. Increase the Lambda timeout

**Q12.** A company runs a three-tier app: web (public), app (private), and database (private). The app tier needs to reach S3 without going through the internet. What should be deployed?

- A. NAT Gateway
- B. Internet Gateway in the private subnet
- C. S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint
- D. S3 Interface VPC Endpoint

**Q13.** A company's website runs on EC2 behind an ALB. They see a sudden spike of requests from malicious IP addresses attempting SQL injection. Which AWS service can automatically block these?

- A. AWS Shield Standard
- B. AWS WAF (with rules on ALB)
- C. Security groups
- D. NACLs

**Q14.** A media company stores 100 TB of video in S3. Most videos are accessed frequently for the first week, then rarely after. They want to minimize cost automatically. Which solution?

- A. S3 Standard for everything
- B. S3 Lifecycle policy: Standard for 7 days, then transition to S3 Standard-IA or Glacier

- A. Amazon RDS
- B. Amazon Athena
- C. Amazon Redshift
- D. Amazon DynamoDB

**Q16.** A DynamoDB table holds customer orders. The architect wants to trigger a Lambda function every time a new order is written to process it in near-real-time. Which feature?

**Q64.** A video streaming service wants to restrict access to their S3 videos so only paying subscribers can download them. What should the architect implement?

- A. Make the S3 bucket public
- B. Use signed URLs generated from CloudFront
- C. Use S3 bucket policies to list paying users
- D. Use SQS to gate access

**Q65.** A company is evaluating its AWS architecture. A trusted advisor check reveals EBS volumes that have not been attached to an EC2 instance for 30 days. What should the architect do to optimize cost?

- A. Resize the EBS volumes
- B. Create snapshots of the unattached volumes, then delete them (restore from snapshot if needed)
- C. Move them to S3
- D. Encrypt the volumes

### Mock Exam 1 — Answers & Explanations (Q1–Q32)

**Q1 -> B.** RDS for MySQL is managed, supports Multi-AZ, automated backups, and read replicas. Aurora is MySQL-compatible but the question says "minimal code changes" from MySQL — RDS MySQL is the most direct match.

**Q2 -> B.** ElastiCache Redis with Multi-AZ = complex data structures + persistence + failover. Memcached has none of these.

**Q3 -> B and C.** Reserved Instances and Savings Plans both give large discounts for commitment. Spot is interruptible (not for steady workloads). On-Demand has no discount. Dedicated Hosts are for compliance.

**Q4 -> B.** S3 static website + CloudFront = cheapest, globally available, no servers. EC2/Beanstalk cost more.

**Q5 -> C.** S3 Object Lock Compliance mode = immutable until retention period, even for root.

**Q6 -> C.** IAM role on EC2 instance = no long-term keys, best practice.

**Q7 -> C.** SQS FIFO = ordered + exactly-once processing.

**Q8 -> D.** RTO < 1 minute requires Active-Active Multi-Region (already running in both). Pilot Light/Warm Standby have longer RTO.

**Q9 -> C.** Step Scaling allows different step sizes for different alarm levels (e.g., CPU 70–80% add 1 instance, CPU 80–90% add 2). Target Tracking at 50% is also correct but C is specifically stated.

**Q10 -> B.** Direct Connect = private, dedicated, up to 10 Gbps or 100 Gbps connections.

**Q11 -> C.** Provisioned Concurrency keeps Lambda functions pre-initialized = no cold starts.

**Q12 -> C.** S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint = S3 access without internet, free. Interface Endpoint costs money and is not needed for S3.

**Q13 -> B.** WAF with rules on the ALB blocks SQL injection and malicious IPs.

**Q14 -> B.** Lifecycle policy gives explicit control: Standard 7 days → S3-IA or Glacier. Intelligent-Tiering also works (C is also acceptable) but B gives more explicit control.

**Q15 -> B.** Athena = serverless SQL on S3. No database setup needed.

**Q16 -> B.** DynamoDB Streams → Lambda is the standard pattern for real-time processing of DynamoDB changes.

**Q17 -> C.** FSx for Windows File Server = Windows SMB shares + Active Directory integration.

**Q18 -> C.** SCPs in Organizations prevent actions across member accounts (e.g., restrict to specific Regions).

**Q19 -> C.** SNS topic → 3 SQS queues (fan-out) → 3 Lambda functions = parallel processing, each service independently decoupled.

**Q20 -> C.** Separate AWS accounts per team + Organizations + consolidated billing = true isolation + one bill.

**Q21 -> C.** WAF rate-based rules throttle requests per IP. Shield is DDoS; SG/NACL are network rules.

**Q22 -> B.** gp3 is cheaper than gp2 with independently configurable IOPS and throughput. The correct answer for "best balance" going forward is gp3.

**Q23 -> C.** ElastiCache Redis as a session store = shared across all instances, scales independently, no code change needed beyond configuration.

**Q24 -> B.** CloudFront cache invalidation removes the old version from all edge locations immediately.

**Q25 -> B.** Cognito: User Pool federates Google login → Identity Pool exchanges the token for temporary AWS credentials to call S3.

**Q26 -> C.** Compute Savings Plans = most flexible (change instance type, family, Region, and covers Lambda/Fargate too).

**Q27 -> B.** Bucket policy denying `aws:SecureTransport = false` = HTTPS only. S3 Block Public Access doesn't affect HTTPS enforcement.

**Q28 -> B.** Lambda + API Gateway = scales to zero + scales to millions, pay per request. Perfect for spiky traffic.

**Q29 -> A.** gp3 allows independent IOPS provisioning (up to 16,000 IOPS regardless of volume size). 20,000 IOPS exceeds gp3 max — actually io2 is correct. **Q29 -> C (io2)** is correct for 20,000 IOPS since gp3 max is 16,000.

**Q30 -> B.** Site-to-Site VPN over Direct Connect = private + encrypted. Direct Connect alone is not encrypted.

**Q31 -> C.** Spot Instances with checkpointing = cheapest for long, fault-tolerant batch jobs. Lambda max 15 min doesn't fit 4-6 hours.

**Q32 -> B.** S3 Object Lock Compliance mode with 10-year retention. S3 Glacier Vault Lock also works but question mentions S3.

### Mock Exam 1 — Answers (Q33–Q65)

**Q33 -> B.** RDS Read Replicas handle read traffic. Multi-AZ standby is NOT readable.

**Q34 -> B.** S3 CRR replicates to a different Region. SRR stays in the same Region. Versioning is required (already configured).

**Q35 -> C.** Storage Gateway Tape Gateway = virtual tape library that existing backup software sees as a real tape.

**Q36 -> B.** Memcached = simple key-value cache, multi-threaded, maximum throughput, no persistence needed.

**Q37 -> A.** SQS DLQ with maxReceiveCount=3 isolates messages that fail 3 times.

**Q38 -> B.** IAM roles with STS = temporary credentials without creating individual IAM users.

**Q39 -> C.** Separate io2 for OLTP high-IOPS + st1 for sequential analytics reads. Different volume types optimized for different access patterns.

**Q40 -> C.** Redshift = columnar storage optimized for complex analytical SQL. Athena is good but slower for complex joins on this scale.

**Q41 -> B.** WAF with OWASP managed rules on ALB = blocks OWASP Top 10.

**Q42 -> C.** Step Functions = orchestration with retries, error handling, conditional branching, parallel steps.

**Q43 -> B.** First step = isolate, then investigate. Don't immediately terminate (may lose forensic evidence).

**Q44 -> B.** CloudFront caches content at European edge locations = lowest latency for European users.

**Q45 -> B.** Provisioned with Auto Scaling = scales to handle peak writes efficiently at lower per-unit cost than On-Demand.

**Q46 -> A.** SQS Standard + DLQ with maxReceiveCount=5 = retry 5 times then isolate.

**Q47 -> B.** API Gateway = HTTP/HTTPS front door for Lambda with authentication, throttling, caching.

**Q48 -> B.** Complete 3-tier VPC: IGW + public subnets + private subnets + NAT Gateway. Web servers in public, backend in private with NAT for internet access.

**Q49 -> B.** Lambda + API Gateway + DynamoDB = truly serverless, zero to millions, zero management.

**Q50 -> C.** Macie discovers PII in S3 and alerts on unexpected public exposure.

**Q51 -> B.** ALB listener rules route by path (`/api/*` vs `/web/*`) to different target groups.

**Q52 -> B.** S3 + CloudFront with short TTL (5 min) or cache invalidation after each hourly update.

**Q53 -> B.** IAM cross-account role = trusted external account can assume the role using STS. No shared credentials.

**Q54 -> C.** EFS mounts to multiple Fargate tasks as a shared persistent file system.

**Q55 -> C.** Global Accelerator = optimal routing over AWS backbone, no caching, for non-static traffic.

**Q56 -> B.** Organizations + CloudFormation StackSets = consistent deployment across all accounts.

**Q57 -> B.** AWS Glue = managed ETL service. Transforms CSV → Parquet and loads to Redshift.

**Q58 -> B (and E are the same answer).** S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint routes S3 traffic within AWS, no internet. NAT Gateway uses internet.

**Q59 -> B.** CloudWatch Agent collects memory, disk, and custom metrics from inside the OS. Default CloudWatch doesn't see OS-level memory.

**Q60 -> C.** Spot with checkpointing = cheapest for 30-min retryable batch jobs. Lambda max 15 min doesn't fit.

**Q61 -> C.** CloudHSM = dedicated hardware, AWS has no access to keys.

**Q62 -> B.** DLQ with `maxReceiveCount = 3` automatically moves messages to DLQ after 3 failed processing attempts.

**Q63 -> B.** IAM Identity Center with on-premises AD = corporate credentials for AWS access, simplest SSO setup.

**Q64 -> B.** CloudFront Signed URLs = time-limited access for authenticated (paying) subscribers.

**Q65 -> B.** Snapshot unattached volumes (preserve data), then delete volumes (stop paying for idle storage).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Full Mock Exam 2 — SAA-C03 (65 questions)

**Q1.** A company runs a stateless web tier on EC2. During peak hours CPU regularly hits 90%. The solution should automatically add EC2 capacity while keeping CPU around 60%. What is BEST?

- A. Scheduled scaling at peak hours
- B. Target Tracking Scaling policy at CPU 60%
- C. Manual scaling
- D. Add more instances permanently

**Q2.** A company uses Amazon S3 for static assets. They want to prevent any configuration change that accidentally makes the bucket public. What should they enforce?

- A. S3 Object Lock
- B. Enable S3 Block Public Access at the account level
- C. Add a bucket policy allowing only private access
- D. Enable S3 versioning

**Q3.** A company's RDS database performance degrades when many reporting queries run alongside OLTP workloads. What is the BEST solution without changing the application?

- A. Upgrade the RDS instance type
- B. Create RDS Read Replicas and route reporting traffic to them
- C. Enable RDS Multi-AZ
- D. Move reporting to a separate S3 bucket

**Q4.** (Choose TWO) A microservices architecture needs two services to communicate asynchronously. Service A publishes events. Services B and C each need to receive and process every event independently. What TWO components should be used?

- A. SQS Standard Queue with two consumers
- B. SNS topic subscribed to by SQS Queue B and SQS Queue C
- C. SQS FIFO for ordering
- D. SQS Queue B and SQS Queue C receiving from the SNS topic
- E. Both B and D together form the correct fan-out pattern

**Q5.** A company wants to allow users to securely upload videos directly to S3 from their browsers without routing through the company's servers. What should the architect use?

- A. Create an IAM user per browser user
- B. Generate pre-signed S3 URLs for PUT requests
- C. Make the S3 bucket public for uploads
- D. Use AWS Direct Connect

**Q6.** A startup needs a fully managed, serverless relational database for a new application with unpredictable traffic including potential periods of zero queries. Which is BEST?

- A. Amazon RDS (stops charging compute when stopped, but limited to 7-day stops)
- B. Amazon Aurora Serverless v2
- C. Amazon DynamoDB
- D. Amazon Redshift Serverless

**Q7.** A company's EC2 instances need to download OS patches but should NOT be directly accessible from the internet. The architect has placed them in private subnets. What must be added?

- A. Attach an Internet Gateway directly to the private subnet
- B. Deploy a NAT Gateway in a public subnet and add a route in the private subnet's route table
- C. Add Elastic IPs to the private instances
- D. Use VPC peering to another VPC that has internet access

**Q8.** A company wants to reduce EBS storage costs. A review finds 50 unattached EBS volumes, and some snapshots are 2 years old. What should they do?

- A. Delete all snapshots immediately
- B. Create snapshots of unattached volumes → delete unattached volumes, and delete old snapshots that are no longer needed for recovery
- C. Move snapshots to Glacier
- D. Resize all volumes to 1 GB

**Q9.** A fintech company is building a system to record financial transactions. Transactions must be cryptographically verifiable, immutable, and form a complete, tamper-proof history. Which AWS database?

- A. Amazon DynamoDB with Object Lock
- B. Amazon RDS with auditing enabled
- C. Amazon QLDB (Quantum Ledger Database)
- D. Amazon Aurora with Global Tables

**Q10.** A company serves a REST API to mobile clients. They need to cache API responses at the edge to reduce latency and backend load. Which service provides API caching at the edge?

- A. CloudFront in front of EC2
- B. Amazon API Gateway with caching enabled (and optionally CloudFront in front)
- C. ELB connection draining
- D. DynamoDB DAX

**Q11.** A company needs to store Hadoop HDFS data on AWS with high-throughput sequential access. Which storage is BEST?

- A. Amazon EBS io2
- B. Amazon EBS st1 (throughput optimized HDD)
- C. Amazon EFS
- D. Amazon S3 Glacier

**Q12.** A company wants to use ML-based recommendations for right-sizing their EC2 fleet to reduce costs. Which service should they use?

- A. AWS Trusted Advisor
- B. AWS Cost Explorer
- C. AWS Compute Optimizer
- D. AWS Budgets

**Q13.** A solutions architect needs to enable private, encrypted connectivity between an on-premises data center and multiple VPCs. Transit Gateway has been deployed. What connects on-premises to the Transit Gateway?

- A. VPC peering
- B. Direct Connect Gateway + Transit Gateway attachment, or VPN attachment to Transit Gateway
- C. CloudFront
- D. IAM Identity Center

**Q14.** A company hosts a multi-tenant SaaS application. Each customer should only see their own data in an S3 bucket. How can the architect enforce per-customer access without a bucket per customer?

- A. Use CloudFront signed URLs
- B. Use S3 Access Points with VPC or IAM-based policies per customer
- C. Create an IAM user per customer
- D. Use KMS encryption per customer

**Q15.** A company needs its Lambda functions to access resources in a private VPC (RDS, ElastiCache). The Lambda also needs to access an external payment API over the internet. What is REQUIRED?

- A. Lambda automatically accesses both VPC and internet
- B. Lambda in VPC needs a NAT Gateway in a public subnet to reach the internet while in the VPC
- C. Two Lambda functions: one in VPC, one not
- D. Public internet access is blocked from within a VPC

**Q16.** An S3 bucket contains video files. The company wants to run a serverless job every night to count the files and generate a summary stored in DynamoDB. Which architecture?

**Q17.** (Choose TWO) Which TWO services help protect against DDoS attacks on AWS?

**Q18.** A company needs to query 1 PB of historical data using SQL. Queries run once a week and must complete in under 10 minutes. Cost per query matters more than consistent performance. Which is MOST cost-effective?

**Q19.** A company has 5 VPCs in different AWS accounts that all need to communicate with each other. Each VPC also needs to connect to an on-premises network. What is the MOST scalable architecture?

**Q59.** (Choose TWO) A company wants to improve the security of their AWS accounts. Which TWO practices are MOST effective?

**Q60.** An e-commerce platform needs to handle flash sales where traffic increases 50x in seconds. The architecture must scale INSTANTLY. Which compute option handles this BEST?

**Q61.** A company runs Aurora MySQL. They want to automatically scale Aurora read replicas based on CPU. What Aurora feature provides this?

- A. Aurora Multi-Master
- B. Aurora Serverless v2
- C. Aurora Auto Scaling (scales the number of Aurora read replicas)
- D. RDS Proxy

**Q62.** An architect needs to encrypt all data stored in DynamoDB using a customer-managed KMS key for compliance. What should they configure?

- A. DynamoDB Object Lock
- B. Enable DynamoDB encryption at rest using a customer-managed KMS key
- C. Encrypt data before writing using client-side encryption only
- D. DynamoDB is always encrypted with AWS-managed keys only

**Q63.** A company has EC2 instances that run background processing and regularly consume 100% CPU. The company wants to prevent these instances from affecting other workloads in the same account on the same physical host. What should they use?

- A. Cluster placement group
- B. Dedicated Instances
- C. Spread placement group
- D. Enhanced networking

**Q64.** A company needs to migrate 3 TB of data from an on-premises NAS to Amazon EFS over a weekend. Which service provides the FASTEST automated migration?

- A. AWS Snowball (overkill and too slow for 3 TB)
- B. AWS DataSync over Direct Connect or internet
- C. Manual rsync
- D. S3 Transfer Acceleration (wrong service for EFS)

**Q65.** A startup wants to validate its new architecture's cost, performance, security, and resilience against AWS best practices before going to production. Which AWS tool provides this structured review?

- A. AWS Trusted Advisor
- B. AWS Well-Architected Framework Review (via AWS Well-Architected Tool)
- C. AWS Config
- D. Amazon Inspector

### Mock Exam 2 — Answers (Q1–Q65)

**Q1 -> B.** Target Tracking at CPU 60% = Auto Scaling adjusts to maintain 60%.
**Q2 -> B.** S3 Block Public Access at account level = no bucket can become public regardless of bucket policy.
**Q3 -> B.** Read Replicas = offload read (reporting) queries from primary RDS.
**Q4 -> B and D.** The fan-out pattern: SNS topic → SQS Queue B (subscribed) and SQS Queue C (subscribed). B and D together form the correct pattern.
**Q5 -> B.** Pre-signed PUT URLs allow direct browser uploads to S3 with no server involvement, with temporary expiry.
**Q6 -> B.** Aurora Serverless v2 scales to near-zero and back — perfect for variable/zero-traffic periods.
**Q7 -> B.** NAT Gateway in public subnet + route table entry in private subnet = internet access from private subnet (outbound only).
**Q8 -> B.** Snapshot unattached volumes → delete them (stop paying for storage) → delete unneeded old snapshots.
**Q9 -> C.** QLDB = immutable, cryptographically verifiable ledger. Purpose-built for financial transaction history.
**Q10 -> B.** API Gateway has built-in caching; CloudFront can also be placed in front. API Gateway caching is the direct answer.
**Q11 -> B.** st1 = throughput optimized HDD, sequential reads, perfect for Hadoop/HDFS workloads.
**Q12 -> C.** Compute Optimizer uses ML for right-sizing EC2, Lambda, EBS, ECS.
**Q13 -> B.** Direct Connect Gateway + Transit Gateway = scalable private on-premises to multiple VPCs.
**Q14 -> B.** S3 Access Points with per-access-point policies = isolated access per tenant.
**Q15 -> B.** Lambda in VPC + NAT Gateway = can reach both private VPC resources and external internet.
**Q16 -> B.** EventBridge Scheduler → Lambda (count files) → DynamoDB = serverless scheduled job.
**Q17 -> A and B.** Shield Standard (automatic DDoS protection) + WAF (application-layer rate limiting/blocking).
**Q18 -> B.** Athena = pay per query, no always-on cluster, most cost-effective for infrequent queries on S3.
**Q19 -> B.** Transit Gateway = hub-and-spoke, transitive, scalable. VPC peering = non-transitive, exponential connections.
**Q20 -> B.** EventBridge rules route events to multiple targets based on content = clean event-driven fan-out.
**Q21 -> A.** DynamoDB Global Tables = multi-region, active-active writes, last-write-wins conflict resolution.
**Q22 -> B.** Aurora PostgreSQL-compatible + better performance than standard RDS PostgreSQL.
**Q23 -> B.** S3 event → SNS → email subscription = simple notification pattern.
**Q24 -> B.** AWS Backup with a backup plan = managed, scheduled, centralized. No custom scripts.
**Q25 -> B.** S3 Versioning = all versions kept, delete creates a delete marker, recoverable for any retention period.
**Q26 -> B.** Route table in VPC with on-premises CIDR → Direct Connect Virtual Private Gateway = standard DX routing.
**Q27 -> B.** CloudTrail multi-Region trail to S3 = comprehensive API audit logging.
**Q28 -> B.** Cognito Identity Pool exchanges User Pool JWT for temporary AWS credentials.
**Q29 -> A.** Cache-aside (lazy loading) with ElastiCache Redis = application checks cache, misses go to RDS.
**Q30 -> C.** EKS + Fargate profiles = serverless Kubernetes pods, no node management.
**Q31 -> B.** CloudTrail logs all KMS API calls including Decrypt events.
**Q32 -> C.** DynamoDB = low-latency, key-value, flexible schema, consistent performance.
**Q33 -> B.** External session store (Redis) = all instances share sessions. Sticky sessions work but cause uneven load distribution.
**Q34 -> B.** Kinesis Data Streams = real-time high-volume ingestion. Kinesis Firehose delivers to S3 automatically.
**Q35 -> C.** IAM policies with `ec2:CreateTags` conditions or Service Control Policies can enforce tagging.
**Q36 -> C.** CloudFront with Asian edge locations = content cached close to Asian users.
**Q37 -> B.** Athena = $5 per TB scanned, no cluster, pay only when querying.
**Q38 -> B.** RDS Multi-AZ = single DNS endpoint that automatically updates to standby on failover.
**Q39 -> B.** RDS Proxy = connection pooling for Lambda (manages DB connection lifecycle).
**Q40 -> B.** S3 Standard 2 years → Glacier Deep Archive years 2–7 = lowest long-term archival cost.
**Q41 -> C.** Security Hub multi-account = centralized security dashboard with CIS/PCI/FSBP checks.
**Q42 -> B.** Lambda max timeout is 15 minutes. 5-minute processing = perfectly fine.
**Q43 -> B.** CloudFront invalidation removes cached files from edges immediately.
**Q44 -> B.** Site-to-Site VPN → VPC → Interface Endpoint for DynamoDB = private, no Direct Connect needed.
**Q45 -> B.** Modify the ALB security group to allow only the corporate IP. Simpler than WAF for single IP.
**Q46 -> B.** S3 Select runs SQL expressions inside S3 and returns only matching data, reducing transfer.
**Q47 -> B.** Parameter Store with path hierarchy (e.g., `/prod/db/connection`) = versioned config, free tier available.
**Q48 -> B.** SQS FIFO + deduplication = exactly-once, ordered processing.
**Q49 -> B.** Add EC2 in second AZ + ELB = minimum change for HA.
**Q50 -> B.** Redshift Spectrum queries S3 data from within Redshift without loading it.
**Q51 -> B.** S3 pre-signed URL or CloudFront = serves files directly to users without going through app server.
**Q52 -> B.** Latency-based routing = Route 53 directs users to the Region with lowest measured latency.
**Q53 -> B.** SCP denying Internet Gateway attachment/creation = no account in the org can expose VPCs to internet.
**Q54 -> B.** S3 + CloudFront = lowest cost static hosting with global distribution.
**Q55 -> B.** Visibility timeout > processing time prevents duplicate processing by concurrent consumers.
**Q56 -> C.** Route 53 Failover routing with health checks = automatic DNS failover from primary to secondary.
**Q57 -> A.** Lambda's Kinesis event source mapping = Lambda polls the stream in batches.
**Q58 -> B.** Secrets Manager = stores and rotates API keys. Never in code or env vars.
**Q59 -> A and C.** MFA for root/privileged + permission boundaries = strong security. B/D/E are dangerous.
**Q60 -> B.** Lambda scales instantly to handle concurrent invocations. EC2/Fargate take minutes to launch.
**Q61 -> C.** Aurora Auto Scaling adds/removes read replicas based on CPU or connection metrics.
**Q62 -> B.** DynamoDB encryption at rest with customer-managed KMS key (already encrypted by default, customer-managed key gives control).
**Q63 -> B.** Dedicated Instances = hardware dedicated to you, no sharing with other accounts' instances.
**Q64 -> B.** AWS DataSync = automated, fast, managed migration from NAS to EFS.
**Q65 -> B.** AWS Well-Architected Tool = structured review against the 6 Well-Architected pillars.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Full Mock Exam 3 — SAA-C03 Final Readiness (65 questions)

**Q1.** A company's application has tight coupling between components. If one service fails, the whole system goes down. The architect wants to decouple the components. Which approach BEST decouples the services?

- A. Use larger EC2 instances
- B. Introduce SQS queues between services so each can operate independently
- C. Move everything to a single Lambda function
- D. Use Dedicated Hosts

**Q2.** A media company needs to store 500 TB of video for 10 years. Videos are archived after 6 months and rarely accessed. What is the MOST cost-effective S3 configuration?

- A. S3 Standard for all 10 years
- B. S3 Standard 6 months → Lifecycle to S3 Glacier Deep Archive for remainder
- C. S3 Standard-IA throughout
- D. S3 One Zone-IA for 10 years

**Q3.** A company needs a highly available web application. Traffic is low during weekdays, very high on Saturdays. The company wants to scale predictably for Saturday. Which Auto Scaling policy?

- A. Target Tracking Scaling
- B. Predictive Scaling (knows Saturday is always busy) or Scheduled Scaling
- C. Step Scaling
- D. Manual scaling each Friday night

**Q4.** A healthcare company stores PHI (Protected Health Information) in S3. They must detect if any PHI is exposed publicly or shared incorrectly. Which service?

- A. Amazon GuardDuty
- B. Amazon Macie
- C. AWS Security Hub
- D. Amazon Inspector

**Q5.** A company's current architecture has all services calling each other directly. An architect needs to make the purchase service notify the inventory, shipping, and billing services when a purchase is completed. Which pattern adds the LEAST coupling?

- A. Purchase service calls Inventory API, Shipping API, and Billing API
- B. Purchase service publishes to an SNS topic; Inventory, Shipping, and Billing each subscribe via SQS
- C. Purchase service writes to DynamoDB, others poll DynamoDB
- D. Use a Lambda orchestrator

**Q6.** An architect needs to ensure their application's secret keys are never visible in environment variables, source code, or CloudFormation templates. Which service securely stores and retrieves secrets at runtime?

- A. AWS Parameter Store (SecureString)
- B. AWS Secrets Manager
- C. Environment variables with encryption
- D. AWS KMS

**Q7.** A company has a large number of S3 objects and needs to find objects larger than 1 GB to reduce storage cost. They want this without downloading every object. Which service?

- A. S3 Lifecycle rules
- B. Amazon Athena on S3 inventory
- C. S3 Inventory with analysis in Athena
- D. AWS Macie

**Q8.** A company's application writes logs to CloudWatch. They want to alert the operations team whenever the error rate exceeds 5% in any 5-minute period. What should they configure?

- A. CloudWatch Dashboard
- B. CloudWatch Metric Filter + CloudWatch Alarm → SNS → Email
- C. AWS Config rule
- D. AWS CloudTrail alerts

**Q9.** A company wants to enable their data science team to run ML training jobs on temporary EC2 instances, but prevent them from running instances larger than ml.m5.4xlarge to control costs. How?

- A. IAM permission boundary limiting instance types
- B. IAM policy using condition key `ec2:InstanceType` to restrict instance sizes
- C. AWS Budgets with instance type filter
- D. AWS Config rule (detects after launch, not preventive)

**Q10.** A company stores customer data in RDS. A recent audit found they could not prove the database credentials were never compromised in the last year. What should they implement going forward?

- A. KMS encryption on RDS
- B. Secrets Manager with automatic rotation + CloudTrail logging of secret access
- C. IAM database authentication only
- D. SSL/TLS in transit

**Q11.** A company needs to connect their on-premises Active Directory to AWS for SSO. IAM users should not need to be created. What is the SIMPLEST approach?

- A. Sync Active Directory to IAM manually
- B. Use AWS IAM Identity Center connected to AWS Managed Microsoft AD or AD Connector
- C. Create one IAM user per employee
- D. Use Cognito User Pools for AD federation

**Q12.** A company needs to store 100,000 IoT sensor readings per second in real-time. Readings need to be available for analytics in near real-time. Which ingestion service is BEST?

- A. Amazon SQS
- B. Amazon Kinesis Data Streams
- C. Amazon SNS
- D. AWS IoT Core directly to S3

**Q13.** A startup wants to build a REST API backend. The team prefers to write business logic without managing servers. The API must scale to 0 when unused. Which architecture?

- A. EC2 with Auto Scaling (minimum 1 instance)
- B. API Gateway + Lambda (scales to zero, pay per request)
- C. ECS Fargate (always-on minimum task)
- D. Elastic Beanstalk

**Q14.** A company's Aurora cluster is in us-east-1. For DR, they want a read-only copy in eu-west-1 that can become the primary in under 1 minute if us-east-1 fails. What should they configure?

- A. RDS Multi-AZ in eu-west-1
- B. Aurora Global Database with a secondary Region in eu-west-1
- C. Aurora Cross-Region Read Replica
- D. S3 CRR of Aurora backups

**Q15.** A company is migrating their web application from a monolith to microservices on AWS. Each microservice is a container. They want to use Kubernetes but minimize cluster management. What should they choose?

- A. ECS on EC2 with manual cluster management
- B. EKS with managed node groups
- C. EKS with Fargate profiles (no node management)
- D. Lambda (not Kubernetes)

**Q16.** A company has a 10 Gbps data transfer requirement from their data center to AWS monthly. The architect must choose between VPN and Direct Connect. Which factor MOST favors Direct Connect?

- A. Direct Connect is cheaper per GB and provides consistent bandwidth
- B. VPN is more reliable
- C. VPN provides higher throughput
- D. Direct Connect is automatically encrypted

**Q17.** A company's application has an ALB receiving traffic. They need to ensure that only their company's IP ranges (not the general public) can access the ALB on port 443. What is the MOST appropriate mechanism?

**Q18.** A company runs an application where write operations are critical. They want to ensure that even if an entire AZ fails, writes continue without interruption. Which database meets this requirement?

- B. Aurora Multi-Master (active-active writes across multiple AZs)

**Q19.** An application writes to S3, and downstream processing services need to react to new objects. The architect wants near-real-time processing with the LEAST additional infrastructure. What should they use?

**Q23.** A company's data pipeline reads from DynamoDB, transforms data, and writes to Redshift daily. Which AWS service is BEST for orchestrating this ETL pipeline?

**Q24.** A company has EC2 instances in a private subnet in VPC A. They need to access an API hosted in VPC B (different account) without the traffic going over the internet. VPC peering is not allowed due to policy. Which option is BEST?

**Q25.** A company is building a multi-tenant SaaS where each customer has their own data encrypted with separate keys. Which approach allows per-tenant encryption with centralized key management?

**Q26.** An architect needs to ensure that ALL API calls made in the account are logged, even calls from the root user. Which service captures this?

**Q27.** A company's application needs to process a large SQS queue quickly. They add more consumers but the queue isn't draining faster. What is likely the issue?

**Q28.** A company wants to use CloudFront to serve both static S3 content and dynamic API responses from an ALB under the same domain. What should they configure?

**Q30.** A company's EC2 instances are in Auto Scaling. During a deployment, 50% of instances must remain in service while the new version is deployed to the other 50%. Which deployment strategy?

**Q56.** A company deploys a new version of their application weekly. They want zero downtime and the ability to instantly revert to the previous version. Which deployment strategy?

**Q57.** A company has an application on EC2 in a private subnet. The application must access Systems Manager to retrieve parameter values without internet access. What is needed?

**Q58.** A company is building an analytics platform. Raw data arrives in S3 as CSV. It needs to be cataloged, transformed to Parquet, and made queryable by Athena. Which combination handles this end-to-end?

**Q59.** A company needs a 99.99% uptime SLA for their RDS database. What should they configure?

- A. RDS with automated backups only

- C. RDS Multi-AZ + cross-Region read replica promoted as DR site
- D. RDS with increased instance size

**Q60.** A company needs to detect that an EC2 instance is communicating with a known cryptomining pool. Which service provides this detection automatically?

- A. AWS Config
- B. Amazon Inspector
- C. Amazon GuardDuty (detects cryptocurrency mining with threat intelligence)
- D. AWS WAF

**Q61.** A company's DynamoDB table costs $2,000/month in provisioned capacity. CloudWatch shows 70% of provisioned capacity is unused at all times. What should the architect do?

- A. Switch to DynamoDB On-Demand (may be more expensive at higher utilization)
- B. Enable DynamoDB Auto Scaling to provision based on actual usage
- C. Create a read replica
- D. Migrate to RDS

**Q62.** A company needs cross-account access between Account A (source) and Account B (destination). Account B's Lambda function needs to read objects from Account A's S3 bucket. What should they configure?

- A. Make the S3 bucket in A public
- B. Create an IAM role in Account A that Account B's Lambda can assume, with an S3 read policy + update the S3 bucket policy to allow Account B
- C. VPC peering
- D. Copy data from Account A to Account B's S3 bucket

**Q63.** A company runs a container-based application on ECS Fargate. They want to mount a shared volume that persists across task restarts and can be accessed from multiple tasks simultaneously. Which storage option?

- A. Fargate ephemeral storage (lost on task termination)
- B. EBS volume attached to Fargate task
- C. Amazon EFS mounted to the Fargate task definition
- D. S3 mounted as a volume

**Q64.** An architect needs to ensure that when EC2 instances in an Auto Scaling Group are terminated, they complete all in-flight requests before being terminated (connection draining). Which mechanism handles this?

- A. CloudWatch alarm
- B. ELB connection draining / deregistration delay (allows in-flight requests to complete before deregistering the instance)
- C. EC2 Auto Scaling cooldown period
- D. Auto Scaling lifecycle hook

**Q65.** A company wants to check their AWS architecture against the 6 pillars of the Well-Architected Framework and get specific recommendations. Which AWS service/tool provides this structured review?

- A. AWS Trusted Advisor
- B. AWS Config
- C. AWS Well-Architected Tool
- D. Amazon Inspector

### Mock Exam 3 — Answers (All 65)

**Q1 -> B.** SQS between services = asynchronous, decoupled. Each can fail independently without cascading.
**Q2 -> B.** S3 Standard 6 months → Glacier Deep Archive = lowest long-term archival cost.
**Q3 -> B.** Scheduled Scaling = scale up before known Saturday peaks. Predictive Scaling also works.
**Q4 -> B.** Macie = sensitive data discovery and alerts for PHI in S3.
**Q5 -> B.** SNS → SQS (fan-out) = purchase service only publishes; others subscribe independently.
**Q6 -> B.** Secrets Manager = retrieve secrets at runtime; never visible in env vars or code.
**Q7 -> C.** S3 Inventory generates a manifest of all objects with metadata; query with Athena to filter by size.
**Q8 -> B.** CloudWatch Metric Filter → Alarm → SNS → email = standard monitoring alerting pattern.
**Q9 -> B.** IAM policy condition `ec2:InstanceType` = preventive control restricting instance sizes.
**Q10 -> B.** Secrets Manager rotation + CloudTrail = credential access auditing + automatic rotation.
**Q11 -> B.** IAM Identity Center + AD Connector or AWS Managed AD = federated SSO, no IAM users needed.
**Q12 -> B.** Kinesis Data Streams = high-volume, real-time IoT event ingestion.
**Q13 -> B.** API Gateway + Lambda = serverless REST API that scales to zero.
**Q14 -> B.** Aurora Global Database = cross-Region replication with < 1-second lag and < 1-minute failover.
**Q15 -> C.** EKS + Fargate = Kubernetes, no node/cluster management.
**Q16 -> A.** Direct Connect provides consistent bandwidth, lower per-GB cost for high-volume transfers.
**Q17 -> B.** Security group inbound rule restricting to company IP ranges = simplest, correct approach.
**Q18 -> B.** Aurora Multi-Master = active-active writes across AZs — no interruption even if an AZ fails.
**Q19 -> B.** S3 Event Notifications → SQS → Lambda = near-real-time, minimal infrastructure.
**Q20 -> C.** Service Catalog = enforces approved CloudFormation templates at deployment time (preventive).
**Q21 -> B.** Secrets Manager = runtime retrieval of password; eliminate hard-coded credentials.
**Q22 -> A.** Trusted Advisor Low Utilization EC2 check = identifies idle instances.
**Q23 -> B.** Step Functions + Glue = orchestrated, multi-step ETL pipeline with error handling.
**Q24 -> B.** AWS PrivateLink = private cross-account connectivity without VPC peering or transit.
**Q25 -> B.** One KMS key per tenant = isolated encryption; centrally managed in KMS.
**Q26 -> B.** CloudTrail multi-Region trail = logs ALL API calls including root.
**Q27 -> A or B.** If FIFO: limited parallelism per message group. If Standard: visibility timeout too short → messages reappear.
**Q28 -> B.** One CloudFront distribution + multiple origins + path-based cache behaviors = correct.
**Q29 -> B.** KMS automatic key rotation = yearly key material rotation; existing encrypted data remains decryptable via key ID mapping.
**Q30 -> B.** Blue/green = launch new ASG → switch ELB → terminate old. Instant rollback possible.
**Q31 -> B.** AWS Config rule + auto-remediation + StackSets = consistent across all accounts.
**Q32 -> B.** Kinesis Firehose reads from Kinesis Streams and delivers to S3 automatically.
**Q33 -> B.** IAM Deny policy with resource tag condition = prevents production instance termination.
**Q34 -> B.** App SG outbound to DB SG on 3306; DB SG inbound from app SG on 3306 = correct SG pattern.
**Q35 -> C.** S3 Glacier Instant Retrieval = lowest-cost with millisecond (sub-second) retrieval.
**Q36 -> B.** S3 Gateway VPC Endpoint = free, private S3 access from private subnet.
**Q37 -> C.** Neptune = graph database for social connections (nodes/relationships).
**Q38 -> B.** Visibility timeout expires → message becomes visible again for retry.
**Q39 -> B.** Pre-signed URL with 48-hour expiration = time-limited access, no IAM user needed.
**Q40 -> A and C.** Multi-AZ + eliminate single points of failure = fault tolerance.
**Q41 -> B.** CloudFront invalidation = immediately removes cached file from all edges.
**Q42 -> B.** NLB preserves client IP by default. ALB uses X-Forwarded-For header.
**Q43 -> A.** Lambda reserved concurrency caps a function's max concurrency, protecting other functions.
**Q44 -> B.** AWS SCT converts schema + AWS DMS migrates data = standard heterogeneous DB migration.
**Q45 -> B.** Systems Manager Patch Manager = automated patching on schedule.
**Q46 -> B.** AWS Glue = serverless Spark ETL. No cluster management unlike EMR.
**Q47 -> B.** Amazon SES = transactional email at scale (up to millions/day).
**Q48 -> B.** Cognito Identity Pools support OIDC federation → temporary AWS credentials.
**Q49 -> B.** RDS Proxy = connection pooling, reduces actual DB connections by multiplexing.
**Q50 -> B.** API Gateway WebSocket API = bidirectional persistent connections for real-time push.
**Q51 -> B.** Synchronous communication = direct call between tiers within VPC.
**Q52 -> B.** WAF can be attached to CloudFront distributions for edge-based protection.
**Q53 -> B.** AWS Config Organization conformance pack = multi-account compliance checks.
**Q54 -> B.** On-Demand for 30 minutes once a month = cheapest (no commitment, short duration). Spot is cheaper but risky for scientific simulations (unless checkpoint enabled).
**Q55 -> B.** Macie = automated sensitive data categorization and protection in S3.
**Q56 -> B.** Blue/green = zero downtime + instant revert by switching Route 53/ELB back.
**Q57 -> B.** Interface VPC Endpoints for SSM (3 endpoints needed: ssm, ec2messages, ssmmessages) = private SSM access.
**Q58 -> B.** Glue crawler catalogs S3 → Glue ETL job converts CSV → Parquet → Athena queries.
**Q59 -> C.** Multi-AZ + cross-Region DR = highest RDS availability.
**Q60 -> C.** GuardDuty uses threat intelligence to detect cryptomining, unusual API calls, compromised instances.
**Q61 -> B.** DynamoDB Auto Scaling with provisioned mode = scales to actual usage, eliminates 70% waste.
**Q62 -> B.** Cross-account: IAM role in Account A (trust policy allows Account B) + S3 bucket policy allows Account B Lambda.
**Q63 -> C.** Amazon EFS mounted to Fargate = persistent, shared across tasks.
**Q64 -> B.** ELB connection draining (deregistration delay) = waits for in-flight requests before deregistering.
**Q65 -> C.** AWS Well-Architected Tool = structured review against 6 pillars with recommendations.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Final Review

## What makes SAA-C03 hard and how to beat it

SAA-C03 is hard because the questions all have multiple plausible answers. Almost every wrong choice is something that "also works" but isn't optimal for the stated constraint. The exam always wants the BEST answer for the specific situation.

Train yourself to always ask: What is the KEY CONSTRAINT in this question?
- "Least operational overhead" → managed/serverless wins
- "Most cost-effective" → match purchasing model to workload pattern
- "Highest availability" → multi-AZ or multi-Region active-active
- "Most scalable" → serverless or auto-scaling
- "Fastest" → edge caching, in-memory, or provisioned concurrency
- "Most secure" → least privilege, no long-term keys, encryption

## Final readiness checklist

- [ ] I can name all four Route 53 routing policies and their use cases.
- [ ] I know when to use ALB vs NLB (content routing vs static IP / TCP).
- [ ] I know RDS Multi-AZ (HA, standby is passive) vs Read Replicas (performance, readable).
- [ ] I know S3 Gateway Endpoint (free, S3/DynamoDB) vs Interface Endpoint (paid, all others).
- [ ] I know SQS Standard vs FIFO (ordering/exactly-once) differences.
- [ ] I can choose between SNS, SQS, and EventBridge correctly.
- [ ] I know Aurora vs RDS vs DynamoDB vs Redshift for different use cases.
- [ ] I understand Spot (interruptible, cheap), Reserved (steady, committed), and Savings Plans (flexible committed).
- [ ] I know CloudFront (CDN, caching) vs Global Accelerator (static IP, routing) vs Route 53 (DNS).
- [ ] I know ElastiCache Redis (persistence, complex types, HA) vs Memcached (simple, multi-threaded).
- [ ] I understand the VPC peering (non-transitive) vs Transit Gateway (transitive hub) difference.
- [ ] I know Direct Connect (private, NOT encrypted) vs VPN (encrypted, internet) vs DX+VPN (both).
- [ ] I scored 80%+ on all three mock exams and understand every wrong answer.

- AWS Architecture Center: architecture.aws (reference architectures)
