6. **Verify full system functionality** — test that everything works AND nothing new broke.
7. **Document** — record what happened and what you did.

> **Exam Tip:** The methodology is tested via scenario questions. The key principle: always question the obvious first, test your theory before implementing, and verify afterward.

## 5.2 PC Troubleshooting Symptoms

### Power issues
| Symptom | Likely cause |
|---|---|
| No POST, no beeps, no video | Dead PSU, bad CPU, bad RAM, bad motherboard |
| Continuous beeps | RAM not seated. Run memtest86 |
| POST beep codes | Motherboard-specific: RAM, GPU, CPU errors |
| PC powers on then off immediately | Overheating, PSU overload, short circuit |
| BSOD (Blue Screen of Death) | Driver issue, failing RAM, failing storage, overheating, corrupt OS |

### POST and boot
- **POST (Power-On Self Test)** — runs at startup, checks CPU, RAM, storage, peripherals.
- **BIOS/UEFI** — set time, boot order, enable/disable ports, XMP for RAM.
- **Boot order** — set which device to boot from first (SSD, USB, optical).
- **No boot device found** — check boot order, check cable connection, storage may have failed.

### Storage troubleshooting
| Symptom | Cause |
|---|---|
| Clicking or grinding sounds | HDD failing — backup immediately |
| Slow performance, excessive page file use | Low RAM causing excessive paging (swapping) |
| S.M.A.R.T. errors | HDD/SSD predicting imminent failure |
| OS not found / no boot device | Failed drive, cable issue, wrong boot order |

### Display issues
| Symptom | Cause |
|---|---|
| No display, fans spin | GPU not seated, monitor cable, monitor dead |
| Display works then goes black | Overheating GPU, loose cable |
| Distorted/garbled video | Failed GPU, driver issue |
| Flickering | Refresh rate mismatch, cable, panel issue |
| Burn-in / image persistence | OLED or plasma display left on static image |
| Dead pixels | Manufacturing defect in LCD panel |

### RAM issues
- Symptoms: BSOD, random reboots, system crashes during memory-intensive tasks.
- Test with **memtest86** (bootable tool).
- Try one stick at a time to isolate bad stick.

## 5.3 Network Troubleshooting

### Windows network commands (exam favorites)
| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `ipconfig` | Show IP address, subnet mask, gateway |
| `ipconfig /all` | Full config including DNS, MAC address, DHCP info |
| `ipconfig /release` | Release DHCP lease |
| `ipconfig /renew` | Renew DHCP lease |
| `ipconfig /flushdns` | Clear DNS resolver cache |
| `ping` | Test connectivity to an IP/hostname |
| `tracert` (traceroute on Linux/Mac) | Show route and latency to destination |
| `nslookup` | Query DNS for a hostname |
| `netstat` | Show active connections and listening ports |
| `netstat -an` | All connections with port numbers |
| `arp -a` | Show ARP cache (IP to MAC mappings) |
| `nbtstat` | NetBIOS stats (Windows-specific) |

### Troubleshooting IP issues

**APIPA (169.254.x.x)** — automatically assigned when DHCP server unreachable. The device has given up waiting for DHCP. Check: DHCP server up? Cable connected? Switch port working?

**Duplicate IP** — two devices have same IP. Symptoms: intermittent connectivity for both. Fix: find and change one.

**Wrong subnet mask** — device can't communicate with other local devices. Mismatched subnets.

**Wrong default gateway** — device can talk locally but not to the internet.

**DNS failure** — websites don't load by name but ping by IP works. Run `ipconfig /flushdns`, check DNS server setting.

**Link light indicators:**
- Solid = link established
- Flashing = activity
- Off = no link (check cable, port, NIC)

### Common network issues

| Symptom | Cause |
|---|---|
| No internet, local network works | Wrong or unreachable gateway/DNS |
| Can ping IP, not hostname | DNS issue |
| Slow network | Duplex mismatch, damaged cable, congestion, interference (wireless) |
| Intermittent drops | Bad cable/connector, interference, failing NIC |
| Wi-Fi shows connected, no internet | IP conflict, DNS issue, router problem |
| 169.254.x.x IP | DHCP unavailable |

### Wireless troubleshooting
- **Interference** — 2.4 GHz congested in apartments (many networks + microwave ovens, Bluetooth). Switch to 5 GHz or 6 GHz.
- **Poor signal** — move closer, check for physical obstructions, add WAP or repeater.
- **Can't connect** — wrong SSID, wrong password, MAC filter blocking, captive portal needed.
- **Channel overlap** — use 1, 6, or 11 on 2.4 GHz. 5 GHz has many non-overlapping channels.

### Domain 5 Mini Quiz (8 questions)

**Q1.** A PC will not POST and makes continuous beeping sounds. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Failed hard drive  B. Incorrect boot order  C. RAM not properly seated  D. Dead GPU

**Q2.** A user's laptop shows 169.254.x.x as its IP address. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. IP conflict  B. DNS failure  C. DHCP server is unreachable  D. Wrong subnet mask

**Q3.** A technician wants to clear the DNS cache on a Windows computer. Which command?
- A. `ipconfig /release`  B. `ipconfig /flushdns`  C. `netstat -r`  D. `arp -d`

**Q4.** A user can browse websites by IP address (e.g., 8.8.8.8) but not by name (e.g., google.com). What is the issue?
- A. Default gateway  B. DHCP  C. DNS  D. Subnet mask

**Q5.** An HDD is making a clicking sound. What should the technician do FIRST?
- A. Run chkdsk  B. Replace immediately  C. Immediately back up all data before the drive fails  D. Run defrag

**Q6.** Which command shows the network path that packets take to reach a destination and the latency at each hop?
- A. `ping`  B. `netstat`  C. `tracert`  D. `nslookup`

**Q7.** A user's workstation connects to the local network but cannot reach the internet. Other workstations are fine. What is the MOST likely issue on this specific workstation?
- A. ISP outage  B. Wrong or missing default gateway configured  C. Firewall at the ISP  D. DNS server down

**Q8.** A wireless user complains of slow speeds and intermittent drops. The WLAN is on 2.4 GHz channel 6. A site survey shows 8 nearby networks also on channel 6. What should you do?
- A. Reset the access point  B. Switch to 5 GHz and use a non-overlapping channel  C. Increase transmit power  D. Change to WPA2

### Domain 5 Answers
**Q1->C.** Continuous beeping = RAM not seated. Long/short beep patterns indicate other failures.
**Q2->C.** 169.254.x.x = APIPA = DHCP unreachable. Check DHCP server and network connection.
**Q3->B.** `ipconfig /flushdns` clears DNS cache.
**Q4->C.** Can reach by IP but not name = DNS resolution failing. DNS server down or misconfigured.
**Q5->C.** Clicking HDD = imminent failure. Backup IMMEDIATELY before the drive dies completely.
**Q6->C.** `tracert` shows the hop-by-hop path and latency to destination.
**Q7->B.** Other workstations fine = ISP/DNS/gateway are OK globally. This workstation has wrong gateway.
**Q8->B.** 8 networks on channel 6 = heavy interference. 5 GHz has more channels and less interference.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# CORE 2 (220-1202)

# Core 2 — Domain 1: Operating Systems (31%)

## 1.1 Windows

### Windows versions (A+ scope)
- **Windows 10** — mainstream support. Home, Pro, Education, Enterprise editions.
- **Windows 11** — requires TPM 2.0, Secure Boot, 64-bit CPU, 4GB RAM minimum.
- **Home vs Pro vs Enterprise:**
  - Home: no domain join, no BitLocker, no Group Policy, no Remote Desktop (server)
  - Pro: domain join, BitLocker, Group Policy, Remote Desktop
  - Enterprise/Education: all Pro features + advanced management (AppLocker, DirectAccess, BranchCache)

### Windows file systems
- **NTFS** — Windows default. Supports: large files, permissions, encryption (EFS), compression, journaling, file sizes >4GB.
- **FAT32** — older. Max file size: 4GB. Max partition: 2TB. Compatible with everything (USB drives, game consoles).
- **exFAT** — FAT32 replacement for flash storage. No 4GB file limit. Cross-platform.
- **ReFS** — resilient file system for Windows Server. Not standard for A+.

> **Exam Tip:** FAT32 max file size = 4GB. This is why large video files need NTFS or exFAT.

### Windows Settings and Control Panel
| Task | Tool |
|---|---|
| Add/remove apps | Settings > Apps OR Control Panel > Programs |
| User accounts | Settings > Accounts OR Control Panel > User Accounts |
| System info | Settings > System > About OR `msinfo32` |
| Device Manager | Control Panel > Device Manager OR `devmgmt.msc` |
| Disk Management | `diskmgmt.msc` |
| Task Manager | Ctrl+Shift+Esc OR right-click taskbar |
| Registry Editor | `regedit` |
| Services | `services.msc` |
| Group Policy | `gpedit.msc` (Pro/Enterprise only) |
| Event Viewer | `eventvwr.msc` |
| Performance Monitor | `perfmon.msc` |
| Remote Desktop | `mstsc.exe` |
| System Configuration | `msconfig` |

### Windows administrative tools
**Task Manager (Ctrl+Shift+Esc):** Monitor processes, CPU/RAM/disk/network usage, startup programs, performance, users.

**Event Viewer:** Logs for Application, Security, System events. Check for errors and warnings.

**Device Manager:** View hardware, update drivers, check for driver errors (yellow !, red X).

**Disk Management:** Create/delete partitions, format drives, change drive letters, extend/shrink volumes, initialize new drives.

**Registry Editor (regedit):** Edit Windows registry. HKLM (machine), HKCU (current user), HKU, HKCR, HKCC. Backup before editing.

**Group Policy Editor (gpedit.msc):** Apply security policies, software restrictions, user settings. Pro/Enterprise only.

### Windows command line tools
| Command | Function |
|---|---|
| `dir` | List directory contents (like `ls` on Linux) |
| `cd` | Change directory |
| `md` / `mkdir` | Make directory |
| `rd` / `rmdir` | Remove directory |
| `copy` | Copy files |
| `move` | Move files |
| `del` | Delete files |
| `rename` / `ren` | Rename file |
| `cls` | Clear screen |
| `type` | Display file content |
| `chkdsk` | Check disk for errors |
| `sfc /scannow` | System File Checker — repairs corrupted system files |
| `DISM /Online /Cleanup-Image /RestoreHealth` | Repairs Windows image |
| `diskpart` | Advanced disk partitioning |
| `net use` | Map network drives |
| `net user` | Manage user accounts |
| `net localgroup` | Manage local groups |
| `gpupdate /force` | Force Group Policy refresh |
| `shutdown /r /t 0` | Restart immediately |
| `taskkill /PID [n]` | Kill a process |
| `robocopy` | Robust file copy with options |
| `xcopy` | Extended copy |
| `format` | Format a drive |
| `cipher` | Manage EFS encryption |
| `winver` | Show Windows version |

### Windows boot process
1. **UEFI/BIOS POST** — hardware check
2. **Boot manager** — `bootmgr` (MBR) or `bootmgfw.efi` (UEFI)
3. **Boot loader** — `winload.exe` or `winload.efi`
4. **Windows kernel loads** — `ntoskrnl.exe`
5. **Session Manager** — `smss.exe`
6. **WinLogon** — `winlogon.exe` shows login screen
7. **Explorer** — `explorer.exe` — desktop

**Boot issues:**
- **MBR/GPT corruption** → Boot into WinRE, run `bootrec /fixmbr`, `bootrec /fixboot`, `bootrec /rebuildbcd`
- **Missing or corrupt system files** → Run `sfc /scannow` or DISM

### Windows Recovery Environment (WinRE)
Access: Hold Shift while clicking Restart, or boot from Windows media.
Options: Startup Repair, System Restore, Command Prompt, Reset this PC, System Image Recovery.

## 1.2 Linux Basics

Linux is tested at a basic level on A+. Know the key commands and file structure.

### Essential Linux commands
| Command | Function |
|---|---|
| `ls` | List files |
| `ls -la` | List with hidden files + permissions |
| `cd` | Change directory |
| `pwd` | Print working directory |
| `mkdir` | Make directory |
| `rm` | Remove file |
| `rm -rf` | Remove directory recursively (be careful!) |
| `cp` | Copy |
| `mv` | Move/rename |
| `cat` | Display file content |
| `grep` | Search text patterns |
| `chmod` | Change file permissions |
| `chown` | Change file owner |
| `sudo` | Run as superuser |
| `apt` / `yum` | Package managers (Debian/Red Hat) |
| `ps aux` | List running processes |
| `kill` / `killall` | Terminate processes |
| `top` / `htop` | Process monitor |
| `ifconfig` / `ip a` | Show network interfaces |
| `ping` | Test connectivity |
| `ssh` | Secure remote shell |
| `scp` | Secure copy over SSH |
| `df -h` | Disk space usage |
| `du -sh` | Directory size |

### Linux file system hierarchy
| Path | Contains |
|---|---|
| `/` | Root of filesystem |
| `/home` | User home directories |
| `/etc` | Configuration files |
| `/var` | Variable data (logs, mail, databases) |
| `/tmp` | Temporary files |
| `/usr` | User programs and utilities |
| `/bin` | Essential binaries |
| `/sbin` | System binaries (root) |
| `/dev` | Device files |
| `/proc` | Virtual filesystem for process info |

### Linux file permissions
Format: `rwxrwxrwx` = owner/group/others. `r`=read(4), `w`=write(2), `x`=execute(1).
Example: `chmod 755 file` = owner rwx (7), group r-x (5), others r-x (5).
`chmod +x file` = add execute permission.
`chown user:group file` = change owner and group.

## 1.3 macOS Basics

| macOS concept | Windows equivalent |
|---|---|
| Finder | File Explorer |
| Terminal | Command Prompt / PowerShell |
| Activity Monitor | Task Manager |
| System Preferences/Settings | Control Panel / Settings |
| Disk Utility | Disk Management |
| AirDrop | No direct equivalent |
| FileVault | BitLocker |
| Gatekeeper | SmartScreen |
| Homebrew | Package manager (like apt/yum) |

**macOS file system:** APFS (Apple File System) — default since 2017. HFS+ = older format.

**macOS key commands:**
- `Command+Space` — Spotlight search
- `Command+Q` — Quit application
- Terminal commands = same as Linux (macOS is Unix-based)

### Domain 1 Mini Quiz (10 questions)

**Q1.** Which Windows edition is required to join an Active Directory domain?
- A. Home  B. Professional  C. Starter  D. Core

**Q2.** A USB drive needs to hold files larger than 4GB and work with both Windows and macOS. Which file system?
- A. NTFS  B. FAT32  C. exFAT  D. APFS

**Q3.** A technician runs `sfc /scannow` on a Windows PC. What does this command do?
- A. Scans for malware  B. Repairs corrupted Windows system files  C. Checks disk for bad sectors  D. Updates drivers

**Q4.** Which Windows tool shows all running processes and their CPU/memory usage?
- A. Event Viewer  B. Device Manager  C. Task Manager  D. Resource Monitor (also valid but Task Manager is primary answer)

**Q5.** On Linux, which command displays the current directory path?
- A. `ls`  B. `dir`  C. `pwd`  D. `cd ~`

**Q6.** A Windows 11 computer fails to install. The technician checks and finds the CPU doesn't support TPM 2.0. What does this mean?
- A. The CPU is incompatible with any Windows version  B. The hardware doesn't meet Windows 11 minimum requirements  C. The RAM needs upgrading  D. The GPU needs to be replaced

**Q7.** What does `ipconfig /flushdns` do on Windows?
- A. Renews the IP address  B. Clears the DNS resolver cache  C. Resets the firewall  D. Releases the DHCP lease

**Q8.** On Linux, which command changes file permissions to allow the owner to read, write, and execute, while group and others can only read?
- A. `chmod 644`  B. `chmod 777`  C. `chmod 744`  D. `chmod 755`

**Q9.** Which Windows recovery option should a technician use to repair the boot sector of a Windows system that fails to start?
- A. `sfc /scannow` from Windows  B. `bootrec /fixmbr` from WinRE command prompt  C. Reinstall Windows  D. Run CHKDSK from Windows

**Q10.** What is the Windows equivalent of the Linux `ls` command?
- A. `list`  B. `show`  C. `dir`  D. `display`

### Domain 1 Answers
**Q1->B.** Windows Pro (and Enterprise/Education) supports Active Directory domain join. Home does not.
**Q2->C.** exFAT = no 4GB file size limit + cross-platform (Windows/macOS/Linux). FAT32 has 4GB limit.
**Q3->B.** `sfc /scannow` = System File Checker = scans and repairs corrupted Windows system files.
**Q4->C.** Task Manager = primary tool for processes, performance, startup. Resource Monitor has more detail.
**Q5->C.** `pwd` = Print Working Directory on Linux/macOS.
**Q6->B.** Windows 11 requires TPM 2.0, Secure Boot, 64-bit CPU — hardware requirements not met.
**Q7->B.** `ipconfig /flushdns` = clears cached DNS entries. Useful when DNS records have changed.
**Q8->C.** `chmod 744` = owner rwx (7), group r-- (4), others r-- (4).
**Q9->B.** `bootrec /fixmbr` from WinRE command prompt repairs the master boot record.
**Q10->C.** `dir` = Windows CMD equivalent of Linux `ls` (list directory contents).

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 2 — Domain 2: Security (25%)

## 2.1 Endpoint Security

### Malware types (A+ level)
- **Virus** — attaches to files, spreads with user action.
- **Worm** — self-replicates over network without user action.
- **Trojan** — disguised as legitimate software.
- **Ransomware** — encrypts files, demands payment.
- **Spyware** — monitors activity, keylogging.
- **Rootkit** — hides in OS kernel, very hard to detect.
- **Adware** — unwanted advertising, often with spyware.
- **Cryptominer** — uses CPU/GPU for cryptocurrency mining without consent.

### Malware removal process
1. **Identify and research** — what malware is it? Identify symptoms.
2. **Quarantine** — isolate infected system from network (prevent spread).
3. **Disable System Restore** — prevents malware from hiding in restore points.
4. **Remediate** — run anti-malware scan (ideally boot from external media or safe mode).
5. **Schedule scan** — run scan in Safe Mode (malware can't hide).
6. **Verify** — confirm infection is gone.
7. **Re-enable System Restore** and create new restore point.
8. **Educate user** — how did this happen? Prevent recurrence.

> **Common Trap:** Run malware scan in Safe Mode — many malware types can't load in Safe Mode, making them easier to detect and remove.

### Windows Defender and built-in security
- **Windows Defender Antivirus** — built-in AV in Windows 10/11. Real-time protection.
- **Windows Defender Firewall** — software firewall controlling network access.
- **Windows Defender SmartScreen** — blocks malicious downloads and websites.
- **Windows Security Center** — unified security dashboard.

## 2.2 System Hardening

### User account security
- **Principle of least privilege** — users only get the access they need.
- **Admin accounts** — should NOT be used for daily work. Create standard user for daily tasks.
- **Guest account** — disable by default.
- **Password policy** — minimum length 12+, complexity, history, lockout policy.
- **Account lockout** — lock account after N failed login attempts.
- **UAC (User Account Control)** — prompts for admin credentials when changes are made. Keep enabled.

### Authentication
- **MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication)** — password + authenticator app, hardware token, or biometric.
- **Biometrics** — fingerprint (Windows Hello), face recognition.
- **Smart card** — physical card with certificate. Common in government/corporate.
- **Software tokens** — TOTP apps (Google Authenticator, Microsoft Authenticator).
- **Hardware tokens** — physical devices (FIDO2 keys like YubiKey).

### Data protection

**BitLocker** — full disk encryption built into Windows Pro/Enterprise. Uses TPM chip to store keys. Requires recovery key if TPM is removed.

**EFS (Encrypting File System)** — file/folder level encryption in NTFS. Tied to user account.

**TPM (Trusted Platform Module)** — hardware chip on motherboard that stores encryption keys, certificates, passwords securely. Required for Windows 11 and BitLocker.

**Secure Boot** — UEFI feature that ensures only trusted (signed) bootloaders and OS kernels load. Prevents rootkits and bootkits.

### Software security
- **Patch management** — keep OS and apps updated. Enable automatic updates.
- **Remove unwanted software** — uninstall unused applications.
- **Disable unused features/services** — reduce attack surface.
- **Browser security** — keep updated, use HTTPS, enable pop-up blocking, review extensions.
- **DNS filtering** — use secure DNS (1.1.1.1, 8.8.8.8) or DNS-based content filtering.

### Physical security
- **Cable locks** — lock laptops to desks (Kensington lock).
- **Privacy screen** — prevents shoulder surfing.
- **Screen lock** — auto-lock screen after inactivity (Win+L manually).
- **BIOS/UEFI password** — prevents boot or settings changes without password.
- **Device encryption** — BitLocker, FileVault on Mac, dm-crypt on Linux.

### Wireless security
- **WPA3** — current best standard. SAE handshake.
- **WPA2** — still widely deployed. Use AES, not TKIP.
- **WEP** — completely broken. Never use.
- **Hide SSID** — minimal security benefit. Sophisticated attackers find hidden networks.
- **MAC filtering** — MAC addresses can be spoofed. Weak security.
- **Disable WPS** — WPS PIN is brute-forceable in under an hour.
- **Change default credentials** — never leave router with default admin password.

## 2.3 Windows Firewall and Network Security

**Windows Defender Firewall:**
- Controls inbound and outbound traffic by app, port, and protocol.
- Three profiles: Domain (corporate network), Private (home), Public (coffee shop).
- Public profile blocks most inbound connections by default.
- Can create custom rules via `wf.msc`.

**Software firewall vs hardware firewall:**
- Software: runs on the host, protects that host only.
- Hardware: dedicated appliance protecting the entire network.

## 2.4 Domain 2 Mini Quiz (8 questions)

**Q1.** A user's PC is running slowly and displaying many popup ads. Which type of malware is most likely present?
- A. Ransomware  B. Rootkit  C. Adware/Spyware  D. Worm

**Q2.** When removing malware from a Windows computer, why should the technician run the anti-malware scan in Safe Mode?
- A. Safe Mode has better anti-malware tools  B. Many malware programs cannot load in Safe Mode, making them easier to detect and remove  C. Safe Mode runs faster  D. Malware hides in restore points

**Q3.** Which Windows feature encrypts the entire hard drive and requires a TPM chip?
- A. EFS  B. Windows Defender  C. BitLocker  D. Secure Boot

**Q4.** Which wireless security setting should ALWAYS be disabled because its PIN can be brute-forced in under an hour?
- A. WPA2  B. WPS (Wi-Fi Protected Setup)  C. MAC filtering  D. SSID broadcast

**Q5.** A user receives a call from someone claiming to be IT support, asking for their Windows password to "fix an issue." What is the BEST response?
- A. Provide the password since IT needs it  B. Hang up and report to the real IT department  C. Give a temporary password  D. Provide read-only access

**Q6.** Which Windows feature prevents system changes without prompting for elevated credentials?
- A. Windows Defender  B. BitLocker  C. UAC (User Account Control)  D. Secure Boot

**Q7.** A company wants employees to use a second verification method in addition to passwords for VPN access. What should they implement?
- A. Longer password requirements  B. MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication)  C. Full disk encryption  D. VPN-only accounts

**Q8.** On which Windows editions is BitLocker available? (Choose TWO)
- A. Home  B. Professional  C. Enterprise  D. Starter  E. Starter N

### Domain 2 Answers
**Q1->C.** Popups + slow = adware/spyware. Ransomware encrypts files. Rootkit hides itself. Worm spreads via network.
**Q2->B.** Malware can't load in Safe Mode = easier detection and removal by AV tools.
**Q3->C.** BitLocker = full disk encryption, requires TPM. EFS = file/folder level.
**Q4->B.** WPS = disable always. 8-digit PIN is split in half = only ~11,000 combinations needed.
**Q5->B.** Hang up, report to real IT. IT never needs your password. Classic social engineering/pretexting.
**Q6->C.** UAC = prompts for admin credentials or approval before allowing system changes.
**Q7->B.** MFA = password + second factor (authenticator app, token, biometric).
**Q8->B and C.** BitLocker available on Pro and Enterprise (and Education). NOT available on Home.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 2 — Domain 3: Software Troubleshooting (22%)

## 3.1 Windows OS Troubleshooting

### Common Windows problems

| Symptom | Likely cause | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| PC won't start, black screen | Boot sector corruption, bad driver, missing OS files | WinRE, bootrec, sfc |
| BSOD (Blue Screen) | Driver conflict, failing RAM, overheating, corrupt OS | Check Event Viewer, update/rollback drivers, memtest, sfc |
| Slow performance | Malware, too many startup programs, low RAM, fragmented HDD, full disk | Task Manager, disable startups, add RAM, cleanup |
| Application crashes | Corrupt install, missing dependencies, compatibility | Reinstall app, compatibility mode, update |
| Application won't install | Insufficient permissions, compatibility, .NET missing | Run as admin, install prerequisites |
| No audio | Muted, wrong output device, driver issue | Check volume mixer, Device Manager, reinstall driver |
| Printer not found | Driver missing, offline, wrong port | Reinstall driver, check Services (Print Spooler) |
| Windows Update fails | Corrupt update files, insufficient disk space | Run Windows Update Troubleshooter, free disk space |
| Profile corruption | Power loss during logon, hardware issue | Create new profile, copy data over |

### Windows troubleshooting tools

**Event Viewer** — look in Windows Logs > Application and System for errors/warnings around the time of the problem.

**Reliability Monitor** — shows stability history timeline. Control Panel > Security and Maintenance > Reliability History.

**Resource Monitor** — detailed CPU, memory, disk, network usage per process.

**System Information (msinfo32)** — full hardware/software inventory.

**System Restore** — roll back system files and registry to a previous restore point without affecting personal files.

**Windows Memory Diagnostics** — schedule memory test on reboot. `mdsched.exe`.

**Safe Mode** — minimal drivers/startup. Boot from WinRE or hold Shift during restart.

### Startup troubleshooting
- **msconfig (System Configuration)** — manage startup items, services, boot options.
- **Task Manager > Startup** — enable/disable startup programs.
- **Clean boot** — disable all non-Microsoft services to isolate conflicts.
- **Last Known Good Configuration** — (legacy BIOS systems) boots with last settings that worked.

### Profile issues
- Profile corrupted: log in as admin, create new profile, copy user data from old profile folder (`C:\Users\OldProfile`).
- Temp profile: if Windows uses a temp profile (TEMP shown in Start menu), log out, delete temp profile files in registry, log back in.

## 3.2 Mobile Device Troubleshooting

### Common mobile issues

| Symptom | Likely cause | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| Battery drains quickly | Too many apps running, high brightness, poor signal | Check battery usage, close apps, lower brightness, airplane mode in poor areas |
| Overheating | Heavy load, blocked vents, bad case | Remove case, stop heavy apps, let it cool |
| Slow performance | Low storage, too many apps, old OS | Free storage, clear cache, update OS |
| No cellular signal | Wrong APN, SIM issue, carrier issue | Check APN settings, re-seat SIM, check with carrier |
| Wi-Fi won't connect | Wrong password, IP conflict, outdated DHCP | Forget network and reconnect, check router |
| App crashes | Outdated app, cache corruption, OS compatibility | Update app, clear cache, reinstall |
| Touchscreen unresponsive | Dirty/cracked screen, software crash | Clean screen, restart, screen replacement |
| No sound | Muted, volume limit, Bluetooth connected elsewhere | Check Do Not Disturb, volume, Bluetooth devices |

### Mobile OS reset options
- **Soft reset** — restart (hold power). Clears RAM, resolves minor software issues.
- **Hard reset / Factory reset** — wipes all user data, returns to factory state. Use as last resort.
- **Backup first** — always backup before factory reset (iCloud, Google Backup).

## 3.3 Application and Browser Troubleshooting

### Application issues
- **Application fails to install** — check system requirements, run as administrator, check disk space.
- **Application compatibility** — right-click > Properties > Compatibility > Run as Windows 8/7 compatibility mode.
- **Missing DLL errors** — reinstall the application, install Visual C++ redistributables or .NET.
- **Application hangs** — use Task Manager to force-close (`End Task`).
- **Slow application** — check CPU/RAM in Task Manager, scan for malware, reinstall.

### Browser troubleshooting
- **Browser crashes** — update browser, disable extensions one-by-one to find culprit, clear cache.
- **Slow browser** — clear cache and cookies, disable extensions, check for malware.
- **Pop-ups despite blocker** — malware or rogue extension. Run malware scan, remove suspicious extensions.
- **Certificates invalid** — check system date/time (wrong date = all certs appear invalid), clear browser cache.
- **Homepage hijacked** — malware/unwanted extension changed settings. Run malware scan, reset browser settings.
- **Browser locked to specific proxy** — malware setting. Reset browser settings, check system proxy settings.

### Domain 3 Mini Quiz (6 questions)

**Q1.** A user's Windows PC is very slow after startup. Task Manager shows 15 programs starting with Windows. What should the technician do?
- A. Reinstall Windows  B. Upgrade RAM  C. Disable unnecessary startup programs in Task Manager > Startup  D. Run sfc /scannow

**Q2.** A user receives an error "DLL file is missing" when launching an application. What is the BEST first step?
- A. Reinstall Windows  B. Reinstall the application (often reinstalls the required DLL)  C. Download the DLL from a website  D. Restart Windows

**Q3.** After a Windows update, a user's audio device no longer works. What should the technician try first?
- A. Replace the audio hardware  B. Roll back the audio driver in Device Manager  C. Reinstall Windows  D. Run sfc /scannow

**Q4.** A user's browser homepage keeps changing back to a suspicious site even after resetting it. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. ISP redirecting traffic  B. Browser cache issue  C. Malware or browser hijacker  D. DNS server issue

**Q5.** A mobile user says their phone battery drains in 2 hours. The phone is 1 year old. What should the technician check FIRST?
- A. Replace the battery immediately  B. Check battery usage in Settings to identify apps consuming excessive power  C. Factory reset the phone  D. Update the OS

**Q6.** Which tool in Windows shows a timeline of system stability with details about crashes and application failures?
- A. Task Manager  B. Event Viewer  C. Reliability Monitor  D. Performance Monitor

### Domain 3 Answers
**Q1->C.** Too many startup programs = slow boot. Disable unneeded ones in Task Manager > Startup.
**Q2->B.** Reinstall the application — the installer will reinstall required DLLs/dependencies. Never download DLLs from random websites (malware risk).
**Q3->B.** Audio stopped after update = driver incompatibility. Roll back driver in Device Manager first.
**Q4->C.** Homepage resets itself = browser hijacker/malware. Run full malware scan, remove extensions.
**Q5->B.** Check battery usage first to identify cause before replacing. A single rogue app can drain battery.
**Q6->C.** Reliability Monitor = stability timeline. Event Viewer has more detail on specific errors.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# Core 2 — Domain 4: Operational Procedures (22%)

## 4.1 Documentation and Change Management

### Documentation types
- **Network diagrams** — logical and physical layout of network infrastructure.
- **Asset inventory** — list of all hardware/software assets with model, serial number, location, owner.
- **Knowledge base (KB)** — articles documenting solutions to common issues.
- **SOP (Standard Operating Procedure)** — step-by-step procedures for common tasks.
- **Tickets** — incident/request tracking (help desk system: ServiceNow, Jira Service Management, Freshdesk).
- **Change log** — record of all system changes made.

### Change management process
1. **Request** — someone submits a change request.
2. **Review** — change advisory board (CAB) or stakeholders review for impact.
3. **Approval** — change is approved (or denied/deferred).
4. **Test** — test in non-production environment.
5. **Implement** — make the change, follow rollback plan if needed.
6. **Document** — record what was changed, when, by whom, outcome.
7. **Review** — post-implementation review.

> **Key principle:** Never make unauthorized changes. All changes must go through the change management process.

## 4.2 Safety and Environmental Procedures

### Electrical safety
- **ESD (Electrostatic Discharge)** — static electricity can damage components. Use:
  - Anti-static wrist strap (ground yourself to the chassis)
  - Anti-static mat
  - Anti-static bags (for transporting components)
  - Don't work on carpet without ESD protection
- **Power off before working** — always disconnect power before opening a PC case.
- **High-voltage caution** — PSU and CRT monitors hold dangerous voltage even when unplugged. Do not open.
- **Fire safety** — know location of fire extinguisher types. For electrical fires: Class C (CO2 or dry powder). **Never use water on electrical fires.**

### Environmental considerations
- **Operating temperature** — PCs typically 10-35°C (50-95°F). Keep server rooms cooled.
- **Humidity** — too dry = ESD risk, too humid = condensation damage.
- **Battery disposal** — laptops, phones use lithium-ion batteries. Do NOT throw in regular trash. Recycle through e-waste programs.
- **Equipment disposal (e-waste)** — computers, monitors, toner cartridges contain hazardous materials (lead, mercury). Must be properly recycled.
- **MSDS/SDS (Material Safety Data Sheet)** — safety information for chemicals (cleaning solutions, toner). Know where to find it.
- **Toner disposal** — toner is a health hazard if inhaled. Use approved disposal method. Don't vacuum toner spills with a regular vacuum (fire risk).

## 4.3 Scripting Basics

A+ 220-1202 includes basic scripting awareness (not deep coding). Know what each scripting type is used for.

### Scripting types
- **Batch / .bat files** — Windows CMD scripting. Simple automation.
- **PowerShell (.ps1)** — Windows scripting, very powerful. Object-oriented. Manages Active Directory, registry, files, services remotely.
- **Bash scripts (.sh)** — Linux/macOS shell scripting. Automation, system tasks.
- **Python (.py)** — cross-platform. Used for automation, web scraping, data processing, security tools.
- **VBScript (.vbs)** — legacy Windows scripting. Being replaced by PowerShell.
- **JavaScript (.js)** — web browser scripting. Also server-side (Node.js).

### Common use cases for scripting
- Automated backups
- User account creation in bulk
- Pushing software updates
- Log parsing and analysis
- System health checks
- Scheduled cleanup tasks

> **Exam Tip:** PowerShell is the Windows admin's primary scripting tool. Python is cross-platform. Bash is Linux.

## 4.4 Remote Access Tools

| Tool | Use |
|---|---|
| RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) | Windows-native remote GUI. Port 3389. Requires Pro or higher to host. |
| VNC | Cross-platform remote desktop. Less secure by default. |
| SSH | Secure command-line remote access. Port 22. Linux/Mac/network devices. |
| TeamViewer / AnyDesk | Third-party remote support tools. Cross-platform. |
| VPN | Secure tunnel to network. Required for accessing internal resources remotely. |
| Remote Assistance | Windows built-in for helpdesk (user must invite). |

## 4.5 Domain 4 Mini Quiz (6 questions)

**Q1.** A technician is replacing a RAM stick in a desktop PC. They notice they're wearing rubber-soled shoes and standing on carpet. What hazard is present?
- A. High-voltage risk  B. ESD (electrostatic discharge) risk — should use anti-static wrist strap  C. Fire risk  D. Radiation risk

**Q2.** An organization wants to track all changes made to IT systems. What process should be formalized?
- A. Incident management  B. Change management  C. Asset management  D. Configuration management

**Q3.** An old laptop battery needs disposal. Where should it go?
- A. Regular recycling bin  B. General trash  C. E-waste recycling program  D. Drain and bury

**Q4.** A technician spills toner while replacing a laser printer cartridge. What should they do?
- A. Vacuum it up with a standard vacuum  B. Leave it to settle then wipe up  C. Use a toner-specific vacuum or damp cloth — standard vacuums can cause fire hazard  D. Use compressed air to blow it away

**Q5.** A company wants to automate monthly cleanup of temp files across 500 Windows servers. Which tool is MOST appropriate?
- A. Batch file (.bat)  B. PowerShell script (.ps1)  C. Python script  D. VBScript

**Q6.** A remote technician needs GUI access to a Windows 10 Pro workstation. Which built-in tool enables this?
- A. SSH  B. Telnet  C. RDP (Remote Desktop) via mstsc.exe  D. VNC

### Domain 4 Answers
**Q1->B.** Carpet + rubber soles = ESD risk. Anti-static wrist strap grounded to chassis prevents static damage.
**Q2->B.** Change management = formal process for tracking all IT system changes.
**Q3->C.** Li-ion batteries = hazardous waste. E-waste recycling programs for proper disposal.
**Q4->C.** Standard vacuums can ignite toner (fine powder + heat). Use toner vacuum or damp cloth.
**Q5->B.** PowerShell = best for Windows server automation at scale (remote execution, object manipulation).
**Q6->C.** RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) = built-in Windows GUI remote access on port 3389. Requires Pro+.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# A+ Comparison Tables and Cheatsheets

## Core 1: Key Ports and Protocols

| Protocol | Port | Use |
|---|---|---|
| FTP | 20 (data) / 21 (control) | File transfer (unencrypted) |
| SSH | 22 | Secure remote shell / file transfer |
| Telnet | 23 | Remote shell (unencrypted — don't use) |
| SMTP | 25 | Send email |
| DNS | 53 | Domain name resolution |
| DHCP | 67/68 | Automatic IP assignment |
| HTTP | 80 | Web (unencrypted) |
| HTTPS | 443 | Web (TLS encrypted) |
| POP3 | 110 | Receive email (downloads, deletes from server) |
| IMAP | 143 | Receive email (syncs, keeps on server) |
| SMB | 445 | Windows file sharing |
| RDP | 3389 | Windows Remote Desktop |
| SNMP | 161/162 | Network device monitoring |
| LDAP | 389 | Directory services |
| LDAPS | 636 | LDAP over TLS |

## Core 1: Wireless Standards

| Standard | Band | Max speed | Range | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 802.11b | 2.4 GHz | 11 Mbps | ~35m indoor | Legacy |
| 802.11g | 2.4 GHz | 54 Mbps | ~38m indoor | Legacy |
| 802.11n (Wi-Fi 4) | 2.4 / 5 GHz | 600 Mbps | ~70m | MIMO |
| 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) | 5 GHz | 3.5 Gbps | ~35m | MU-MIMO, wider channels |
| 802.11ax (Wi-Fi 6/6E) | 2.4 / 5 / 6 GHz | 9.6 Gbps | ~35m | OFDMA, better in dense environments |

## Core 1: IPv4 Subnetting Quick Reference

| CIDR | Subnet mask | Hosts |
|---|---|---|
| /24 | 255.255.255.0 | 254 |
| /25 | 255.255.255.128 | 126 |
| /26 | 255.255.255.192 | 62 |
| /27 | 255.255.255.224 | 30 |
| /28 | 255.255.255.240 | 14 |
| /30 | 255.255.255.252 | 2 |

**Private address ranges:**
- 10.0.0.0/8 (Class A private)
- 172.16.0.0–172.31.255.255 (Class B private)
- 192.168.0.0/16 (Class C private)
- 169.254.x.x = APIPA (no DHCP server found)
- 127.0.0.1 = loopback (localhost)

## Core 1: Cable Types Summary

| Cable | Max speed | Max distance | Connector |
|---|---|---|---|
| Cat 5e | 1 Gbps | 100m | RJ-45 |
| Cat 6 | 1 Gbps (100m) / 10 Gbps (55m) | 100m | RJ-45 |
| Cat 6a | 10 Gbps | 100m | RJ-45 |
| Fiber OM1 (MMF) | 1 Gbps | 275m | LC, SC, ST |
| Fiber OM3 (MMF) | 10 Gbps | 300m | LC, SC |
| Fiber OS2 (SMF) | 100 Gbps | 10km+ | LC, SC |

## Core 2: Windows Tools Quick Reference

| Tool | Command | Use |
|---|---|---|
| Task Manager | Ctrl+Shift+Esc | Processes, performance, startup |
| Device Manager | devmgmt.msc | Hardware, drivers |
| Disk Management | diskmgmt.msc | Partitions, format, letters |
| Registry Editor | regedit | Edit registry |
| Group Policy | gpedit.msc | Policy settings (Pro+) |
| Event Viewer | eventvwr.msc | System/app logs |
| Services | services.msc | Start/stop services |
| System Info | msinfo32 | Hardware/software info |
| Remote Desktop | mstsc.exe | Remote GUI access |
| Performance Monitor | perfmon.msc | Detailed performance |
| Reliability Monitor | via Control Panel | Stability timeline |
| System Config | msconfig | Startup, services, boot |
| Resource Monitor | resmon.exe | Per-process resource detail |
| Windows Memory Diag | mdsched.exe | RAM test |

## A+ Keyword Decoder

| Keyword in question | Think of |
|---|---|
| "169.254.x.x address" | APIPA — DHCP server unreachable |
| "Cannot browse by name, can ping by IP" | DNS failure |
| "No internet, local network OK" | Wrong default gateway |
| "PC clicks or grinding sound" | Failing HDD — backup immediately |
| "Toner smears when touched" | Fuser assembly failure |
| "Continuous beeping on POST" | RAM not seated |
| "Blue USB port" | USB 3.0 (5 Gbps) |
| "Laptop RAM form factor" | SO-DIMM |
| "Full drive encryption + TPM" | BitLocker |
| "File/folder encryption (NTFS)" | EFS |
| "UEFI prevents unsigned bootloaders" | Secure Boot |
| "Hardware security chip" | TPM |
| "Battery backup, safe shutdown" | UPS |
| "Yellow fiber optic cable" | Single-mode fiber (long distance) |
| "Run elevated, admin prompt" | UAC (User Account Control) |
| "Malware scan won't run in Windows" | Boot into Safe Mode |
| "Windows Pro vs Home: domain join" | Pro supports domain join, Home does not |
| "FAT32 max file size" | 4 GB |
| "Cross-platform flash storage, no 4GB limit" | exFAT |
| "Windows file permissions, encrypted, large files" | NTFS |
| "SMB Windows file sharing port" | 445 |
| "Secure remote CLI" | SSH port 22 |
| "Remote GUI Windows native" | RDP port 3389 |
| "Auto-assign IP when DHCP unavailable" | APIPA 169.254.x.x |
| "Discover → Offer → Request → Acknowledge" | DHCP DORA process |
| "Non-overlapping 2.4GHz channels" | 1, 6, 11 |
| "2.4GHz interference fix" | Move to 5 GHz |
| "PC boot sector won't load" | bootrec /fixmbr or /rebuildbcd |
| "Repair corrupt system files in Windows" | sfc /scannow |
| "ESD risk mitigation" | Anti-static wrist strap |
| "Can't use water on this fire" | Class C electrical fire |
| "Dispose of battery/electronics" | E-waste recycling |
| "Toner spill — don't use this" | Regular vacuum (fire hazard) |
| "Windows scripting for mass automation" | PowerShell |
| "View startup stability history timeline" | Reliability Monitor |
| "Verify full system after repair" | Last step of troubleshooting methodology |

# A+ Mock Exams

## Core 1 Mock Exam — 220-1201 (50 questions, 60 minutes)

> Core 1 full exam is 90 questions. This condensed version covers all 5 domains. Study with this, then attempt a full 90-question exam via CompTIA practice tests.

**Q1.** A laptop's battery indicator shows 98% but the laptop powers off when unplugged. What should be replaced?
- A. The power adapter  B. The laptop battery  C. The CMOS battery  D. The DC jack

**Q2.** Which cellular technology is associated with 5G networks?
- A. CDMA  B. GSM  C. LTE  D. NR (New Radio)

**Q3.** An IP camera is connected to a switch but doesn't have a power adapter. It powers on via the network cable. What technology enables this?
- A. VLAN  B. PoE (Power over Ethernet)  C. NAS  D. QoS

**Q4.** A user's desktop cannot reach the internet. `ipconfig` shows IP: 192.168.1.100, Mask: 255.255.255.0, Gateway: (blank). What is the problem?
- A. DHCP failure  B. DNS failure  C. No default gateway configured  D. Wrong subnet mask

**Q5.** Which connector type is found on the end of a network (Ethernet) cable?
- A. RJ-11  B. RJ-45  C. BNC  D. LC

**Q6.** A user reports their laptop overheats and shuts down. The fan runs very loudly. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Failing HDD  B. RAM failure  C. Clogged/dusty heatsink and fan — poor airflow  D. Bad display cable

**Q7.** Which type of RAM is used in laptops?
- A. DIMM  B. ECC RDIMM  C. SO-DIMM  D. DDR4 UDIMM (desktop)

**Q8.** A printer prints blank pages. The toner cartridge is new. What should be checked?
- A. Fuser  B. Remove the toner cartridge protective tape/strip before installing  C. Drum  D. Paper tray

**Q9.** Which network address is the loopback (localhost) address?
- A. 192.168.0.1  B. 0.0.0.0  C. 127.0.0.1  D. 255.255.255.255

**Q10.** A VM needs to receive its own IP from the corporate DHCP server and be reachable from other machines on the network. What network mode should be configured?
- A. NAT  B. Host-only  C. Bridged  D. Internal

**Q11.** A technician is disposing of old laser toner cartridges. What is the correct procedure?
- A. Place in regular trash  B. Burn them  C. Return to manufacturer or approved recycling — toner is hazardous  D. Crush and bury

**Q12.** Which command displays the IP address, subnet mask, and default gateway in Windows?
- A. `netstat`  B. `tracert`  C. `ipconfig`  D. `ping`

**Q13.** A printer produces pages where text appears faded on one side. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Wrong paper size  B. Low toner (toner not distributed evenly)  C. Fuser failure  D. Drum failure

**Q14.** An organization wants to minimize the number of IP addresses wasted. Their network has 200 workstations. Which subnet gives the MOST efficient allocation?
- A. /16 (65,534 hosts — wasteful)  B. /24 (254 hosts — too small)  C. /23 (510 hosts — fits 200 with room)  D. /8 (16 million — extremely wasteful)

**Q15.** Which Wi-Fi band has shorter range but less interference and higher speeds?
- A. 2.4 GHz  B. 5 GHz  C. 900 MHz  D. 6 MHz

**Q16.** A PC powers on but no image appears on the monitor. The monitor works with another PC. What should the technician check first?
- A. Replace the CPU  B. Check the video cable connection and try reseating the GPU  C. Replace the motherboard  D. Run memtest86

**Q17.** Which cloud service model gives the customer responsibility for the operating system and applications?
- A. SaaS  B. PaaS  C. IaaS  D. CaaS

**Q18.** A user's phone screen cracked. Which component needs replacement?
- A. LCD only  B. Digitizer only  C. Digitizer + LCD assembly (on modern phones, these are fused)  D. Battery

**Q19.** Which wireless protocol uses SAE for key exchange, replacing PSK, and is resistant to offline dictionary attacks?
- A. WPA2-Personal  B. WPA  C. WPA3  D. WEP

**Q20.** A laser printer leaves vertical black lines on every page. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Low toner  B. Scratch or debris on the imaging drum  C. Fuser failure  D. Paper jam

**Q21.** A technician needs to connect two switches together in a network closet. What cable type should be used?
- A. Straight-through Cat 6  B. Crossover Cat 6 (or use an auto-MDI/MDI-X capable switch with straight-through)  C. Coaxial  D. Fiber only

**Q22.** Which DNS record type maps a hostname to an IPv4 address?
- A. AAAA  B. MX  C. A  D. CNAME

**Q23.** A printer connected via USB works but not via Wi-Fi. What should be checked?
- A. Replace the toner  B. Verify the printer is connected to the correct SSID and Wi-Fi password is correct  C. Reinstall Windows  D. Replace the printer

**Q24.** Which power connector does a CPU typically use?
- A. 24-pin  B. PCIe 8-pin  C. 4+4 or 8-pin EPS  D. Molex

**Q25.** A laptop does not charge when plugged in. The power adapter is confirmed working. What should the technician check?
- A. Replace the motherboard  B. Replace the battery and check the DC power jack for damage  C. Update BIOS  D. Replace the screen

**Q26.** Which command shows active network connections and which ports are listening on a Windows PC?
- A. `ipconfig /all`  B. `netstat -an`  C. `arp -a`  D. `tracert`

**Q27.** A SOHO router assigns IPs in the range 192.168.1.1–192.168.1.254. A new device receives 169.254.x.x. What does this mean?
- A. Device is connected via Wi-Fi  B. DHCP server is unreachable or ran out of addresses  C. Device has a static IP  D. DNS is misconfigured

**Q28.** Which storage form factor connects via PCIe and provides the fastest speeds on modern PCs?
- A. SATA SSD  B. M.2 NVMe SSD  C. HDD 7200 RPM  D. eSATA SSD

**Q29.** A user cannot send email but can receive it. Which protocol is likely having issues?
- A. IMAP (incoming)  B. POP3 (incoming)  C. SMTP (outgoing)  D. HTTPS

**Q30.** Which component converts AC power from the wall outlet to DC power for PC components?
- A. UPS  B. Surge protector  C. PSU (Power Supply Unit)  D. Motherboard

**Q31.** An A+ technician is asked about cloud characteristics. Which characteristic allows users to provision cloud resources without interacting with the provider's staff?
- A. Broad network access  B. On-demand self-service  C. Rapid elasticity  D. Measured service

**Q32.** Which type of cable should be used for a 10 Gbps connection spanning 100 meters?
- A. Cat 5e  B. Cat 6  C. Cat 6a  D. Cat 7 is preferred but Cat 6a is the correct standard answer for this scenario

**Q33.** A technician replaces a CPU. During POST, the system gives 3 short beeps. What does this typically indicate?
- A. CPU failure  B. No GPU installed  C. RAM error — check RAM seating  D. BIOS corruption

**Q34.** Which mobile device connector is universal (works both ways) and supports USB 3.2 and video output?
- A. Micro-USB  B. Lightning  C. USB-C  D. USB-A

**Q35.** A technician documents that the root cause of a printer issue was a jammed paper fragment. What phase of troubleshooting is documentation?
- A. Identify the problem  B. Test the theory  C. Verify and document — final step  D. Implement solution

**Q36.** A user wants to transfer a 6GB video file to a USB drive. The drive is FAT32 formatted. What will happen?
- A. Transfer succeeds normally  B. File is split automatically  C. Transfer fails because FAT32 max file size is 4GB  D. File is compressed automatically

**Q37.** Which RAID level provides the best performance for read operations but offers NO fault tolerance?
- A. RAID 1  B. RAID 5  C. RAID 0 (striping only)  D. RAID 10

**Q38.** A network printer is accessible from some computers but not others on the same subnet. What should the technician check?
- A. Firewall rules on the computers that can't access it  B. Replace the printer  C. Restart all computers  D. Check the DNS server

**Q39.** A mobile user reports that their phone shows "Emergency calls only" despite having a SIM inserted. What should be checked?
- A. Factory reset immediately  B. Check that the SIM is seated correctly and the carrier account is active  C. Update the OS  D. Replace the battery

**Q40.** Which display technology provides true blacks by turning off individual pixels?
- A. IPS LCD  B. TN LCD  C. OLED  D. VA LCD

**Q41.** (Choose TWO) Which two devices operate at Layer 2 (Data Link) of the OSI model?
- A. Router  B. Switch  C. Bridge  D. Hub (Layer 1)  E. Firewall (Layer 3+)

**Q42.** A user gets a new laptop with Windows 11. They notice there's no Start menu option to join a domain. What is the likely cause?
- A. Group Policy is preventing domain join  B. The laptop has Windows 11 Home, which doesn't support domain join  C. TPM is not enabled  D. Windows Update is needed

**Q43.** Which tool is used to remove dust from components in a PC without creating ESD risk?
- A. Damp cloth  B. Regular vacuum  C. Compressed air canister (canned air)  D. Dry towel

**Q44.** An inkjet printer produces correct text but colors are wrong (green shows as blue). What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Fuser issue  B. Wrong color profile / specific color ink cartridge empty or clogged  C. Driver issue  D. Paper type

**Q45.** A company needs to share files between 10 computers on a local network with centralized storage. What device should be added?
- A. Additional router  B. NAS (Network Attached Storage)  C. More switches  D. A second ISP connection

**Q46.** Which command tests connectivity to a specific IP address and shows round-trip time?
- A. `tracert`  B. `netstat`  C. `ping`  D. `nslookup`

**Q47.** A technician needs to verify that a specific port (e.g., 3389/RDP) is open on a remote Windows computer. Which tool can test this?
- A. `ping` (ICMP only)  B. `tracert`  C. `telnet [IP] [port]` or `Test-NetConnection` in PowerShell  D. `nslookup`

**Q48.** Which type of mobile connection provides the highest throughput for a smartphone in 2025?
- A. 3G  B. 4G LTE  C. 5G NR  D. Wi-Fi 4

**Q49.** A technician enables ESD precautions before working inside a PC. They connect the wrist strap to the PC chassis. The PC is plugged in but powered off. Why is the PC still plugged in?
- A. This is incorrect — PC should be unplugged  B. Plugged in provides the ground path for the wrist strap via the chassis  C. The PSU needs power to function as a ground  D. Unplugging causes static buildup

**Q50.** Which diagnostic tool runs before the OS loads and checks RAM for errors?
- A. Windows Memory Diagnostics (schedules test on reboot)  B. memtest86 (boots independently, runs before OS)  C. chkdsk  D. perfmon

### Core 1 Mock Answers

**Q1->B.** Battery shows charge but dies immediately = dead cells in battery. Replace battery.
**Q2->D.** 5G uses NR (New Radio). LTE = 4G.
**Q3->B.** PoE = Power over Ethernet — switch delivers power via Ethernet cable. No separate adapter needed.
**Q4->C.** No gateway = can reach local network but not internet.
**Q5->B.** RJ-45 = network cable connector. RJ-11 = phone. BNC = coax. LC = fiber.
**Q6->C.** Loud fan + overheating = dust blocking airflow to heatsink. Clean with compressed air.
**Q7->C.** SO-DIMM = laptop RAM form factor (smaller than desktop DIMM).
**Q8->B.** New toner printing blank = protective tape not removed. Always check this first.
**Q9->C.** 127.0.0.1 = loopback/localhost. 192.168.0.1 = common default gateway.
**Q10->C.** Bridged = VM gets own IP from corporate DHCP, visible to network.
**Q11->C.** Toner = hazardous material. Return to manufacturer or approved recycler.
**Q12->C.** `ipconfig` shows IP, mask, gateway. `/all` shows more detail.
**Q13->B.** Faded side = toner low or unevenly distributed. Shake cartridge, replace if still faded.
**Q14->C.** /23 = 510 usable hosts — fits 200 with growth room. /24 = only 254.
**Q15->B.** 5 GHz = shorter range, less interference, higher speeds than 2.4 GHz.
**Q16->B.** Check cable first (quick), then reseat GPU. Most no-display issues are connection problems.
**Q17->C.** IaaS = customer manages OS and apps. SaaS = vendor manages everything including app.
**Q18->C.** Modern phones fuse digitizer and LCD — replace as one assembly.
**Q19->C.** WPA3 = SAE, resistant to offline dictionary attacks.
**Q20->B.** Vertical black lines = scratch or debris on imaging drum leaving toner in that track.
**Q21->B.** Switch-to-switch traditionally needs crossover. Most modern switches auto-MDI/MDI-X so straight-through also works.
**Q22->C.** A record = hostname → IPv4. AAAA = IPv6. MX = mail. CNAME = alias.
**Q23->B.** Wi-Fi but not USB = wireless connectivity issue. Check SSID, password, DHCP.
**Q24->C.** CPU uses 4+4 or 8-pin EPS connector. 24-pin is for motherboard. PCIe 8-pin is for GPU.
**Q25->B.** Battery/DC jack are most common charging failure points after confirming adapter is good.
**Q26->B.** `netstat -an` = all connections and listening ports with addresses.
**Q27->B.** 169.254.x.x = APIPA = DHCP unreachable or pool exhausted.
**Q28->B.** M.2 NVMe SSD = PCIe, fastest storage (3,000–7,000 MB/s). SATA SSD = ~550 MB/s max.
**Q29->C.** Can receive (IMAP/POP3 working) but can't send = SMTP (port 25/587) issue.
**Q30->C.** PSU = AC to DC conversion for all PC components.
**Q31->B.** On-demand self-service = provision without talking to provider.
**Q32->C.** Cat 6a = 10 Gbps at 100m (full run). Cat 6 only does 10 Gbps up to 55m.
**Q33->C.** 3 short beeps on most BIOS = RAM error.
**Q34->C.** USB-C = reversible, supports USB 3.x, DisplayPort Alt Mode, USB Power Delivery.
**Q35->C.** Documentation = final step after verifying fix works.
**Q36->C.** FAT32 max single file size = 4GB. 6GB file fails. Use NTFS or exFAT.
**Q37->C.** RAID 0 = fastest reads (all disks in parallel), zero fault tolerance.
**Q38->A.** Some can reach printer, others can't = per-computer firewall blocking traffic.
**Q39->B.** "Emergency calls only" = SIM not recognized or account issue. Check SIM seating and carrier.
**Q40->C.** OLED = self-emitting pixels, true blacks by turning off pixels completely.
**Q41->B and C.** Switch and Bridge = Layer 2. Router = Layer 3. Hub = Layer 1.
**Q42->B.** Windows Home = no domain join. Windows Pro/Enterprise required.
**Q43->C.** Canned/compressed air = safe for dust removal. Regular vacuum creates static.
**Q44->B.** One color wrong = that specific ink empty or nozzle clogged. Run cleaning cycle or replace cartridge.
**Q45->B.** NAS = networked file storage shared by multiple users. Perfect for this scenario.
**Q46->C.** `ping` = connectivity test with round-trip time. `tracert` shows the path.
**Q47->C.** `telnet [IP] [port]` or PowerShell `Test-NetConnection -Port` tests specific port connectivity.
**Q48->C.** 5G NR = highest mobile bandwidth (1–10+ Gbps theoretical).
**Q49->B.** Plugged in (but off) = chassis connected to earth ground via PSU. Wrist strap → chassis → ground. Safe.
**Q50->B.** memtest86 = boots independently from USB, runs before OS loads — best RAM tester.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

## Core 2 Mock Exam — 220-1202 (50 questions, 60 minutes)

**Q1.** A Windows 10 Pro user receives a UAC prompt when trying to install software. What does this prompt indicate?
- A. The software is malware  B. The action requires administrator elevation  C. The drive is full  D. The license is invalid

**Q2.** A user's computer is infected with ransomware. Files are encrypted. What should the technician do FIRST?
- A. Pay the ransom  B. Isolate/disconnect the computer from the network immediately  C. Run antivirus  D. Contact the attacker

**Q3.** Which Windows command checks and repairs file system errors on a disk?
- A. `sfc /scannow`  B. `chkdsk /f`  C. `defrag`  D. `diskpart`

**Q4.** A technician needs to reset a Windows password for a user who is locked out. The technician has admin access. Which tool is used?
- A. `regedit`  B. `net user [username] [newpassword]`  C. `msconfig`  D. `gpedit.msc`

**Q5.** A Windows PC is sluggish. Task Manager shows a process named "cryptominer.exe" using 95% CPU. What should the technician do?
- A. End the process and reinstall the CPU  B. End the process, run a full malware scan, and investigate how it got there  C. Upgrade the CPU  D. Increase virtual memory

**Q6.** Which Linux command shows all running processes?
- A. `ls -la`  B. `top` or `ps aux`  C. `ifconfig`  D. `netstat`

**Q7.** A user reports that their browser keeps redirecting to unwanted websites. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. ISP throttling  B. Browser hijacker / malware  C. Wrong DNS server  D. Router configuration

**Q8.** Which Windows feature allows rolling back system files and registry settings to a previous state without losing personal files?
- A. Windows Reset  B. System Restore  C. Windows Backup  D. File History

**Q9.** An employee wants to connect to the company network from home using the company's internal file server. What should be implemented?
- A. Public Wi-Fi access  B. Port forwarding  C. VPN (Virtual Private Network)  D. Remote Desktop without VPN

**Q10.** Which security principle states that users should only be given the minimum permissions required to do their job?
- A. Separation of duties  B. Need to know  C. Least privilege  D. Zero trust

**Q11.** A technician is about to replace a CPU. What ESD precaution should be taken?
- A. Wear thick rubber gloves  B. Work faster to reduce exposure time  C. Use an anti-static wrist strap connected to the chassis  D. Keep the CPU in its anti-static bag until last moment (insufficient alone)

**Q12.** A user's macOS computer won't start up. It shows a flashing question mark folder. What does this mean?
- A. RAM failure  B. Display driver issue  C. macOS cannot find a bootable drive  D. Battery failure

**Q13.** Which type of Linux permissions allows the group to read and execute but NOT write to a file? (numeric)
- A. 7  B. 6  C. 5  D. 4

**Q14.** A company wants to prevent users from installing software on their Windows workstations. What Group Policy setting accomplishes this?
- A. Enable BitLocker  B. Configure Software Restriction Policies or AppLocker  C. Disable Windows Update  D. Enable audit logging

**Q15.** A user sees a popup stating their computer is infected with 47 viruses and to call a number for support. What is this?
- A. A legitimate Windows Security alert  B. Ransomware  C. Scareware / tech support scam  D. An antivirus notification

**Q16.** Which type of backup captures ALL data regardless of when it was last backed up?
- A. Incremental  B. Differential  C. Full  D. Synthetic

**Q17.** An employee's workstation is suspected of being compromised. The manager asks the technician NOT to touch the machine until IT security arrives. What principle does this follow?
- A. Chain of custody / evidence preservation  B. Change management  C. Documentation procedure  D. User privacy

**Q18.** A new laptop doesn't detect its Wi-Fi adapter. Device Manager shows a yellow exclamation mark next to the adapter. What should the technician do?
- A. Replace the laptop  B. Run Windows Update and/or reinstall the Wi-Fi driver  C. Use ethernet instead  D. Run sfc /scannow

**Q19.** Which Windows tool shows the full hardware configuration of a computer including BIOS version, RAM, and installed hardware?
- A. Device Manager  B. Task Manager  C. msinfo32 (System Information)  D. Control Panel

**Q20.** A user reports that after a Windows update, their second monitor is no longer detected. What is the MOST likely fix?
- A. Replace the GPU  B. Roll back or update the display driver  C. Replace the monitor cable  D. Run sfc /scannow

**Q21.** Which mobile feature allows a smartphone to share its cellular internet connection via Wi-Fi?
- A. AirDrop  B. Hotspot / Mobile Wi-Fi tethering  C. NFC  D. Bluetooth PAN

**Q22.** A Windows user cannot log in with their standard account because the profile is corrupted. They can log in as Administrator. What is the BEST fix?
- A. Reinstall Windows  B. Create a new user account, copy data from old profile in `C:\Users\`, delete the corrupt profile  C. Run chkdsk  D. Roll back Windows Update

**Q23.** Which macOS utility is equivalent to Windows' Disk Management?
- A. Activity Monitor  B. System Preferences  C. Disk Utility  D. Finder

**Q24.** A user complains that their phone randomly reboots several times a day. Battery health shows 40%. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. Malware  B. Too many apps installed  C. Failing battery causing voltage drops and random restarts  D. OS corruption

**Q25.** Which Windows command forces a Group Policy update immediately?
- A. `gpresult /r`  B. `gpupdate /force`  C. `secedit /configure`  D. `regedit`

**Q26.** A user's laptop screen is dim even at maximum brightness settings. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. GPU failure  B. Wrong resolution  C. Failing inverter (older CCFL screens) or failing backlight (LED)  D. Driver issue

**Q27.** An organization enforces that no sensitive data can be copied to USB drives. This is a function of:
- A. BitLocker  B. DLP (Data Loss Prevention) endpoint agent or Group Policy restriction  C. Antivirus  D. Windows Firewall

**Q28.** A technician discovers an unknown USB device plugged into a workstation. What should they do FIRST?
- A. Ignore it if the computer is running fine  B. Immediately unplug it and scan the system for malware, report to security team  C. Ask the user if it's theirs — if so, leave it  D. Format the USB

**Q29.** Which Windows tool is used to view and configure startup programs in Windows 10/11?
- A. msconfig > General tab  B. Task Manager > Startup tab  C. regedit HKCU\Run only  D. services.msc

**Q30.** A technician needs to migrate a user's data from an old PC to a new one. Which Windows built-in tool can assist?
- A. xcopy  B. Windows Easy Transfer (legacy) / manual file copy + Settings sync  C. defrag  D. chkdsk

**Q31.** A user's Windows 10 computer shows the error "NTLDR is missing" on startup. What is the correct interpretation?
- A. The hard drive is physically broken  B. This error is from a Windows XP-era boot failure — may indicate MBR corruption or wrong boot order  C. RAM failure  D. GPU failure

**Q32.** A mobile user cannot receive MMS messages. Their SMS works fine. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. SIM card issue  B. Incorrect APN (Access Point Name) settings  C. Wrong Wi-Fi password  D. Low storage

**Q33.** Which Linux command changes the owner of a file to a specific user?
- A. `chmod user:file`  B. `chown username:group filename`  C. `setowner`  D. `usermod file`

**Q34.** A workstation's antivirus software reports that it cannot update its definitions. What should be checked first?
- A. Reinstall antivirus  B. Verify the computer has internet access and the AV server is reachable  C. Reinstall Windows  D. Replace the hard drive

**Q35.** A Windows computer freezes randomly. Event Viewer shows critical errors for "Kernel-Power." What does this indicate?
- A. RAM failure  B. GPU failure  C. Unexpected shutdowns — often caused by overheating, PSU failure, or power issues  D. Software corruption

**Q36.** A user needs to copy a folder of 50,000 files from one server to another with verification. Which Windows command is BEST?
- A. `copy`  B. `xcopy`  C. `robocopy` (with logging and verification options)  D. `move`

**Q37.** A company wants to remotely manage mobile devices, enforce encryption, and wipe lost devices. What should be deployed?
- A. Antivirus for mobile  B. MDM (Mobile Device Management) solution  C. VPN for all mobile devices  D. MFA only

**Q38.** A user's Windows 10 computer is running very slowly. Opening Task Manager shows Disk at 100%. What is the MOST common cause?
- A. CPU overloading  B. Windows Update running in background, malware, or failing HDD  C. Too many monitors  D. RAM failure only

**Q39.** Which file system is required for NTFS features like permissions, encryption, and files larger than 4GB on Windows?
- A. FAT32  B. exFAT  C. NTFS  D. ReFS

**Q40.** A technician installs a new video driver and the screen goes black, unresponsive. What should they do?
- A. Reinstall Windows  B. Boot into Safe Mode, then roll back or uninstall the problematic driver  C. Replace the GPU  D. Wait 30 minutes for the driver to install

**Q41.** Which protocol does Windows use for domain authentication using tickets?
- A. NTLM  B. Kerberos  C. LDAP  D. RADIUS

**Q42.** A call center employee's headset audio quality is poor — muffled and distorted. What should be checked?
- A. Replace the motherboard audio chip  B. Check volume mixer levels, audio driver, and test the headset on another PC  C. Run sfc /scannow  D. Check hard drive health

**Q43.** A company policy requires that all terminated employees' accounts be disabled immediately. Which principle does this enforce?
- A. Separation of duties  B. Account management / least privilege (no longer needed = remove access)  C. Password complexity  D. MFA

**Q44.** A technician receives a computer with suspected malware. Before beginning cleanup, what should be done?
- A. Begin cleanup immediately to prevent spread  B. Document the symptoms and isolate the computer from the network  C. Reinstall Windows first  D. Run Windows Update

**Q45.** Which Windows command can be used to create a new local user account from the command line?
- A. `useradd`  B. `net user /add`  C. `adduser`  D. `newuser`

**Q46.** A user's Android phone shows "Storage full" after installing one app. Internal storage shows 90% full. What is the BEST immediate recommendation?
- A. Factory reset  B. Clear cache for apps (Settings > Apps > each app > Clear Cache) and delete unused files  C. Replace the phone  D. Add more RAM

**Q47.** Which statement about BitLocker is TRUE?
- A. BitLocker is available on Windows 10 Home  B. BitLocker encrypts individual files only  C. BitLocker encrypts the entire drive and uses TPM to protect the key  D. BitLocker requires a USB key to function

**Q48.** A user says they need to access a shared folder on the company server but are getting an "Access denied" error. The folder exists and other users can access it. What is the MOST likely cause?
- A. The server is down  B. The user's account doesn't have permissions to the shared folder  C. The network cable is bad  D. DNS failure

**Q49.** A laptop's battery health is 28%. The user reports frequent unexpected shutdowns. What is the BEST solution?
- A. Replace the charger  B. Increase power plan performance mode  C. Replace the laptop battery  D. Turn off background apps

**Q50.** A technician completes a repair and confirms it fixed the issue. What should they do before closing the ticket?
- A. Ask the user to pay  B. Verify with the user that the system works fully, document the solution, and close the ticket  C. Immediately move to the next ticket  D. Back up all user data

### Core 2 Mock Answers

**Q1->B.** UAC prompt = action requires admin elevation. Not a malware detection.
**Q2->B.** Ransomware: isolate FIRST to prevent spread to other network resources.
**Q3->B.** `chkdsk /f` = fixes file system errors. `sfc /scannow` = repairs system files.
**Q4->B.** `net user [username] [newpassword]` = changes password from admin CMD.
**Q5->B.** End process, full malware scan, investigate entry point.
**Q6->B.** `top` (real-time) or `ps aux` (snapshot) = show running processes on Linux.
**Q7->B.** Redirecting to unwanted sites = browser hijacker/malware.
**Q8->B.** System Restore = rolls back system files/registry without deleting personal files.
**Q9->C.** VPN = secure tunnel to access internal resources remotely.
**Q10->C.** Least privilege = minimum permissions for the job function.
**Q11->C.** Anti-static wrist strap to chassis = ESD protection for CPU replacement.
**Q12->C.** Flashing ? folder = macOS can't find a valid startup disk.
**Q13->C.** 5 = r-x = read (4) + execute (1) = 5. No write.
**Q14->B.** Software Restriction Policies / AppLocker = prevents unauthorized software installation via Group Policy.
**Q15->C.** "47 viruses, call this number" = scareware / tech support scam. Close the browser, don't call.
**Q16->C.** Full backup = captures all data regardless of last change date.
**Q17->A.** Don't touch the machine = evidence preservation / chain of custody for forensic investigation.
**Q18->B.** Yellow ! = driver issue. Update via Windows Update or reinstall manually.
**Q19->C.** `msinfo32` = System Information = comprehensive hardware/software/BIOS info.
**Q20->B.** Second monitor lost after update = driver regression. Roll back or update display driver.
**Q21->B.** Hotspot = smartphone shares cellular internet via Wi-Fi.
**Q22->B.** Create new profile, copy data, delete old corrupt profile.
**Q23->C.** Disk Utility = macOS disk management tool.
**Q24->C.** 40% battery health + random reboots = failing battery causing voltage drops → random shutdowns.
**Q25->B.** `gpupdate /force` = immediately applies Group Policy.
**Q26->C.** Dim at max brightness = failing backlight or inverter (on older CCFL screens).
**Q27->B.** Block USB data transfer = DLP endpoint policy or Group Policy.
**Q28->B.** Unknown USB = potential security threat. Unplug, scan system, report.
**Q29->B.** Task Manager > Startup = manage startup programs in Windows 10/11.
**Q30->B.** Manual file copy + Settings sync (cloud) is standard modern approach.
**Q31->B.** "NTLDR is missing" = old Windows XP/Vista boot error. MBR issue or wrong boot order.
**Q32->B.** MMS fails, SMS works = APN settings incorrect. MMS requires data path via APN.
**Q33->B.** `chown username:group filename` = changes file owner and group on Linux.
**Q34->B.** AV can't update definitions = check internet access and AV server reachability first.
**Q35->C.** Kernel-Power events = unexpected shutdowns = overheating, PSU issues, or power loss.
**Q36->C.** `robocopy` = robust copy with retry, logging, verification — best for large file migrations.
**Q37->B.** MDM = remotely manage, enforce policy, and wipe mobile devices.
**Q38->B.** Disk 100% = often Windows Update background activity, malware, or failing HDD.
**Q39->C.** NTFS required for permissions, EFS, and files >4GB on Windows.
**Q40->B.** Bad driver = black screen. Safe Mode loads minimal drivers = can uninstall/roll back.
**Q41->B.** Windows domain = Kerberos. NTLM is legacy and being replaced.
**Q42->B.** Audio quality issue: check software (mixer, driver) before hardware replacement.
**Q43->B.** Disable terminated accounts = access management = part of least privilege principle.
**Q44->B.** Document symptoms, isolate = before beginning any cleanup.
**Q45->B.** `net user [name] [password] /add` = create local Windows user from CMD.
**Q46->B.** Storage full = clear app cache + delete unused files as immediate action.
**Q47->C.** BitLocker = full drive encryption + TPM key storage. Available on Pro/Enterprise, not Home.
**Q48->B.** Other users can access = server is up, network is fine = user's specific permissions.
**Q49->C.** 28% health + shutdowns = battery needs replacement.
**Q50->B.** Verify with user + document + close = complete troubleshooting methodology.

<div style="page-break-after: always;"></div>

# A+ Final Readiness Cheatsheet

## Core 1 Last-Day Review (10 must-knows)
1. **169.254.x.x = APIPA** — DHCP unreachable. Check DHCP server and cable.
2. **SO-DIMM = laptop RAM. DIMM = desktop RAM.**
3. **Cat 6a = 10 Gbps at 100m** — not Cat 6 (only 55m at 10 Gbps).
4. **Blue USB port = 3.0 (5 Gbps). Black = 2.0 (480 Mbps).**
5. **Toner smears = fuser failure** — fuser bonds toner to paper with heat.
6. **Clicking HDD = backup immediately** — physical media failing.
7. **WPA3 = SAE** — modern wireless. Disable WPS (brute-forceable).
8. **Bridged VM = own IP on network. NAT = shares host IP.**
9. **Non-overlapping 2.4 GHz channels: 1, 6, 11.**
10. **DORA = DHCP process: Discover → Offer → Request → Acknowledge.**

## Core 2 Last-Day Review (10 must-knows)
1. **Containment before cleanup** — isolate infected machine from network first.
2. **Malware removal in Safe Mode** — malware can't hide in Safe Mode.
3. **BitLocker = Pro/Enterprise only** — requires TPM. Not available on Home.
4. **UAC keeps enabled** — prevents unauthorized system changes.
5. **`sfc /scannow`** — repairs Windows system files. `chkdsk /f` — fixes file system.
6. **Least privilege** — users get minimum permissions needed.
7. **Disable WPS** — Wi-Fi Protected Setup is brute-forceable.
8. **`gpupdate /force`** — immediately applies Group Policy.
9. **Flashing ? folder (Mac)** = can't find bootable drive.
10. **Disable accounts immediately** when employee is terminated.

## Readiness checklist
- [ ] I know all common ports (22, 23, 25, 53, 67/68, 80, 110, 143, 443, 445, 3389).
- [ ] I know USB 2.0/3.0/USB-C speeds and port colors.
- [ ] I know Cat 5e/6/6a speed and distance limits.
- [ ] I can diagnose 169.254.x.x (APIPA), wrong gateway, and DNS failure.
- [ ] I know RAID 0/1/5/6/10 — which tolerate disk failure, which are fastest.
- [ ] I know Windows editions (Home vs Pro) and their limitations.
- [ ] I know the malware removal steps in order.
- [ ] I know BitLocker = Pro+ with TPM. EFS = file level.
- [ ] I know the 7-step troubleshooting methodology and can apply it.
- [ ] I scored 75%+ on both Core 1 and Core 2 mock exams.
